City of Vernon
Code of Ordinances
Current through Ordinance 1702 adopted 2/14/17
PART II
CODE OF ORDINANCES
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL PROVISIONS
Sec. 1-1. How Code designated and cited.
The ordinances embraced in this and the following chapters and sections shall constitute and be designated the
“Code of Ordinances, City of Vernon, Texas,” and may be so cited. (1969 Code, sec. 1-1)
State Law reference- Authority to publish code, V.T.C.A., Government Code sec. 53.001.
Sec. 1-2. Catchlines of sections.
The catchlines of the several sections of this Code printed in boldface type are intended as mere catchwords to
indicate the contents of the section and shall not be deemed or taken to be titles of such sections, nor as any
part of the section, nor, unless expressly so provided, shall they be so deemed when any of such sections,
including the catchlines, are amended or reenacted. (1969 Code, sec. 1-2)
Sec. 1-3. Rules of construction and definitions.
In the construction of this Code, and of all ordinances and resolutions passed by the city commission, the
following rules shall be observed and the following definitions shall apply, unless such construction would be
inconsistent with the manifest intent of the city commission:
Generally. The provisions of this Code shall be liberally construed to effect the purposes expressed therein or
implied from the expression thereof. In case of doubt or ambiguity in the meaning of such provisions, the
general shall yield to the particular. Words shall be construed in their common and usual significance unless the
contrary is clearly indicated.
City. The term “the city” or “this city” means the City of Vernon, in the County of Wilbarger, and the State of
Texas.
City commission, commission, city council or council. The term “city commission,” “commission,” “city council”
or “council” means the City Commission of Vernon, Texas, constituting the governing body of the city.
City officers and departments. Whenever reference is made to an officer or a department, the same shall be
construed as if followed by the words “of the City of Vernon, Texas.”
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 2/283
Computation of time. In computing any period of time mentioned in the provisions of this Code, the day of the
act, event or default after which the designated period of time begins to run is not to be included, and the last
day of the period so computed is to be included, unless it is a Sunday or a legal holiday, in which event the
period runs until the end of the next day which is neither a Sunday nor a holiday.
County. The term “the county” or “this county” means the County of Wilbarger, Texas.
Gender. A term importing the masculine gender only shall extend to and be applied to females and to firms,
partnerships, associations and corporations, as well as to males.
Highway. The term “highway” includes any street, alley, highway, avenue or public place or square, bridge,
viaduct, tunnel, underpass, overpass and causeway in the city, dedicated or devoted to public use.
Month. The term “month” means a calendar month.
Number. Any term importing the singular number shall include the plural and any word importing the plural
number shall include the singular.
Oath. The term “oath” includes an affirmation in all cases in which, by law, an affirmation may be substituted for
an oath, and in such cases the terms “swear” and “sworn” shall be equivalent to the terms “affirm” and
“affirmed.”
Or, and. The term “or” may be read as “and,” and the term “and” may be read as “or,” if the sense requires it.
Owner. The term “owner,” applied to a building or land, includes any part owner, joint owner, tenant in common,
tenant in partnership, joint tenant, or tenant by the entirety of the whole or of a part of such building or land.
Person. The term “person” extends and may be applied to associations, corporations, firms, partnerships, and
bodies politic and corporate as well as to individuals. Where criminal prosecution may lie, the officers of any
corporation shall jointly and severally be subject to prosecution as being included within the term “person.”
Police chief or chief of police. The term “police chief” or “chief of police” refers to the marshal of the city.
Preceding, following. The terms “preceding” and “following” mean next before and next after, respectively.
Roadway. The term “roadway” means that portion of a street improved, designed or ordinarily used for
vehicular traffic.
Sidewalk. The term “sidewalk” means any portion of the street between the curb, or the lateral line of the
roadway and the adjacent property line, intended for the use of pedestrians.
Signature or subscription. The term “signature” or “subscription” includes a mark when a person cannot write.
Standard time. All hours of time mentioned in this Code refer to and shall be determined by Central Standard
Time, or Central Daylight Savings Time, as the case may be, except that, if at any future time any different
standard of time is established by the state for an area which includes this city, all such hours shall be
determined by such officially proclaimed standard, so long as the same remains in effect.
State. The term “the state” or “this state” shall be construed to mean the State of Texas.
Street. The term “street” includes any highway, alley, street, avenue, or public place or square, bridge, viaduct,
underpass, overpass, tunnel and causeway in the city, dedicated or devoted to public use.
Tense. Terms used in the past or present tense include the future as well as the past and present.
Written or in writing. The term “written” or “in writing” includes any representation of words, letters, or figures,
whether by printing or otherwise.
Year. The term “year” means a calendar year.
(1969 Code, sec. 1-3)
Sec. 1-4. Amendments to Code.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 3/283
(a) All ordinances passed subsequent to this Code which amend, repeal, or in any way affect this Code may
be numbered in accordance with the numbering system of this Code and printed for inclusion therein. When
subsequent ordinances repeal any chapter, section, or subsection or any portion thereof, such repealed
portions may be excluded from the Code by omission from reprinted pages. The subsequent ordinances as
numbered and printed, or omitted in the case of repeal, shall be prima facie evidence of such subsequent
ordinances until such time that this Code and subsequent ordinances numbered or omitted are readopted as a
new Code by the city commission.
(b) Amendments to any of the provisions of this Code shall be made by amending such provisions by specific
reference to the section number of this Code in the following language: “Section ____________ of the Code of
Ordinances, City of Vernon, Texas, is hereby amended to read as follows:....” The new provisions shall then be
set out in full as desired.
(c) In the event a new section not heretofore existing in the Code is to be added, the following language shall
be used: “That the Code of Ordinances, City of Vernon, Texas, is hereby amended by adding a section, to be
numbered ____________ , which said section reads as follows:....” The new section shall then be set out in full
as desired.
(1969 Code, sec. 1-4)
Sec. 1-5. Specific reference to ordinances in amending or repealing required.
No ordinance shall be amended or repealed by any general term or by implication, but the ordinance intending
to repeal or amend an ordinance shall set forth clearly the ordinance desired to be changed. (1969 Code, sec.
1-5)
Sec. 1-6. General penalty; continuing violations.
(a) Whenever in this Code or in any ordinance of the city an act is prohibited or is made or declared to be
unlawful or an offense or a misdemeanor, or wherever in such Code or ordinance the doing of any act is
required or the failure to do any act is declared to be unlawful, and no specific penalty is provided therefor; the
violation of any such provision of this Code or any such ordinance shall be punished by fines not to exceed a
penalty greater than is indicated for a like offense by the laws of the state, except that the commission may
provide a different penalty for the obstruction of its streets, alleys, avenues and highways from that provided by
the state law.
(b) Unless otherwise specifically stated within the provisions of this Code, any violation of this Code or of any
ordinance set forth herein that is punishable by a fine that does not exceed the amount authorized by section
12.23 of the Texas Penal Code (V.T.C.A., Penal Code sec. 12.23) does not require a culpable mental state, and
a culpable mental state is hereby not required to prove any such offense.
(c) Unless otherwise specifically stated within the provisions of this Code, any violation of this Code or of any
ordinance set forth herein that is punishable by a fine that exceeds the amount authorized by section 12.23 of
the Texas Penal Code (V.T.C.A., Penal Code sec. 12.23) shall require a culpable mental state of criminal
negligence.
(1969 Code, sec. 1-6; Ordinance 1542, sec. 1, adopted 9/28/10)
Sec. 1-7. Annexation procedures on petitions.
Upon the filing with the city secretary of a written petition signed by all of the owners of real property situated in
the territory sought to be annexed to the city, the city commission may, in regular or special called session,
without notice, pass an ordinance annexing such territory to the city. (1969 Code, sec. 1-8; Ordinance 724, sec.
1, adopted 11/12/65)
Sec. 1-8. Commission initiative.
In the event the city commission shall desire to annex to the city any territory adjacent to the city, the owners of
which have not filed a petition for annexation to the city, it may do so by ordinance describing such territory by
metes and bounds; provided the city shall provide an opportunity for all interested persons to be heard at a
public hearing to be held not more than 20 days nor less than ten days prior to the first reading of the ordinance
of annexation. Notice of such hearing shall be published in a newspaper having general circulation in the city
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 4/283
and in the territory proposed to be annexed. The notice shall be published at least once in such newspaper not
more than 20 days nor less than ten days prior to such hearing. The minimum number of public hearings
required under state law must be held. (1969 Code, sec. 1-9; Ordinance 724, sec. 2, adopted 11/12/65)
Sec. 1-9. Severability of parts of Code.
It is hereby declared to be the intention of the city commission that the sections, paragraphs, sentences,
clauses, and phrases of this Code are severable and, if any phrase, clause, sentence, paragraph, or section of
this Code, or of any secondary code adopted herein, shall be declared invalid or unconstitutional by the valid
judgment or decree of any court of competent jurisdiction, such invalidity or unconstitutionality shall not affect
any of the remaining phrases, clauses, sentences, paragraphs, and sections of this Code, or of such secondary
code, since the same would have been enacted by the commission without the incorporation in this Code of
any such invalid or unconstitutional phrase, clause, sentence, paragraph, or section. (1969 Code, sec. 1-10)
CHAPTER 2
ADMINISTRATION*
ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL
Sec. 2-1. City seal.
The seal of the city shall be in design the same as usual seals, with the words inscribed, “City of Vernon,
Texas,” in a circle. (1969 Code, sec. 2-1)
Sec. 2-2. Installation of officers.
All officers elected at an annual election shall be installed at the first regular meeting of the city commission
after said election; except in case some officer is absent he is to be installed at first meeting thereafter, provided
it be within 30 days of his election. All officers who are appointed shall be installed within 30 days after
appointment. (1969 Code, sec. 2-3)
Sec. 2-3. Turning over books, etc., on leaving office.
When the duties of any officer of this city shall cease from any cause, whatsoever, he shall turn over to his
successor in office, if he has a successor, and if not, then to the city secretary, all books, records, papers and
appurtenances of his office. (1969 Code, sec. 2-3)
Sec. 2-4. City attorney-Attending court.
It shall be the duty of the city attorney to attend all prosecutions before the corporation court, when notified of
the pendency of such prosecutions, and to prosecute when notified on behalf of the corporation, and he is
entitled to appear in every case where the defendant fails to plead or enters the plea of guilty, or where the
defendant enters the plea of not guilty. (1969 Code, sec. 2-4)
Sec. 2-5. Same-Summoning offenders and witnesses and filing complaints.
Whenever the city attorney hears of any violation of the law or ordinances of the city, or when he has reason to
believe that said laws or ordinances have been violated, he may cause any person whom he may believe to be
in possession or knowing the facts or having witnessed such violation of said laws or ordinances, to be
summoned before the recorder, instant, for the purpose of being interrogated, under oath, either by the recorder
or city attorney, in reference to any such offense which such person so summoned may know has been
committed within the corporate limits of the city against the laws or ordinances of the city. If he finds from said
examination that an offense has been committed within said corporate limits he may file complaint against the
offender. (1969 Code, sec. 2-5)
Sec. 2-6. Same-Attending commission meetings; furnishing advice.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 5/283
It shall also be the duty of the city attorney to attend all meetings of the city commission and give the members
thereof all such legal advice and information as they may at any time require. He may be required to submit his
opinion upon any legal question in writing. (1969 Code, sec. 2-6)
Sec. 2-7. Duties of city secretary at commission meetings.
The city secretary shall attend every meeting of the city commission and keep account of the proceedings
thereof in a book to be provided for that purpose by the city, and to engross and enroll all laws, resolutions and
ordinances of the city commission; to take charge of and preserve and keep in order all books, records, papers,
documents and files of the commission, and to countersign all commissions issued to city officers, and all
licenses issued, and keep a record or register thereof; and to make out all notices required under any regulation
or ordinance of the city relating to his office. (1969 Code, sec. 2-7)
Sec. 2-8. Duties of city finance manager.
The city finance manager shall draw all warrants on the treasurer and countersign the same and keep an
account in a book to be furnished him by the city. He shall be general accountant of the corporation and shall
keep in books regular accounts of the receipts and disbursements for the city separately under proper hands
and also account with each person, including officers who have money transactions with the city, crediting
amounts with the city, crediting amounts allowed by proper authority and specifying the particular transaction to
which such entries apply. He shall also keep a register of bonds and bills issued by the city, and all entries of
debt and payments to it; noting the particulars thereof and facts connected therewith, as they occur. (1969
Code, sec. 2-8; Ordinance 1083 adopted 3/12/85)
Sec. 2-9. Keeping contracts; other duties.
The city secretary shall carefully keep all contracts made by the city commission on behalf of the city and he
shall do and perform such other duties as may be required by law, ordinances, resolutions, or orders of the city
commission or city manager. (1969 Code, sec. 2-9)
Sec. 2-10. Planning and zoning commission-Membership.
There is created and established for the city a planning and zoning commission, which shall be composed of
seven members. The members shall be resident citizens, taxpayers, and qualified voters of the city, all of whom
shall be appointed by the mayor subject to confirmation by the city commission. The terms of office shall be for
two years, except that of the first commissioners so appointed, the terms of three members shall be for two
years and the terms of four members shall be for three years. All vacancies shall be filled for the unexpired term
in the same manner as provided for the original appointments. All expired terms shall be filled for terms as
provided for the original appointments and in the same manner. Members of the commission may be removed
by the mayor, with the consent of the city commission, after public hearing and for cause assigned in writing.
The members of the commission shall serve without compensation. (1969 Code, sec. 2-10; Ordinance 664,
sec. 1, adopted 3/14/61)
Sec. 2-11. Same-Organization; employees; procedure.
The planning and zoning commission shall elect a chairman and vice-chairman from its membership and shall
have power to employ such qualified persons as may be necessary for the proper conduct and undertakings of
the commission and to pay for their services and such other necessary expenses; provided the cost of such
services and expenses shall not exceed the amount appropriated by the city commission for the use of the
commission. It shall also have the power to make rules, regulations, and bylaws for its own government, which
shall conform as nearly as possible with those governing the city commission. Such bylaws shall include,
among other items, provisions for:
(1) Regular and special meetings, open to the public;
(2) Records of its proceedings, to be open for inspection by the public;
(3) Reporting to the city commission and the public, from time to time and annually; and
(4) The holding of public hearings on its recommendations.
(1969 Code, sec. 2-11; Ordinance 664, sec. 2, adopted 3/14/61)
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 6/283
Sec. 2-12. Same-Powers and duties.
The planning and zoning commission shall have the power and it shall be its duty to make and recommend for
adoption a master plan, as a whole or in part, for the future development and redevelopment of the municipality
and its environs and shall have power and it shall be its duty to prepare a comprehensive plan and ordinance
for zoning the city in accordance with state law. The commission shall perform such other duties as may be
prescribed by ordinance or state law. (1969 Code, sec. 2-12; Ordinance 664, sec. 3, adopted 3/14/61)
Sec. 2-13. Purchases-Office of purchasing agent created.
The office of purchasing agent is created. (1969 Code, sec. 2-13; Resolution 484, sec. 1, adopted 6/12/34)
Sec. 2-14. Same-Commission approval; policy.
(a) Commission approval. It shall be the duty of the purchasing agent to contract for and purchase all
supplies, materials, goods, wares and merchandise, and things necessary for the use of the city in any of its
departments; provided, however, he shall not make any purchase in an amount in excess of $5,000.00, without
first having submitted the same to the city commission for its approval; and no separate purchase in an amount
in excess of $5,000.00 made without the approval of the city commission shall be binding on the city.
(b) Purchasing policy.
(1) Goods or services costing up to and including $500.00 may be purchased by department
heads or their authorized representatives.
(2) Goods and services costing more than $500.00 and up to and including $5,000.00 will require
a requisition from the requesting department. Departments will be responsible for placing an order
after soliciting at least three bids.
(3) Goods and services costing more than $5,000.00 and up to the amount as set out in V.T.C.A.,
Local Government Code sec. 252.021 will require a requisition from the requesting department.
Each department will be responsible for soliciting at least three written bids and placing an order for
the items as authorized by the city commission.
(4) Goods and services costing more than the amount as set out in V.T.C.A., Local Government
Code sec. 252.021 will require a requisition from the requesting department and must be purchased
in accordance with V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 252.
(c) Method of buying; emergency purchase order. In those instances where an emergency purchase order is
required to secure parts, service or repairs to restore equipment to operating condition, and the determination
of the total charges cannot be made in advance of the procurement of the parts, service or repairs, an
emergency purchase order authorization procedure shall apply. The emergency purchase order authorization
procedure is as follows:
(1) The requesting department will call the purchasing department for an emergency purchase
order number.
(2) The purchasing department will complete an emergency purchase order authorization. The
original may also be picked up at the purchasing department the same day.
(3) After obtaining the emergency purchase order number from the purchasing department, the
requesting department may contact the vendor and authorize the purchase of needed parts,
maintenance service of combination thereof, issuing the emergency purchase order number to the
vendor as the city's authorization for the product or service.
The original copy of the payment authorization form shall be attached to the vendor invoice and forwarded to
the accounting department for prompt payment. The duplicate copy of the payment authorization form is to be
maintained in the requesting department's file as a permanent file record of the completed repair transaction.
The emergency purchase order may not exceed the amount as set out in V.T.C.A., Local Government Code
sec. 252.021, and any amount in excess of $5,000.00 must have final approval of the finance director and the
city manager.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 7/283
(1969 Code, sec. 2-15; Resolution 484, sec. 3, adopted 6/12/34; Ordinance 1022, secs. 1, 2, adopted 5/10/83;
Ordinance 1096 adopted 6/20/85; Ordinance 1120 adopted 6/10/86; Ordinance 1501, secs. 1-3, adopted
6/2/08)
Sec. 2-15. Record of accounts.
The finance manager shall keep strict account of all invoices paid by him for and on behalf of the city, showing
the articles purchased, the amount to be paid therefor and to whom payable, and shall submit same to the city
commission for review with his approval endorsed thereon. (1969 Code, sec. 2-16; Resolution 484, sec. 4,
adopted 6/12/34; Ordinance 1097 adopted 7/9/85)
Sec. 2-16. Liability for property damage or personal injury.
The city shall never be liable for any claim for property damage or for personal injury, whether such personal
injury results in death or not unless the person damaged or injured, or someone in his behalf, or in the event the
injury results in death, the person who may have a cause of action under the law by reason of such death or
injury, shall, within six months from the date the damage or injury was received, give notice in writing to the
mayor and city commission of the following facts:
(1) The date and time when the injury occurred and the place where the injured person or
property was at the time when the injury was received.
(2) The nature of the damage or injury sustained.
(3) The apparent extent of the damage or injury sustained.
(4) A specific and detailed statement of how and under what circumstances the damage or injury
occurred.
(5) The amount for which each claimant will settle.
(6) The actual place of residence of each claimant by street, number, city and state on the date
the claim is presented.
(7) In the case of personal injury or death, the names and addresses of all persons who,
according to the knowledge or information of the claimant witnessed the happening of the injury or
any part thereof and the names of the doctors, if any, to whose care the injured person is committed.
(8) In the case of property damage, the location of the damaged property at the time the claim
was submitted along with the names and addresses of all persons who witnessed the happening of
the damage or any part thereof.
(1969 Code, sec. 2-18; Ordinance 1273, sec. 18, adopted 6/21/95)
Sec. 2-17. Adoption of policy; prohibitions; penalty; liability.
(a) The city hereby adopts and will enforce the policy prohibiting the use of excessive force by the law
enforcement agencies within its jurisdiction against any individual engaged in nonviolent civil rights
demonstrations. The city also prohibits the physical barring of any entrance or exit of such a facility and will
enforce all applicable state laws regarding the same.
(b) Any person found to be violating any provision of this section shall be served by the city with written
notice stating the nature of the violation.
(c) Any person violating any provision of this section shall be deemed guilty of an offense, and upon
conviction shall be punished by a penalty as provided in section 1-6 for each violation. Each day in which any
such violation shall continue shall be deemed a separate offense.
(d) Any person violating any provision of this article shall become liable to the city for any expense, loss, or
damage to the city by reason of such violation.
(1969 Code, sec. 2-19; Ordinance 1313, secs. 1-4, adopted 12/23/97)
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 8/283
Sec. 2-18. Collection policy.
The city manager, or his agent, is hereby directed to collect or contract with a third party agency, all delinquent
balances. The city manager is also authorized to designate certain accounts as charged-off for municipal
accounting purposes and take any steps to attempt additional collection thereafter.
The city manager in conjunction with the finance director shall develop individual collection time tables for each
type of receivable and annually review and update the accounting records and aging schedules for accounts
still outstanding from prior years and report these amounts to the finance committee for approval.
(Ordinance 1659, sec. 1, adopted 4/28/15)
Secs. 2-19—2-37. Reserved.
ARTICLE II. MAYOR
Sec. 2-38. Enforcement of commission rules.
The mayor shall have powers as president of the city commission to enforce such rules for the regulation of its
proceedings in the order of business, discussion, order and decorum as the commission may adopt. (1969
Code, sec. 2-39)
Sec. 2-39. Process or notice of proceedings against city.
Whenever any process or notice shall be served upon the mayor in any legal or other proceeding against the
city or in which the city is a party, he shall deliver the same, or a note thereof, to the city attorney in order that
same may be attended to. (1969 Code, sec. 2-40)
Sec. 2-40. Execution of instruments.
Whenever it shall be necessary by any law or ordinance of the city to execute any bond or other instrument in
any such suit or action at law, begun, or about to be instituted, or for any purpose, or whenever the city shall be
a party to any contract or agreement the same may be executed and signed by the mayor in the name of the
city and attested by the city secretary and the seal of the city affixed, and such signing, execution and
attestation, shall be valid to all intents and purposes upon the city. (1969 Code, sec. 2-41)
Secs. 2-41—2-70. Reserved.
ARTICLE III. BOARDS AND COMMISSIONS
DIVISION 1. GENERALLY
Secs. 2-71—2-90. Reserved.
DIVISION 2. LAW ENFORCEMENT ADVISORY BOARD
Sec. 2-91. Creation and establishment.
(a) There is hereby created and established a law enforcement advisory board for the purpose of reviewing
applications for financial assistance grants or projects from local, regional, state and federal agencies. This
board shall be composed of seven members. Composition of the board shall be as follows:
(1) The police chief;
(2) A representative of the Wilbarger County Crime Stoppers;
(3) An employee of the Vernon Independent School District;
(4) A representative of the local court system;
(5) An employee of the county sheriff's office;
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 9/283
(6) Chaplain of the police department; and
(7) A representative of the county attorney's office.
(b) The board members shall be resident citizens, taxpayers, and qualified voters of the city, all of whom shall
be appointed by the city commission. Terms of office shall be three consecutive years with staggered terms.
The first two board members appointed are for a one-year term, the next two board members appointed are for
a two-year term, and the last three board members appointed are for a three-year term. All vacancies shall be
filled for the unexpired term in the same manner as provided for in the original appointments. All expired terms
shall be filled for three-year terms. Members may be removed by the governing body, and serve at the pleasure
of the city commission. The members of this board shall serve without compensation.
(Ordinance 1292, sec. I, adopted 1/28/97)
Sec. 2-92. Officers of the board.
This board shall elect a chair and a vice-chair from its membership. (Ordinance 1292, sec. II, adopted 1/28/97)
Sec. 2-93. Duties and responsibilities.
The board's duties shall be for the review of law enforcement projects or applications requesting financial
assistance (grants) from local, regional, state and federal agencies. In the review of these types of projects, the
board should review these projects for duplication of services and be consistent with any approved criminal
justice long range plans for the county. Any public hearings required by a grantor agency may be held before
this body. This board shall serve in an advisory role to the city commission. All board action shall be in the form
of a recommendation to the city commission.
(Ordinance 1292, sec. III, adopted 1/28/97)
Secs. 2-94—2-116. Reserved.
DIVISION 3. MAIN STREET ADVISORY BOARD
Sec. 2-117. Board creation and establishment.
There is hereby created and established a Main Street Advisory Board for the purpose of reviewing Main Street
projects to effectuate such program. This board shall be composed of seven members. The city manager, or his
designee, is hereby assigned to coordinate the activities of this advisory board. The board members shall be
resident citizens, or owners of businesses within the city, all of whom shall be appointed by the city commission.
Terms of office shall be for three consecutive years with staggered terms. The first two board members
appointed are for a one-year term, the next two board members appointed are for a two-year term, and the last
three board members appointed are for a three-year term. All vacancies shall be filled for the unexpired term in
the same manner as provided for in the original appointments. All expired terms shall be filled for three-year
terms. Members may be removed by the city commission, and serve at the pleasure of the city commission.
The members of this board shall serve without compensation.
(1969 Code, sec. 2-81; Ordinance 1299, sec. I, adopted 1/28/97; Ordinance 1574, sec. 1, adopted 12/20/11)
Sec. 2-118. Board officers.
This board shall elect a chairperson and a vice chairperson from its membership. (1969 Code, sec. 2-82;
Ordinance 1299, sec. II, adopted 1/28/97)
Sec. 2-119. Board's duties and responsibilities.
The board's duties shall be for the review of the projects developed for the Vernon Main Street Program. In the
review of these types of projects, the board should review them for duplication of services and consistency with
the Texas Main Street Program, as defined by the state historical commission. Any public hearings required by
this state agency or any other governmental entity may be held before this body. This board shall serve in an
advisory role to the city commission, as needed. All board action shall be in the form of a recommendation to
the city commission. (1969 Code, sec. 2-83; Ordinance 1299, sec. III, adopted 1/28/97)
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 10/283
Sec. 2-120. Operational guidelines.
The city commission may adopt operating procedures and/or rules for the Main Street Advisory Board not
inconsistent with provisions of this section. A copy of which shall be kept on file in the office of the city
secretary. (Ordinance 1574, sec. 2, adopted 12/20/11)
Secs. 2-121—2-124. Reserved.
DIVISION 4. TOURISM ADVISORY BOARD
Sec. 2-125. Board creation and establishment.
There is hereby created and established a tourism advisory board for the purpose of reviewing tourism projects
funded through the hotel occupancy tax funds to effectuate such program. This board shall be composed of five
members. The city manager, or his designee, is hereby assigned to coordinate the activities of this advisory
board. The board members shall be resident citizens of the county or owners of businesses within the city, all of
whom shall be appointed by the city commission. Terms of office shall be for three consecutive years with
staggered terms. The first two board members appointed are for a one-year initial term, the next two board
members appointed are for a two-year initial term, and the last board member will be appointed for a three-year
term. All vacancies shall be filled for the unexpired term in the same manner as provided in the original
appointments, except for the fact that all expired terms shall be filled for three-year terms. Members may be
removed by the city commission, and serve at the pleasure of the city commission. The members of this board
shall serve without compensation. (Ordinance 1651, sec. 1, adopted 10/21/14)
Sec. 2-126. Board officers.
The board shall elect a chairperson and a vice-chairperson from its membership. (Ordinance 1651, sec. 2,
adopted 10/21/14)
Sec. 2-127. Board's duties and responsibilities.
The board's duties shall be for the review of the projects developed for the city tourism program. In review of
these types of projects, the board should review them for duplication of services and consistency with V.T.C.A.,
State Tax Code sec. 156. Any public hearings required by this section of the tax code or any other applicable
statute may be held before this body. This board shall serve in an advisory role to the city commission, as
needed. All board action shall be in the form of a recommendation to the city commission. (Ordinance 1651,
sec. 3, adopted 10/21/14)
Sec. 2-128. Operational guidelines.
The city commission may adopt operating procedures and/or rules for the tourism advisory board not
inconsistent with provisions of this division. A copy of which shall be kept on file in the office of the city
secretary. (Ordinance 1651, sec. 4, adopted 10/21/14)
Secs. 2-129—2-136. Reserved.
ARTICLE IV. RECORDS MANAGEMENT PROGRAM*
Sec. 2-137. City records.
All documents, papers, letters, books, maps, photographs, sound or video recordings, microfilm, magnetic
tapes, electronic media, or other information regarding media, regardless of physical form or characteristic and
of whether public access to it is open or restricted under the laws of the state, created or received by the city or
any of its officers or employees pursuant to law or in the transaction of public business are hereby declared to
be the records of the city and shall be created, maintained, and disposed of in accordance with the provisions
of this article or procedures authorized by it and in no other manner. (1969 Code, sec. 2-105; Ordinance 1502,
sec. 1, adopted 6/2/08)
Sec. 2-138. Definitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in
this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 11/283
Department head means the officer, who by ordinance, order, or administrative policy is in charge of an office of
the city that creates or receives records.
Essential record means any record of the city necessary to the resumption or continuation of operations of the
city in an emergency or disaster, to the re-creation of the legal and financial status of the city, or to the
protection and fulfillment of obligations to the people of the state.
Permanent record means any record of the city for which the retention period on a records control schedule is
given as permanent.
Records control schedule means a document prepared by or under the authority of the records management
officer listing the records maintained by the city, the retention periods, and other records disposition information
that the records management program may require.
Records liaison officer means a person designated under section 2-146.
Records management means the application of management techniques to the creation, use, maintenance,
retention, preservation, and disposal of records for the purposes of reducing the costs and improving the
efficiency of recordkeeping. The term “records management” includes the development of records control
schedules, the management of filing and information retrieval systems, the protection of essential and
permanent records, the economical and space-effective storage of inactive records, control over the creation
and distribution of forms, reports, and correspondence, and the management of micrographics and electronic
and other records storage systems.
Records management committee means the committee established in section 2-142.
Records management officer means the person designated under section 2-141.
Records management plan means the plan developed under section 2-143.
Retention period means the minimum time that must pass after the creation, recording, or receipt of a record, or
the fulfillment of certain actions associated with a record, before it is eligible for destruction.
(1969 Code, sec. 2-106; Ordinance 1502, sec. 2, adopted 6/2/08)
Sec. 2-139. City records declared public property.
All city records as defined in section 2-137 are hereby declared to be the property of the city. No city official or
employee has, by virtue of his position, any personal or property right to such records even though he may
have developed or compiled them. The unauthorized destruction, removal from files, or use of such records is
prohibited. (1969 Code, sec. 2-107; Ordinance 1502, sec. 3, adopted 6/2/08)
Sec. 2-140. Policy.
It is hereby declared to be the policy of the city to provide for efficient, economical, and effective controls over
the creation, distribution, organization, maintenance, use, and disposition of all city records through a
comprehensive system of integrated procedures for the management of records from creation to ultimate
disposition, consistent with the requirements of the Texas Local Government Records Act and accepted records
management practice. (1969 Code, sec. 2-108; Ordinance 1502, sec. 4, adopted 6/2/08)
Sec. 2-141. Designation of records management officer.
The city secretary, and the successive holders of said office, shall serve as records management officer for the
city. As provided by state law, each successive holder of the office shall file his name with the director and
librarian of the state library within 30 days of the initial designation or of taking up the office, as applicable.
(1969 Code, sec. 2-109; Ordinance 1502, sec. 5, adopted 6/2/08)
Sec. 2-142. Establishment of records management committee: duties.
A records management committee consisting of the city manager, finance director, and city secretary is hereby
established. The committee shall:
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 12/283
(1) Assist the records management officer in the development of policies and procedures
governing the records management program;
(2) Review the performance of the program on a regular basis and propose changes and
improvements if needed;
(3) Review and approve records control schedules submitted by the records management officer;
(4) Give final approval to the destruction of records in accordance with approved records control
schedule; and
(5) Actively support and promote the records management program throughout the city.
(1969 Code, sec. 2-110; Ordinance 1502, sec. 6, adopted 6/2/08)
Sec. 2-143. Records management plan development, approval; authority of plan.
(a) The records management officer and the records management committee shall develop a records
management plan for the city for submission to the city commission. The plan must contain policies and
procedures designed to reduce the costs and improve the efficiency of recordkeeping, to adequately protect the
essential records of the city, and to properly preserve those records of the city that are of historical value. The
plan must be designed to enable the records management officer to carry out his duties prescribed by state law
and this article effectively.
(b) Once approved by the city commission, the records management plan shall be binding on all offices,
departments, divisions, programs, commissions, bureaus, boards, committees, or similar entities of the city and
records shall be created, maintained, stored, microfilmed, or disposed of in accordance with the plan.
(c) State law relating to the duties, other responsibilities, or recordkeeping requirements of a department
head do not exempt the department head or the records in the department head's care from the application of
this article and the records management plan adopted under it and may not be used by the department head as
a basis for refusal to participate in the records management program of the city.
(1969 Code, sec. 2-111; Ordinance 1502, sec. 7, adopted 6/2/08)
Sec. 2-144. Duties of records management officer.
In addition to other duties assigned in this article, the records management officer shall:
(1) Administer the records management program and provide assistance to department heads in
its implementation;
(2) Plan, formulate, and prescribe records disposition policies, systems, standards, and
procedures;
(3) In cooperation with department heads, identify essential records and establish a disaster plan
for each city office and department to ensure maximum availability of the records in order to reestablish
operations quickly and with minimum disruption and expense;
(4) Develop procedures to ensure the permanent preservation of the historical valuable records of
the city;
(5) Establish standards for filing and storage equipment and for recordkeeping supplies;
(6) Study the feasibility of and, if appropriate, establish a uniform filing system and a forms design
and control system for the city;
(7) Provide records management advice and assistance to all city departments by preparation of a
manual or manuals of procedure and policy and by on-site consultation;
(8) Monitor records retention schedules and administrative rules issued by the Texas State Library
and Archives Commission to determine if the records management program and the city's records
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 13/283
control schedules are in compliance with state regulations;
(9) Disseminate to the city manager and department heads information concerning state laws and
administrative rules relating to local government records;
(10) Instruct records liaison officers and other personnel in policies and procedures of the records
management plan and their duties in the records management program;
(11) Direct record liaison officers or other personnel in the conduct of record inventories in
preparation for the development of records control schedules as required by state law and this
article;
(12) Ensure the maintenance, preservation, microfilming, destruction, or other disposition of the
records of the city is carried out in accordance with the policies and procedures of the records
management program and the requirements of state law;
(13) Maintain records on the volume of records destroyed under approved records control
schedules, or through records destruction authorization requests, the volume of records microfilmed
or stored electronically, and the estimated cost and space savings as the result of such disposal or
disposition;
(14) Report annually to the city commission on the implementation of the records management
plan in each department of the city, including summaries of the statistical and fiscal data compiled
under subsection (13) of this section; and
(15) Bring to the attention of the city commission, noncompliance by department heads or other
city personnel with the policies and procedures of the records management program of the Local
Government Records Act.
(1969 Code, sec. 2-112; Ordinance 1502, sec. 8, adopted 6/2/08)
Sec. 2-145. Duties and responsibilities of department heads.
In addition to other duties assigned in this article, department heads shall:
(1) Cooperate with the records management officer in carrying out the policies and procedures
established in the city for the efficient and economical management of records and in carrying out
the requirements of this article;
(2) Adequately document the transaction of government business and the services, programs,
and duties for which the department head and his staff are responsible; and
(3) Maintain the records in his care and carry out preservation, microfilming, destruction, or other
disposition only in accordance with the policies and procedures of the records management program
of the city and the requirements of this article.
(1969 Code, sec. 2-113; Ordinance 1502, sec. 9, adopted 6/2/08)
Sec. 2-146. Designation of records liaison officers.
Each department head, or a person within the department designated by the department head, shall serve as
records liaison officer for his department. (1969 Code, sec. 2-114; Ordinance 1502, sec. 10, adopted 6/2/08)
Sec. 2-147. Duties and responsibilities of records liaison officers.
In addition to other duties assigned in this article, records liaison officers shall:
(1) Conduct or supervise the conduct of inventories of the records of the department in
preparation for the development of records control schedules;
(2) In cooperation with the records management officer, coordinate and implement the policies
and procedures of the records management program in their departments; and
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 14/283
(3) Disseminate information to department staff concerning the records management program.
(1969 Code, sec. 2-115; Ordinance 1502, sec. 11, adopted 6/2/08)
Sec. 2-148. Records control schedules developed, approved; state filing.
(a) The records management officer, in cooperation with department heads, shall prepare records control
schedules on a department-by-department basis listing all records created or received by the department and
the retention period for each record.
(b) Each records control schedule shall be monitored and amended, as needed, by the records management
officer on a regular basis to ensure that it is in compliance with records retention schedules issued by the state
and that it continues to reflect the recordkeeping procedures and needs of the department and the records
management program of the city.
(c) Before its adoption, a records control schedule, or amended schedule, for a department must be
approved by the department head and the members of the records management committee.
(d) Before its adoption, a records control schedule must be submitted and accepted for filing by the director
and librarian as provided by state law.
(1969 Code, sec. 2-116; Ordinance 1502, sec. 12, adopted 6/2/08)
Sec. 2-149. Records control schedule implementation; destruction of records under schedule.
(a) A records control schedule for a department that has been approved and adopted under section 2-143
shall be implemented by department heads according to the policies and procedures of the records
management plan.
(b) A record whose retention period has expired on a records control schedule shall be destroyed unless an
open records request is pending on the record, the subject matter of the record is pertinent to a pending law
suit, or the department head requests in writing to the records management committee that the record be
retained for an additional period.
(c) Prior to the destruction of a record under an approved records control schedule, authorization for the
destruction must be obtained by the records management officer from the records management committee.
(1969 Code, sec. 2-117; Ordinance 1502, sec. 13, adopted 6/2/08)
Sec. 2-150. Destruction of unscheduled records.
A record that has not yet been listed on an approved records control schedule may be destroyed, if its
destruction has been approved in the same manner as a record destroyed under an approved schedule and the
records management officer has submitted to and received back from the director and librarian an approved
destruction authorization request. (1969 Code, sec. 2-118; Ordinance 1502, sec. 14, adopted 6/2/08)
CHAPTER 4
ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES*
Sec. 4-1. Definitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them
in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning. A term defined in the state
alcoholic beverage code has the meaning it has in the state alcoholic beverage code, except as otherwise
specifically provided in this chapter.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 15/283
Place of business means the location of the business identified in the application for the permit or license to sell
alcohol under this chapter.
(1969 Code, sec. 3-1; Ordinance 1434, sec. 1, adopted 1/25/05)
Sec. 4-2. Construction consistent with state law.
This chapter shall be construed to be consistent with the state alcoholic beverage code, rules, and regulations
promulgated under its authority. (1969 Code, sec. 3-2; Ordinance 1434, sec. 2, adopted 1/25/05)
Sec. 4-3. Restriction on sale or use of alcohol.
A person commits an offense if the person sells, stores, handles for the purpose of sale an alcoholic beverage,
unless the use is authorized by and complies with the applicable provisions of this Code and the state alcoholic
beverage code. (1969 Code, sec. 3-3; Ordinance 1434, sec. 3, adopted 1/25/05)
Sec. 4-4. Minimum distance from certain uses.
(a) Except as provided by the state alcoholic beverage code, a person may not sell or engage in the
business of selling an alcoholic beverage at a place of business located within 300 feet from the following:
(1) A private school;
(2) A day care center;
(3) A childcare facility;
(4) A church; or
(5) A public hospital.
(b) Except as provided by the state alcoholic beverage code, a person may not sell or engage in the
business of selling an alcoholic beverage at a place of business located within 1,000 feet of a public school.
(c) Distances under this section shall be calculated using the method prescribed by the state alcoholic
beverage code.
(1969 Code, sec. 3-4; Ordinance 1434, sec. 4, adopted 1/25/05)
Sec. 4-5. Exceptions to required minimum distances.
(a) Section 4-4 (minimum distances from certain uses) does not apply to:
(1) The renewal or transfer of a permit or license to sell alcoholic beverages, if the permit or
license being renewed or transferred was originally issued before the date a private school, church,
public hospital, day care center, or child care facility use was established within 300 feet or a public
school use was established within 1,000 feet from the place of business named in the permit or
license; or
(2) A new application at a location, if the sale of alcoholic beverages at the proposed place of
business was authorized not less than one year before the date a private school, church, public
hospital, day care center, or child care facility use was established within 300 feet or a public school
use was established within 1,000 feet from the place of business, and the new application is filed no
later than 90 days after the previous permit or license authorizing the sale of alcoholic beverages at
that location expired or was terminated.
(b) Section 4-4 (minimum distances from certain uses) does not apply to a permit or license holder who sells
alcoholic beverages if:
(1) The permit or license holder's place of business and the private school, day care center or
child care facility are located on different stories of a multistory building; or
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 16/283
(2) The permit or license holder's place of business and the private school or day-care center or
child-care facility are located in separate buildings and either the permit or license holder's place of
business or the private school or day care center or child care facility is located on the second story
or higher of a multistory building.
(1969 Code, sec. 3-5; Ordinance 1434, sec. 5, adopted 1/25/05)
Sec. 4-6. Approval of certificate for permit or license.
Before the city secretary shall sign any certificate for an applicant for a permit or license required by the state
alcoholic beverage code, such certificate shall be submitted to the community development director to ensure
that the application complies with this chapter. (1969 Code, sec. 3-6; Ordinance 1434, sec. 6, adopted 1/25/05)
Sec. 4-7. Permit fees and issuance.
(a) Unless state law exempts a permittee or licensee from payment of a fee established by this section, a
permittee or licensee must pay the city an annual permit or license fee of one-half the amount of the state fee
for each permit and license authorizing the sale of alcoholic beverages.
(b) An applicant shall pay the fees established under subsection (a) of this section to the community
development director no later than the 30th day after the date the applicant's payment of a state permit or
license fee is due.
(c) A permittee or licensee who sells an alcoholic beverage at a business location before the applicant pays
the fees established by this section commits a class C misdemeanor, punishable in accordance with this
chapter.
(d) The community development director shall issue and deliver a receipt under this section to the permittee
or licensee authorizing the sale of alcoholic beverages under this chapter and a state permit or license, if the
permittee or licensee:
(1) Pays the fees established by subsection (a) of this section; and
(2) Exhibits the permit or license issued by the state.
(1969 Code, sec. 3-7; Ordinance 1434, sec. 7, adopted 1/25/05)
Sec. 4-8. Penalty.
A person who violates this chapter commits an offense punishable under section 1-6. An offense under this
chapter is a class C misdemeanor. (1969 Code, sec. 3-8; Ordinance 1434, sec. 8, adopted 1/25/05)
