CHAPTER 8
ANIMALS AND FOWL
ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL
Sec. 8-1. Definitions.
Terms as used in this chapter shall have the respective meanings ascribed to them:
Animal means any live, nonhuman, vertebrate creature, be it domestic, wild, livestock, reptile, or other.
Animal control officer means:
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 18/283
(1) An employee of the city police department authorized to enforce all ordinances and state laws
pertaining to the ownership, care, and management of animals by exercising lawful authority to issue
citations, notices of violation, and seizing animals, and obtaining warrants or court orders pertaining
to animals;
(2) Any state peace officer acting to enforce this chapter or state laws pertaining to animals.
At large means any animal not restrained, including, without limitation, domestic, wild, and livestock animals as
defined herein and estrays as defined in state law.
Commercial feeding means the feeding of livestock for gain other than as may be naturally grown on the
premises with nominal, seasonal, or drought feeding of supplemental food.
Dangerous animal. Any animal shall be deemed dangerous upon the occurrence of any of the following events:
(1) An unprovoked attack on a person, domestic animal, or livestock causing serious bodily injury
by an animal outside a secure enclosure in which the attacking animal is kept;
(2) An unprovoked attack of aggression by an animal outside a secure enclosure which causes a
person to reasonably believe the animal will attack and cause serious bodily injury to a human or to
a domestic animal or livestock; or
(3) Certification by a doctor of veterinary medicine that an animal poses a danger to human life,
animal life, or property based on a reasonable medical probability after observation.
Domestic animal means those animals which are naturally tame and gentle or which, by long association with
man, have become thoroughly domesticated and are now reduced to such a state of subjection to his will that
they no longer possess the disposition or inclination to escape. The term “domestic animal” specifically includes
household pets, such as dogs and cats and miniature animals.
Kennel means any place where five or more animals, not wild, livestock, or estray, over the age of four months,
are raised, trained, boarded, harbored, or kept. A farm, ranch, horse lot (private or commercial), private stable,
veterinary clinic, animal hospital, and an animal pound, as defined in the zoning ordinance outlined in appendix
A to this Code, are specifically excluded from this definition.
Livestock means:
(1) Any species or family of bovine, ox, cattle, swine, pig, horse, equine, tapir, elephant, deer, or
antelope;
(2) Other grass- or plant-eating single- or cloven-hoofed mammals, whether indigenous to this
state or not;
(3) Any species or family of domestic barnyard animal, such as, a duck, chicken, goose, pigeon,
guinea, rabbit, other bird or fowl, emu, ostrich, or any other animal (not listed in this chapter as
domestic or wild) which may be raised for human consumption in the United States of America; and
(4) Any animal designated or defined by state law as an estray when straying or at large.
Microchip means a passive electronic device that is injected into an animal by means of a hypodermic-type
device. Each microchip must contain a unique and original number that is readable by an electronic scanning
device for purposes of animal identification. The microchip shall be supplied with a tag that must be attached to
the animal's collar to notify others of the presence of the microchip.
Miniature animals means those animals, not wild or livestock, which when fully grown do not exceed 18 inches
in height at shoulder level and weight no more than 90 pounds are considered to be miniature.
Neutered means any animal, male or female, rendered incapable of breeding or being bred.
Owner means any person who owns, keeps, harbors, controls (physically or by verbal or hand commands),
feeds, shelters or aids any animal; or any person who is the owner's agent left in charge of an animal or any
person who states that he will be responsible for an animal.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 19/283
Restrain. Any animal shall be deemed to be restrained when it is:
(1) Confined on the premises of the owner within a fenced enclosure, capable of confining the
animal, and pursuant to and in compliance with all applicable city ordinances regarding such fenced
enclosures;
(2) Under the control of a person by a leash of at least five and not more than ten feet in length
and of sufficient strength to control the animal while the animal is being walked; or
(3) Within a vehicle being driven or parked.
Serious bodily injury means an injury characterized by severe bite wounds or severe ripping and tearing of
muscle that would cause a reasonably prudent person or animal owner to seek treatment from a medical
professional or veterinarian and would require hospitalization or clinic treatment or veterinarian services.
Sterilized. See Neutered.
Wild animal means any animal of a wild nature or disposition to require to be reclaimed and made tame by art,
industry, or education, or else must be kept in confinement to be brought within the immediate control of the
owner. Without limiting the general definition just stated, this term specifically includes poisonous reptiles, a wolf
hybrid, or any nondomestic animal whose normal bodyweight at maturity is typically 15 pounds or more.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-1; Ordinance 556, sec. 3, adopted 5/14/47; Ordinance 658, sec. 2, adopted 5/10/60;
Ordinance 1320, sec. 1, adopted 7/28/98; Ordinance 1386, sec. 1, adopted 1/22/02; Ordinance 1419, sec. 1,
adopted 10/28/03; Ordinance 1472, sec. 1, adopted 1/23/07; Ordinance 1500, sec. 1, adopted 4/15/08)
Sec. 8-2. Inhumane treatment.
It is unlawful and a violation of this article to cruelly treat an animal, as defined in V.T.C.A., Penal Code sec.
42.09. Upon discovering or being notified by any person that an animal is or may be cruelly treated as
prescribed by V.T.C.A., Penal Code sec. 42.09, or successor statute, an animal control officer shall investigate
such charges. If probable cause is found for an allegation of cruelty to an animal, then the animal control officer
may issue a citation for the violation of this section, or refer the matter to the county attorney for prosecution in
the county court, or seize the animal pursuant to V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 821, or a combination of
these. The animal control officer shall follow V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 821, or successor statute, as
it relates to hearings, seizure and disposition of such allegedly cruelly treated animal. The remedies for
inhumane or cruel treatment of animals are under this chapter. V.T.C.A., Penal Code sec. 42.09, or V.T.C.A.,
Health and Safety Code ch. 821, are cumulative and the use of one does not preclude use of another in a given
case. (1969 Code, sec. 4-1.1; Ordinance 937, sec. 1, adopted 2/14/78; Ordinance 1472, sec. 2, adopted
1/23/07)
Sec. 8-3. Setting traps prohibited.
No person shall expose an open trap or metal jaw trap that shall be liable to injure any domestic animal or
person. (1969 Code, sec. 4-1.2; Ordinance 1472, sec. 4, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-4. Proper care of animals.
Every owner or other person having care and control of any animal shall provide the following for each animal
under his care and control:
(1) Sufficient nutritious and wholesome food served to the animal in clean containers, to maintain
the animal in good health;
(2) Clean and wholesome water served to the animal in a clean container, such water to be
available to the animal at all times;
(3) Adequate shelter which shall allow the animal to remain dry and protected from the elements
at all times and which shall provide either natural or artificial shade for the animal to avoid direct
sunlight. If the shelter is provided by enclosure, the enclosure shall allow for adequate ventilation;
and
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 20/283
(4) Veterinary care, as needed to prevent suffering.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-1.3; Ordinance 1500, sec. 2, adopted 4/15/08)
Sec. 8-5. Nuisance animals.
(a) It shall be unlawful for any person to own or maintain an animal in such a manner as to constitute a public
nuisance. The following acts shall constitute a public nuisance:
(1) Failure to restrain an animal, except and unless the animal is under control and obedience to
oral command in the course of:
a. Duties or training as a working or service animal; or
b. While performing in an organized exhibition or training event is scheduled and held in a
public venue or business.
(2) Damage to property caused by an animal.
(3) Maintaining a domestic animal or livestock in an unsanitary environment, which shall include
but not be limited to the failure to remove urine and feces daily from the confinement area to
minimize the breeding of flies and rodents.
(4) Permitting an animal to bark, whine, howl, crow, cackle, or make any other noise which causes
annoyance or interference with the reasonable use and enjoyment of a premises.
(5) Herding of animals along or upon any public right-of-way, except by any officer, agent or
employee of the federal, state or local government or agency thereof, if such herding is done in the
performance of his official duties.
(b) It shall be a nuisance and unlawful for any person to keep livestock within any enclosure within the limits
of the city that contains less than 1,600 square feet of floor or ground space for each head of livestock, except
for keeping of livestock upon the premises of public and private schools, fairs, livestock shows, of a licensed
veterinarian's office, or of a United States Department of Agriculture's inspected meat processing facility. For
purposes of this section, the term “livestock” shall include swine, horses, donkeys, mules, goats, sheep, and
other animals of the ox kind or bovine species.
(c) It shall be a nuisance and unlawful for any person to keep livestock within any enclosure within the limits
of the city that is within 50 feet of a occupied residence, except for keeping of livestock upon the premises of
public and private schools, fairs, livestock shows, of a licensed veterinarian's office, or of a United States
Department of Agriculture's inspected meat processing facility.
(d) All domestic animals authorized to be kept shall be confined to the premises of the owner or custodian of
such domestic animal, and it shall be unlawful for any person to allow such domestic animal to run or fly at
large, or go upon the premises of another person, or to allow any shelter or cage for any animal to be located in
violation of applicable building setback lines, as set forth in zoning appendix A. No domestic animal shall be
kept within a front yard of a residential dwelling as this term is defined in zoning appendix A.
(e) It shall be a nuisance and unlawful for the owner or custodian of any animal which has been killed or died,
and which is not intended as food for human consumption, to permit or suffer any such dead animal to remain
upon any premises.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-2; Ordinance 223, sec. 1, adopted 6/13/1906; Ordinance 1472, sec. 4, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-6. Vaccination.
(a) No person shall own, keep or harbor a dog or cat, within the city limits unless a licensed veterinarian shall
have vaccinated the dog or cat with antirabies vaccine.
(b) The minimum requirements are that dogs and cats shall be so vaccinated at the ages and intervals
specified by regulations of the state department of health or its successor agency.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 21/283
(1969 Code, sec. 4-3; Ordinance 223, sec. 7, adopted 6/13/1906; Ordinance 1472, sec. 6, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-7. Vaccination tag.
Upon complying with the vaccination provisions of this chapter, there shall be issued to the owner a numbered
metallic tag stamped with the number and year of vaccination. Dogs and cats shall at all times wear the rabies
vaccination tag issued to that animal. (1969 Code, sec. 4-4; Ordinance 223, sec. 8, adopted 6/13/1906;
Ordinance 1472, sec. 7, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-8. Dangerous animals.
(a) As a public safety requirement. It shall be unlawful for any person to keep or harbor any dangerous
animal within the corporate limits of the city without complying with V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code sec.
822.042, as amended, whether the animal be a dog or of another species. In addition, the owner must comply
with each of the following local requirements, at the owner's expense, before the animal is released from the
county humane society's animal shelter:
(1) Obtain liability insurance coverage or showing financial responsibility in an amount of at least
$250,000.00 to cover damages resulting from an attack by the dangerous animal causing bodily
injury to a person or for damages to any person's property resulting from the keeping of such
dangerous animal. A certificate of insurance or other evidence of meeting the above requirements
shall be filed with the police department. The policy must require the company to give advance
notice to the city of cancellation or non-renewal of the policy;
(2) Register with the city by providing:
a. The name and address of the owner;
b. The breed, age, sex, color and any other identifying marks of the animal;
c. The location where the animal is to be kept, if it is not at the address of the owner; and
d. Two color photographs that clearly identify the dangerous animal;
(3) Have the animal sterilized;
(4) Construct a cage, pen, or enclosure for the dangerous animal that has secure sides; a secure
top attached to the sides; and a secure bottom which is either attached to the sides or else the sides
of the structure must be embedded in the ground no less than two feet. The pen or enclosure must
be completely encircled by a fence constructed in such a manner as to prevent a person or child
from being able to reach the animal's pen or enclosure;
(5) Not allow the animal to go outside of its cage, pen, or enclosure unless the animal is under
physical restraint. No person shall permit a dangerous animal to be kept outside of its cage, pen, or
enclosure on a chain, rope, or other type of leash unless a person is in physical control of the chain,
rope, or other type of leash and the person is of competent strength to control the animal at all times.
Dangerous animals shall not be leashed to inanimate objects, such as trees, posts, buildings, etc. All
dangerous animals outside their cage, pen, or enclosure must be securely fitted with a muzzle that
will not cause injury to the animal nor interfere with its vision or respiration but shall prevent the
animal from biting other animals or human beings;
(6) Post signs giving notice of a dangerous animal on the premises in which such animal is
confined. Such signs shall be conspicuously posted at both the front and rear property entrances
and shall bear letters not less than two inches high, stating “dangerous animal on premises.” Such
signs shall also display a symbol, that is understandable by small children, that warns of the
presence of a dangerous animal;
(7) Attach a fluorescent orange tag provided by the police department to the animal's collar that is
worn at all times so that the animal can be easily identified;
(8) Implant a microchip into the animal which is compatible with a scanning equipment used by
the animal control authority and register it for life with the city's police department and a recognized
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 22/283
national animal registry;
(9) Pay the appropriate dangerous animal permit fee annually, not later than five business days
prior to the annual expiration renewal date;
(10) Pay the impoundment and daily care fees accrued during the investigation and any appeal of
the dangerous animal determination process; and
(11) Present proof of current vaccination or pay the fee for vaccination.
In the event the owner or keeper fails or refuses to timely comply with these requirements in
accordance with state law, then the animal control officers shall humanely destroy the dangerous
animal.
(b) Complaint. When a person reports a dangerous animal to the animal control authorities, the authorities
shall investigate the report and notify the owner of the report. The animal control authority shall obtain a sworn
written statement from at least one witness, describing at a minimum:
(1) The animal;
(2) The facts of the complaint;
(3) Identity of any other known witness; and
(4) Other information necessary or helpful to the investigation.
(c) Investigation. The animal control authorities shall conclude the investigation no longer than ten days after
receipt of the report or sworn statement, which ever occurs later. Upon completion of investigation the animal
control authorities shall either:
(1) Close the case if it is determined that the report or complaint is unsubstantiated; or
(2) Declare the animal to be a dangerous animal.
(d) Seizure pending disposition. Upon sworn application of the animal control authorities or a peace officer
stating probable cause that the animal is dangerous and there is some reason to believe that the animal may
endanger other persons before the investigation and any hearings or appeals can be completed, then a
municipal court judge may issue a warrant authorizing the animal control authorities or peace officer to:
(1) Retain the animal if it has been captured at large; or
(2) Enter the building, dwelling, other structure or enclosure to seize the animal and detain same,
until disposition of the investigation and any hearing and appeal.
(e) Notice. The police chief or his designee shall promptly notify the owner or keeper of the animal of his
determination on the dangerousness of the animal, by a written notice mailed to or posted on the front door of
the last known address of the owner or keeper or other means reasonably calculated to give actual notice of the
determination to the owner.
(f) Appeal.
(1) The owner may appeal the dangerous animal determination by filing a written notice of appeal
to municipal court within 15 days after the determination, for a trial de novo. The consequences of
the determination shall be suspended pending the municipal court judge's final decision, but the
animal control authority shall retain the custody and care of the animal until all appeals are
exhausted. An owner may appeal a decision of the municipal court to the county court at law, in
accordance with V.T.C.A., Government Code ch. 30, as amended. Following a final judicial
determination that the animal is dangerous, each day the owner fails to comply with subsection (a)
of this section shall constitute a separate violation of this chapter.
(2) The municipal court judge may compel the attendance of complainant, any known witnesses,
the animal owner against whom the complaint was filed, and the police chief or his representative
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 23/283
who investigated. The city shall be represented by the city attorney or assistant in all appeals of a
dangerous animal determination.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-5; Ordinance 223, sec. 2, adopted 6/13/1906; Ordinance 1320, sec. 2, adopted 7/28/98;
Ordinance 1472, sec. 8, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-9. Female dogs and cats in heat.
It shall be unlawful for any owner of any female dog or cat in heat to fail to keep such animal confined in a
building or in a veterinary hospital or boarding kennel, in such a manner that another dog or cat cannot come
into contact with it, except for controlled breeding purposes. (1969 Code, sec. 4-6; Ordinance 223, sec. 3,
adopted 6/13/1906; Ordinance 1075 adopted 12/11/84; Ordinance 1320, sec. 3, adopted 7/28/98; Ordinance
1472, sec. 9, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-10. Guard dogs.
(a) Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:
Guard dog means any dog trained or used to protect persons, premises, or property by attacking or threatening
to attack any person found within the area patrolled by the dog and that is either securely enclosed within the
area at all times or under the continuous control of a trained handler.
Nonresidential or multifamily use means the placing of guard dogs on any nonresidential or multifamily property,
whether the dogs are owned by the property owner, tenant, or other person with the right of possession or
control of the property, or whether the dogs are owned by another.
(b) Requirements for use of guard dogs. It shall be unlawful for any person to place or maintain guard dogs in
any area for the protection of person or property unless the following provisions are met:
(1) The dogs shall be confined to an enclosed area adequate to ensure they will not escape.
(2) They shall be under the absolute control of a handler at all times when not securely enclosed.
(3) The owner or other persons in control of a premises upon which a guard dog is maintained
shall post a warning sign at each entrance to the area under guard with lettering clearly visible from
a distance of 50 feet, and shall additionally, in the case of the nonresidential or multifamily land uses,
contain a telephone number where some person responsible for controlling such guard dog can be
reached 24 hours a day.
(4) Prior to the placing of guard dogs on any nonresidential or multifamily property, the persons
responsible for the placing shall inform the police department in writing of their intention to post such
dogs, the number of dogs to be posted, the location where dogs will be posted, and the approximate
length of time the dogs will be guarding the area.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-7; Ordinance 223, sec. 4, adopted 6/13/1906; Ordinance 1472, sec. 10, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-11. Records.
It shall be the duty of the police department to keep, or cause to be kept, accurate and detailed records of the
following:
(1) Impounding and disposition. Records shall be kept that detail the impoundment and
disposition of all animals coming into the county humane society's custody. Such records shall be
kept for a period of at least three years and shall give the description of all animals impounded, date
of impounding, date of sale or other disposition, the amount realized for such animal and the name
and address of the purchaser.
(2) Bite cases. All bite cases reported to the police department and the investigation of the same.
(3) Monies received by the county humane society. All monies received under the provisions of
this chapter. Such records shall be open to inspection at reasonable times by persons responsible
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 24/283
for similar records of the city, and shall be audited annually in the same manner as other city records
are audited.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-8; Ordinance 223, sec. 5, adopted 6/13/1906; Ordinance 1472, sec. 11, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-12. Fees.
(a) Impoundment fees. Any animal impounded under the provisions of this chapter may be reclaimed by the
owner or person taking custody of such animal upon complying with section 8-80 and payment of the following
fees based upon owner impoundment records within a two-year period:
(1) Impoundment of any animal, except those outlined in subsection (a)(2) and (3) of this section:
(A) First impoundment: $15.00.
(B) Second impoundment and thereafter: $75.00.
(2) Impoundment of livestock: double the fees listed in subsection (a)(1) of this section, per head.
(3) Daily care fees (excluding first day of impoundment): $10.00 per day.
(b) Other fees.
(1) Rabies vaccination fee, pursuant to section 8-6 (with humane society receipt): $10.00.
(2) Bite animal, impoundment, and observation, ten days: $100.00.
(3) Requested pathological examination: $80.00.
(4) Any impounded animal other than livestock that is adopted by a person, other than the original
owner, must pay for the neutering of the animal: $65.00.
(5) Registration of dangerous animal: $100.00.
(c) Computation of boarding day. For fee computation purposes, each boarding day shall begin at 12:01 p.m.
The daily fee rate shall be applicable when an animal is kept for any portion of a day.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-9; Ordinance 223, sec. 6, adopted 6/13/1906; Ordinance 1472, sec. 12, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-13. Commercial feeding of livestock.
It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in commercial feeding operations of livestock unless the premises
are zoned as a heavy industrial district as set forth in zoning appendix A. (1969 Code, sec. 4-10; Ordinance
240, sec. 1, adopted 7/13/1909; Ordinance 1472, sec. 13, adopted 1/23/07)
Secs. 8-14—8-44. Reserved.
ARTICLE II. WILD ANIMALS AND LIVESTOCK
Sec. 8-45. Applicability.
This article shall be applicable only to wild animals and livestock, as defined in section 8-1. (1969 Code, sec. 4-
21; Ordinance 1472, sec. 14, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-46. Keeping or harboring.
(a) It shall be unlawful to keep, harbor or maintain within the city limits the following:
(1) Any animal designated by the state department of health as an animal with a high-risk of
having rabies.
(2) Any wild animal.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 25/283
(b) This section shall not apply to or prohibit the following:
(1) A publicly or privately owned zoo maintained or operated by a nonprofit organization or
governmental entity.
(2) A publicly or privately maintained circus, traveling show or rodeo, which does not remain in the
city longer than 15 consecutive days.
(3) A retail or commercial business located in a C-C, C-A/R, C-G, C-F, I-L, or I-H zoning district as
defined by the zoning appendix A, and displaying one poisonous snake on its premises solely for
purposes of educating the general public, provided:
a. An application to display the snake has been submitted to and approved by the police
chief;
b. The display area/controlled environment wherein the snake is to be displayed has been
inspected by the police department; and
c. The display area/controlled environment wherein the snake is displayed is maintained in
such a manner as to ensure the safety of the general public and the health of the snake and
meets the following minimum requirements:
1. The display area/controlled environment must be lock secured to prevent
movement.
2. The display area/controlled environment must be so placed as to prevent any
physical contact by the public.
3. The length of the display area/controlled environment must be equal to or exceed
the length of the snake's body, with a depth and height equal to or exceeding half the
snake's length.
(4) A television or motion picture production company in possession or custody of a wild animal
during the filming of a television or motion picture within the city limits.
(5) A research facility, as defined by section 2(e) of the Animal Welfare Act (7 USC 2132(e)), as
amended, that is licensed by the Secretary of Agriculture under that Act.
(c) In the event a wild animal allowed within the city limits, pursuant to one of the exceptions found in this
section, should escape from its cage, confinement, or other restraint, then the owner or person in custody of the
wild animal shall immediately notify either the city police department, or county sheriff. Failure to immediately
make this notification is an offense.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-22; Ordinance 1472, sec. 14, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-47. Impoundment.
Any animal control officer may take up and impound at the county humane society's animal shelter any of the
following found within the city limits:
(1) A wild animal (unless excepted by section 8-46(b);
(2) An excepted wild animal, which has escaped and is at large;
(3) Livestock at large found within the city limits in violation of either this chapter or V.T.C.A.,
Agriculture Code ch. 142, or successor statute.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-23; Ordinance 1472, sec. 14, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-48. Sale of impounded animals; notice; disposition of proceeds.
(a) The police department may sell any animal impounded under the provisions of this article at public
auction for cash after having held such animal for at least five days and after having published notice of such
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 26/283
sale together with a general description of the animal to be sold. Such notice shall appear one time at least five
days prior to the date of the sale and shall state that such animal will be sold to defray cost if not reclaimed prior
to such date.
(b) The proceeds of any such sale shall be used to defray sale expenses and expenses of taking up and
keeping of such animal. The balance, if any, shall be paid to the owner of the animal, if known, and if such
owner if unknown, such balance shall be paid into the city treasury. Within six months after such sale, an owner
may, upon proof of such ownership satisfactory to the city's police chief, be entitled to receive the amount paid
into the city treasury because of such sale.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-24; Ordinance 1472, sec. 14, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-49. Disposition of unclaimed, unadopted or unsold impounded animal.
Any impounded animal which is:
(1) Not timely reclaimed or adopted;
(2) Found to be infected with rabies;
(3) Seriously injured; or
(4) Determined by the police chief, or designee, to be unsalable or unadoptable;
shall forthwith be destroyed. The police chief or designee shall make all decisions as to the condition, status,
and disposition of such animal.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-25; Ordinance 1472, sec. 14, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-50. Redemption of impounded animals after sale.
The owner of any animal impounded under the provisions of this article may redeem the animal by reimbursing
the purchaser for the adoption fee as well as the reasonable costs for keeping the animal as determined by the
police chief, or designee. The owner must redeem the animal within 30 days after the date of the sale;
otherwise, the animal becomes the absolute property of the purchaser. (1969 Code, sec. 4-26; Ordinance 1472,
sec. 14, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-51. Confinement of animal by owner of private premises; notice to department.
If any animal is found upon the premises of any person, the owner or occupant of the premises shall have the
right to confine such animal temporarily pending its release to the police department or to the true owner of
such animal. (1969 Code, sec. 4-27; Ordinance 1472, sec. 14, adopted 1/23/07)
Secs. 8-52—8-75. Reserved.
ARTICLE III. DOMESTIC ANIMALS
Sec. 8-76. Unlawful restraint of dogs or other domestic animals on private property.
A person may not restrain a dog or other domestic animal with a chain, rope or tether. (1969 Code, sec. 4-40;
Ordinance 1472, sec. 15, adopted 1/23/07; Ordinance 1500, sec. 3, adopted 4/15/08)
State Law reference- Unlawful restraint of dog, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code sec. 821.077.
Sec. 8-77. Impoundment when found at large.
Animal control officer is authorized to take up all domestic animals found not to be restrained by their owners
and impound such animals in the county humane society's shelter. All such animals shall be confined in a
humane manner. (1969 Code, sec. 4-41; Ordinance 1472, sec. 15, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-78. Notice of violation.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 27/283
Where the ownership of an animal found at large is known, a notice of such violation may be issued by an
animal control officer, or if a peace officer, then a citation may be issued. Upon issuance of a notice of violation,
the police department shall report the same to the municipal court and request that the violator be summoned
to appear in such court and answer to such charges. (1969 Code, sec. 4-42; Ordinance 1472, sec. 15, adopted
1/23/07)
Sec. 8-79. Notice of impoundment of tagged animals.
Upon impounding an animal found at large with current vaccination or other identifying tags, the police
department or the county humane society shall make a reasonable effort to notify the owner of such animal,
and of the conditions whereby the owner may regain custody of such animals. (1969 Code, sec. 4-43;
Ordinance 1472, sec. 15, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-80. Redemption requirements.
(a) Any animal impounded under the provisions of this article may be reclaimed by the owner upon the
payment of required impoundment fees set forth in this chapter, and based upon impoundment records
maintained by the county humane society.
(b) Any domestic or miniature animal over the age of four months which does not have a current rabies
vaccination may not be redeemed, transferred or adopted until it has been so vaccinated.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-44; Ordinance 1472, sec. 15, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-81. Disposition of animals.
(a) Unclaimed or unredeemed. After the requirements of notice as set forth in this article and the expiration of
three days, any impounded animal that is unclaimed or unredeemed shall become the property of the county
humane society. The society shall have the following powers:
(1) Authority to transfer ownership. The society may transfer ownership of any impounded animal
that is unclaimed or unredeemed. In the event of such transfer of ownership, the person or agency
to whom ownership is transferred shall pay for such animal's food and care while in the animal
shelter and shall comply with the applicable vaccination provisions.
(2) Right to destroy. The county humane society may humanely destroy any impounded animal
that is unclaimed or unredeemed.
(b) Donated, sick, unweaned or injured animals. The county humane society may destroy any animal by a
humane method if the animal is unweaned, so sick or injured that its cure is considered by the police
department or the county humane society to be impracticable or if death is imminent. In any of such events,
such destruction may be done immediately without notice of any waiting period.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-45; Ordinance 1472, sec. 15, adopted 1/23/07)
Secs. 8-82—8-105. Reserved.
ARTICLE IV. RABIES CONTROL*
Sec. 8-106. Administration; report by veterinarian.
(a) The police chief is designated as the rabies control authority of the city for the purposes of administering
the Rabies Control Act of 1981, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 826.
(b) It shall be the duty of every licensed veterinarian to report to the police department his diagnosis of any
animal observed by him as a rabies suspect.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-50; Ordinance 1472, sec. 16, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-107. Report of bite cases.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 28/283
(a) It shall be the duty of every physician or other practitioner to report to the police department the names
and addresses of persons treated for bites inflicted by animals, together with such other information as will be
helpful in rabies control.
(b) It shall be the duty of every person owning or having custody of an animal, which has bitten a human
being to report the same to the police department, and to confine it in an enclosure or to securely hold the
animal by the means of a chain or other device for observation and examination by the police department. No
person having the custody or possession of such animal shall fail, refuse, or neglect to allow an animal control
officer to make an inspection or examination of such animal for determining whether such animal has rabies.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-51; Ordinance 1472, sec. 16, adopted 1/23/07)
State Law reference- Reports of rabies, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 826.
Sec. 8-108. Quarantine regulations; pathological examination.
(a) No person may keep an animal within the city which has bitten a person or which is suspected of having
bitten a person unless the bite or suspected bite shall have been immediately reported to the police
department. A dog or cat shall after such report be securely quarantined for a period of ten days. Any other
biting animal shall be humanely killed, and its brain shall be tested for rabies. In lieu thereof the police chief
may allow the biting animal to be confined for 30 days for observation, should such confinement conform to the
regulations of the state department of health.
(b) Quarantining shall be at the following places:
(1) The county humane society's animal shelter, in which case the owner of the suspected animal
shall pay the county humane society a fee as set forth in this chapter.
(2) A licensed veterinary hospital at the expense of the owner, upon the owner's request.
(3) Home quarantine where all of the following requirements are met:
a. The animal owner is a resident of the city and has a facility in the city limits to provide
absolute security and isolation for the animal. If the owner of a biting animal fails to keep the
animal so confined, an offense shall have been committed;
b. The owner of the biting animal agrees that he will have the animal inspected by a licensed
veterinarian on the first day of isolation and on the day immediately following the ten-day
isolation period. The owner further agrees to furnish the police department with a certificate of
health showing the animal to be free of rabies. If the owner of the biting animal fails to have the
animal inspected on the first day of and on the day immediately following this ten-day
observation period as required, an offense shall have been committed;
c. The biting animal was currently vaccinated and was not at large at the time of the bite;
d. If an animal dies while in home quarantine, the police department shall be notified
immediately, and the animal will be surrendered to the department for testing; and
e. Failure to comply with the home observation requirements shall constitute an offense.
(4) An animal of unknown ownership will be quarantined at the county humane society's animal
shelter.
(c) Upon the demand made by the police department, it shall be unlawful for the owner to fail to surrender
any animal which has bitten a human or another animal, or which is suspected of having been exposed to
rabies, for quarantine, which expense shall be borne by the owner.
(d) The quarantined animal may be reclaimed by the owner if adjudged free of rabies, upon payment of the
fees set forth in this chapter and upon compliance with the vaccination provisions of this chapter.
(e) When an animal under quarantine, diagnosed by a licensed veterinarian as being rabid or suspected of
being rabid, dies while under observation, the police department shall immediately send the head of such
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 29/283
animal to the state health department for pathological examination. The police department shall notify the
proper public health officer of reports of human contacts and the diagnosis made of the suspected animal after
the pathological examination has been made.
(f) Any unvaccinated animal bitten by another animal suspected of or known to be rabid shall be immediately
destroyed or shall be surrendered to the police department for a period of three months' quarantine, and shall
be vaccinated during the third and eighth week of quarantine. Any vaccinated animal bitten by another animal
suspected of being or known to be rabid shall be immediately vaccinated and surrendered to the police
department for a period of 45 days' quarantine. When the biting animal is determined not to be rabid, the bitten
animal shall be released. All animals quarantined shall be at the owner's expense. Upon surrender of an animal
for quarantine, the owner shall be required to pay in advance one month's quarantine fee to defray a portion of
the expense of care and feeding of the animal. Additional quarantine expenses shall be paid at the beginning of
each subsequent month's quarantine. If an owner fails to pay for any expense of quarantine when due, the
animal shall become the property of the city and shall be subject to immediate disposal. The police chief is
authorized to permit the quarantine of a bitten animal at a licensed veterinary clinic for the necessary
quarantine period at the owner's option and expense.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-52; Ordinance 1472, sec. 16, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-109. Citywide quarantine.
(a) Conditions warranting; period. A citywide quarantine may be invoked for a period of 30 days by the city
commission upon the recommendation of the police department after it has been notified by the state health
department of a positive diagnosis of rabies of an animal or after an investigation it has determined there exists
an immediate threat of rabies.
(b) Extending time. If there are additional positive cases of rabies occurring during the 30-day period of the
citywide quarantine, such period of quarantine may be extended for an additional reasonable period of time.
(c) Animals bitten by rabid animals. During such period of citywide rabies quarantine, every animal bitten by
an animal suspected of being rabid shall be quarantined for six months as provided in this chapter at the
owner's expense. The expense shall be paid at the end of each month's quarantine or the animal shall become
the property of the city and shall be forthwith disposed of.
(d) Animals in public. It shall be unlawful for any person to take or permit any animal in the streets or any
other public place during the period of quarantine.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-53; Ordinance 1472, sec. 16, adopted 1/23/07)
Sec. 8-110. Unauthorized killing of suspected animals; surrender to city.
(a) It shall be unlawful for any person to kill, or cause to be killed, any rabid animal, any animal suspected of
having been exposed to rabies or any animal which has bitten a human or is suspected to have bitten a human,
except as provided in this article, nor to remove same from the city limits without written permission from the
police department.
(b) The carcass of any dead animal suspected of having been exposed to rabies shall, upon demand, be
surrendered to the police department.
(c) The police department shall direct the disposition of any animal found to be infected with rabies.
(d) It shall be unlawful for any person to fail or refuse to surrender any animal for quarantine, destruction or
disposal as required herein when demand is made therefore by the police department.
(1969 Code, sec. 4-54; Ordinance 1472, sec. 16, adopted 1/23/07)
Secs. 8-111—8-133. Reserved.

Sec. 8-134. Penalty for violation.

civil action or penal charge available under state law or other remedies provided by law or equity. (1969 Code,

CHAPTER 10
BUILDINGS*
ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL
Sec. 10-1. Fire limits.
The fire limits of the city are declared to be as follows:
Beginning at the alley in block 11, OT Addition where it intersects Marshall Street; thence east with Marshall
Street to its intersection with Fannin Street; thence south on Fannin Street to its intersection with Paradise
Street; thence east on Paradise Street to its intersection with the alley in block 30, OT Addition; thence north
with said alley line to its intersection with Marshall Street; thence east on Marshall Street to the Southeast
corner of block 14, OT Addition, corner of Marshall and Mesquite Streets; thence north along Mesquite Street to
its intersection with East Texas Street; thence west on Texas Street to the alley in block 5, OT Addition; thence
north along said alley to Olive Street; thence west on Olive Street to Cumberland Street; thence north on
Cumberland Street to Wanderers Street; thence west on Wanderers Street to the alley in block 65, OT addition;
thence north along said alley to Harrold Street; thence west on Harrold Street to the alley in block 18, North
Addition; thence south along said alley to Dawson Street; thence west on Dawson Street to the alley in block
67, OT Addition; thence south with said alley to the point of beginning.
(1969 Code, sec. 6-1; Ordinance 441, sec. 1, adopted 4/20/27)
Sec. 10-2. Building code adopted; penalty.
(a) There is hereby adopted a building code known as the International Building Code, with the most current
published edition. Such code is published in book form and is to be maintained in the community development
director's office and is referred to, incorporated herein, and made a part hereof for all purposes. Provided,
however, that in the event any conflict may arise between the provisions of the code adopted by the provisions
of this article and any other applicable provisions of this Code, state law, or city ordinance, rule, or regulation,
the provisions of this Code, state law, or city ordinance, rule, or regulation shall prevail and be controlling.
(b) Any person violating the provisions of said building code shall be punished as provided in section 1-6.
(1969 Code, sec. 6-2; Ordinance 1364, sec. 1, adopted 3/6/01)
Sec. 10-3. Construction in fire limits.
Construction in the fire limits, Ordinance No. 441 (adopted 4/20/27), is hereby amended in its entirety and the
appendix of the International Building Code, latest published edition, is hereby adopted.
Sec. 10-4. International Existing Building Code adopted.
(a) There is hereby adopted an existing building code known as the International Existing Building Code, with
the most current published edition. Such code is published in book form and is to be maintained in the
community development director's office and is referred to, in corporate herein, and made a part hereof for all
purposes. The International Existing Building Code regulates and governs the repair, alteration, change of
occupancy, addition and relocation of existing buildings, including historic buildings within the city.
(b) The following sections of the International Existing Building Code are hereby revised:
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 31/283
Section 101.1 Insert: City of Vernon
Section 1301.2 Insert: 1927
(Ordinance 1577, secs. 1, 2, adopted 12/20/11)
Sec. 10-5. Exterior masonry construction requirements.
(a) Definitions.
Masonry means the form of construction composed of stone, brick, brick veneer, concrete, hollow clay tile,
decorative concrete block or tile, glass block or other similar building units or materials or a combination of
these materials laid up unit by unit and set in mortar. For the purposes of this definition, stucco is not
considered masonry. Synthetic products (e.g., EIFS - exterior insulation and finish systems, hardi plank, or
other materials of similar characteristics) shall not be considered a masonry material.
(b) Exterior masonry construction requirements. Buildings requiring masonry on all sides: All buildings
constructed on property zoned CBD (Central Business District) under the city's comprehensive zoning
ordinance shall have all exterior walls constructed using a masonry material covering at least 80 percent of said
walls, exclusive of all windows, doors, roofs, glass construction materials, or sidewalk and walk-way covers.
(c) Nonconforming buildings. Where a lawful building exists at the effective date of adoption or amendment of
this section and said building could not be built under the terms of this section, it may continue so long as it
remains lawful, subject to the following provisions:
(1) Such building may not be enlarged in a way which increases its nonconformity unless the
enlargement is in conformity with the provisions of this section;
(2) The exterior walls of such building may not be modified, altered, or enlarged in a way which
increases its nonconformity unless the modification, alteration, or enlargement is in conformity with
the provisions of this section;
(3) Should such building be destroyed by any means to an extent of more than 50 percent of its
replacement cost at the time of destruction, it shall not be reconstructed except in conformity with
the provisions of this section;
(4) Should such building be moved for any reason for any distance whatever, it shall thereafter
conform to the regulations of the district in which it is located after it is moved.
(Ordinance 1579, sec. 1, adopted 12/20/11)
Secs. 10-6—10-9. Reserved.
Sec. 10-10. Construction board of appeals (CBOA).
(a) Board creation and establishment. There is hereby created a construction board of appeals for the city.
(b) Board members and term. The construction board of appeals shall consist of five regular members and
two alternates that reside or maintain a business within the city limits selected as follows:
(1) One building contractor;
(2) One master electrician;
(3) One master plumber;
(4) One fire/explosives expert;
(5) One utility representative;
(6) Alternate 1: Tradesperson;
(7) Alternate 2: Vernon citizen.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 32/283
The city commission shall appoint members of the construction board of appeals. It is the declared policy of the
city commission that it will consider and appoint only those persons who have demonstrated their civic interest,
general knowledge of the community, independent judgment, and availability to prepare for and attend
meetings. The members of the board shall regularly attend meetings of the board and shall serve without
compensation.
Appointees to the construction board of appeals shall serve until replaced by the city commission.
(c) Board duties and responsibilities. The construction board of appeals shall hear appeals on decisions by
the fire marshal, fire chief, and building official as they concern the fire, building, electrical, mechanical and
plumbing codes adopted by the city; determine the suitability of alternate materials and alternate types of
construction; establish licensing regulations; establish fee schedules; and interpret the fire, building, electrical,
mechanical and plumbing codes adopted by the city.
(d) Meetings and quorum. Meetings of the construction board of appeals shall be scheduled as required.
Four of the members (members and/or alternates) shall constitute a quorum for the conduct of business.
(e) Requests for board considerations. Any person who desires to schedule any item before the construction
board of appeals shall submit a written request to the fire marshal, fire chief, or building official. Appeals of
decisions of the fire marshal, fire chief, or building official shall also include a $50.00 application fee. Such
request shall include justification for the action requested of the board.
An application for appeal shall be based on a claim that the true intent of the code or the rules legally adopted
thereunder have been incorrectly interpreted, the provisions of the adopted code do not fully apply or an equally
good or better form of construction is proposed. The board shall have no authority to waive requirements of the
adopted code.
(f) Appeals of decisions of the construction board of appeals. Any person who is dissatisfied with a decision
of the construction board of appeals may appeal to the city commission within ten days from the date of
notification of the board's ruling by filing a written request with the city secretary that the appeal be heard by the
city commission.
Upon appeal the fire marshal, fire chief, or building official shall transmit to the city commission all papers for
the record of the appealed action. The city secretary shall thereupon fix a time for a hearing before the city
commission and shall notify those known to be interested. The decision of the city commission concerning the
appeal shall be final.
(Ordinance 1578, sec. 1, adopted 12/20/11)
Secs. 10-11—10-22. Reserved.
ARTICLE II. ABATEMENT OF DILAPIDATED, SUBSTANDARD STRUCTURES*
Sec. 10-23. Order to remove; city's remedy on default.
(a) Whenever in the opinion of the city commission any building, fence, shed, awning, or any other
improvement of any kind, or any part thereof, is likely to collapse and endanger persons or property or is an
otherwise dangerous structure, the city commission may order the owner, agent, or occupant of the dangerous
structure or the premises on which it stands or to which it is attached to take down and remove the same or any
part hereof within ten days after notice is served or published as directed by order of the city commission.
(b) If the owner, agent or occupant shall fail or refuse to remove the same after notice is served or published,
the city commission shall have the power to remove the same at the expense of the city and assess the
expenses on the land on which it stood or to which it was attached in such manner as may be directed by the
order of the city commission.
(c) All buildings or structures which are:
(1) Structurally unsafe;
(2) Not provided with adequate egress;
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 33/283
(3) Constitute a fire hazard; or
(4) Otherwise dangerous to human life, or which by way of existing use, constitute a hazard to
safety, health or public welfare by reason of inadequate maintenance or dilapidation or
obsolescence or fire hazard or abandonment;
are hereby declared to be public nuisances and shall be abated by repair, rehabilitation, demolition or removal
in accordance with the procedure specified in this article.
(1969 Code, sec. 6-21; Ordinance 1302, sec. II(A), adopted 2/25/97)
Sec. 10-24. Notice; service.
(a) The community development director shall examine or cause to be examined every building or structure
or portion thereof reported as dangerous, damaged or unsafe and, if such is found to be unsafe and, if such is
found to be unsafe or dangerous, the community development director shall give the owner of such building or
structure written notice stating the defects found to exist.
(b) The notice from the community development director shall require the owner or person in charge of the
building or premises to obtain the proper permit and commence the required repairs, improvements or
demolition and removal of the building or structure or portions thereof within 15 days from the date such notice
is received by the owner or person in charge of such building or premises. Such notice may also require the
building, structure or portion thereof to be vacated forthwith and not occupied until the required repairs and
improvements are completed, inspected and approved by the community development director.
(c) Service of notice may be by certified mail or personal service.
(d) The community development director shall cause to be posted at each entrance at any building ordered
to be vacated, a notice to read:
“Danger-This building is deemed unsafe for human occupancy.”
Such notice shall not be removed without written permission of the community development director, except for
the purpose of making the required repairs or demolishing the building.
(e) In case the owner shall fail, neglect or refuse to comply with the notice to repair, rehabilitate or to
demolish the building or structure or portion thereof, the community development director may proceed to
prosecute the owner or person in charge of the building or structure as a violator of this article.
(f) In case the owner shall fail, neglect, or refuse to comply with the notice to repair, rehabilitate or to
demolish and remove the building or structure or portion thereof, the community development director shall
notify the city commission of such fact. The city commission may order the community development director to
proceed with the work specified in such notice, or order such building or structure demolished or removed and
may cause the cost of such work to be levied as a special assessment against the property. The decision shall
be made at a public hearing before the city commission.
(g) Notice shall be given to the owner or person in charge of such building or structure of the public hearing
before the city commission and the order directing the community development director to proceed with the
work and assessing the cost thereof against the property.
(h) Notice of the public hearing to be held before the city commission shall be given by causing a notice of
such hearing to be mailed at least ten days before the date of such hearing to the owner, agent, or occupant of
the dangerous building or structure at his last known address and by publication of a notice of such hearing at
least one time in a newspaper of general circulation of the city prior to the date of such hearing.
(i) If the owner, agent or occupant of the dangerous building or structure or of the premises on which it stands
shall appear before the city commission at such hearing, no further notice shall be required, but if he fails to
appear, the notice of the order of the city commission made at such hearing shall be delivered by mailing a
copy of such order to the owner, agent, or occupant of the dangerous building or structure or the premises on
which it stands at his last known address by certified mail and by publication of a copy of such order at least
one time in a newspaper of general circulation of the city.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 34/283
(1969 Code, sec. 6-22; Ordinance 1302, sec. II(B), adopted 2/25/97)
Sec. 10-25. Procedure after service of notice.
Upon the expiration of ten days from the date of service of the order of the city commission upon the owner or
person in charge of a dangerous structure and the publication thereof as required herein, the community
development director shall proceed with the work specified in the order of the city commission. (1969 Code,
sec. 6-23; Ordinance 1302, sec. II(C), adopted 2/25/97)
Sec. 10-26. Default of owner.
If the owner, agent or occupant of the premises shall fail or refuse to pay or discharge the expenses as
determined by this article after a period of 30 days, then the city shall file a lien, which shall bear interest at the
rate of ten percent per annum, against such property in the county deed of records. In no case shall the city
foreclose such lien by forced sale. (1969 Code, sec. 6-24; Ordinance 1302, sec. II(D), adopted 2/25/97;
Ordinance 1479, sec. 1, adopted 5/22/07)
Sec. 10-27. Charges after abatement by city.
Any residential property as defined by the city zoning ordinance specified in appendix A to this Code, the
owner, agent, or occupant of such premises at the minimum, at the discretion of the community development
director, shall be invoiced for the solid waste charges incurred by the city in abating the said dilapidated and
substandard structure. Any commercial property as defined by the city zoning ordinance, the owner, agent, or
occupant of such premises at the minimum, at the discretion of the community development director, shall be
invoiced for the solid waste charges, equipment usage and manpower incurred by the city in abating the said
dilapidated and substandard structure. (1969 Code, sec. 6-25; Ordinance 1475, sec. 1, adopted 3/27/07)
Sec. 10-28. Administrative charges after abatement by city.
A $25.00 administrative fee shall be invoiced to any (residential or commercial) property owner after the city
abates a dilapidated and substandard structure. (1969 Code, sec. 6-26; Ordinance 1479, sec. 2, adopted
5/22/07)
Secs. 10-29—10-59. Reserved.
ARTICLE III. ZONING, SUBDIVISION AND BUILDING PERMIT AND INSPECTION FEES
Sec. 10-60. Zoning change application fee.
Any person applying for a change in the zoning district classification of any property or a specific use permit, or
a planned unit development permit, shall be required to pay an application processing fee of $100.00 at the
time of the filing of an application. In the event the application is withdrawn prior to the mailing of the required
written notification or publication in the local newspaper, the fee shall be refunded. (1969 Code, sec. 6-41;
Ordinance 1087, sec. 1, adopted 3/28/95)
Sec. 10-61. Subdivision regulation inspection fees.
(a) Inspection. The community development director (director) shall provide for inspection of required
improvements during construction and ensure satisfactory completion. The applicant shall pay to the city an
inspection fee of two percent of the amount of the performance bond or the estimated cost of required
improvements, and the subdivision plat shall not be signed by the chairperson of the planning and zoning
commission unless such fee has been paid at the time of application. These fees shall be due and payable
upon demand of the city and no building permits or certificates of occupancy shall be issued until all fees are
paid. If the city engineer finds upon inspection that any of the required improvements have not been
constructed in accordance with the city's construction standards and specifications, the applicant shall be
responsible for completing the improvements. Whenever the cost of improvements is covered by a performance
bond, the applicant and bonding company shall be severally and jointly liable for the improvements according to
specifications.
(b) Certificate of satisfactory completion. The following applies to the certificate of satisfactory completion:
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 35/283
(1) The city will not accept dedication of required improvements nor release nor reduce a
performance bond, until the city's engineer has submitted a certificate stating that all required
improvements have been satisfactorily completed and until the applicant's engineer or surveyor has
certified to the city engineer, through submission of the detailed as-built survey plat of the
subdivision, indicating location, dimension, materials, and other information required by the planning
and zoning commission or city engineer, that the layout of the line and grade of all public
improvements are in accordance with the construction plans for the subdivision and that a title
insurance policy has been furnished to and approved by the city attorney indicating that the
improvements shall have been completed, are ready for dedication to the city and are free and clear
of any and all liens and encumbrances. Upon such approval and recommendation, the city
commission shall thereafter accept the improvements for dedication in accordance with the
established procedure.
(2) A performance bond shall be reduced upon actual dedication of public improvements and then
only to the ratio that the public improvements dedicated bear to the total public improvements for the
plat. In no event shall a performance bond be reduced below 25 percent of the principal amount.
(c) Acceptance of escrow funds. The following applies to escrow funds:
(1) Whenever, by reason of the season of the year, any lot improvements required by the
subdivision regulations cannot be performed, the director may issue a certificate of occupancy,
provided there is no danger to health, safety, or general welfare upon accepting a cash escrow
deposit in an amount to be determined by the city engineer for the cost of said improvements. The
performance bond covering such lot improvements shall remain in full force and effect.
(2) Procedures on escrow fund are as follows:
a. All required improvements for which escrow monies have been accepted by the director at
the time of issuance of a certificate of occupancy shall be installed by the developer within a
period of 12 months from the date of deposit and issuance of the certificate of occupancy. In
the event that the improvements have not been properly installed, at the end of the time
period, the director shall give two weeks written notice to the developer requiring him to
properly install same. If not properly installed, the director may request the city commission to
authorize the city to proceed to contract out the work for the installation of the necessary
improvements in a sum not to exceed the amount of the escrow deposit.
b. At the time of the issuance of the certificate of occupancy for which escrow monies are
being deposited with the director, the applicant shall obtain and file with the director prior to
obtaining the certificate of occupancy a notarized statement from the purchaser of the
premises authorizing the director to install the improvements at the end of the 12-month period
in the event that the same have not been duly installed by the developer.
(d) Sketch plan application fee. Sketch plans shall be accompanied by a fee of $10.00 per lot.
(e) Preliminary plat. Preliminary plats shall require a fee of $10.00 per lot.
(f) Final plat. Applicant shall file a fee of $15.00 per lot for final approval, together with an additional fee of
$12.00 per lot for reproduction of plans.
(1969 Code, sec. 6-42; Ordinance 1087, sec. 2(B)-2(F), adopted 3/28/95)

Sec. 10-63. Electrical permit fees.
The electrical permit fees are as follows:
(1) Minimum permit: $10.00 for the first 20 openings and $0.05 thereafter.

(1) Residential: $10.00.

ARTICLE IV. MECHANICAL
Sec. 10-87. Mechanical code adopted; penalty.
(a) There is hereby adopted a mechanical code known as the International Mechanical Code, with the most
current published edition. Such code is published in book form and is to be maintained in the community
development director's office and is referred to, incorporated herein, and made a part hereof for all purposes.
Provided, however, that in the event any conflict may arise between the provisions of the code adopted by the
provisions of this article and any other applicable provisions of this Code, state law, or city ordinance, rule or
regulation, the provisions of this Code, state law or city ordinance, rule or regulation shall prevail and be
controlling.
(b) Any person violating the provisions of said mechanical code shall be punished as provided in section 1-6.
(1969 Code, sec. 6-60; Ordinance 1364, sec. 2, adopted 3/6/01)

ARTICLE II. PERPETUAL CARE*
DIVISION 1. GENERALLY
Sec. 12-25. City authorized as trustee.
The city, owning and operating a cemetery known as East View Cemetery, is authorized to act as a permanent
trustee for the perpetual care and upkeep of lots and graves in such burial grounds and is authorized to accept
such trust as herein provided and the same shall become perpetual. (1969 Code, sec. 7-15; Ordinance 653,
sec. 1, adopted 5/10/60)
State Law reference- Municipal cemetery authorized, Health and Safety Code sec. 713.001.
Sec. 12-26. Successor to trustee.
In any event should the city, after having entered into and accepted such trust herein provided for, renounce
said trust or fail or refuse to act further as such trustee, as herein provided for, then the district judge or highest
trial judge of the county shall appoint a suitable successor to such trustee who shall faithfully execute the trust
as herein provided for. (1969 Code, sec. 7-16; Ordinance 653, sec. 7, adopted 5/10/60)
Sec. 12-27. Accepting gifts, donations, or sales proceeds.
The city is authorized to accept by gift, donation, or sales proceeds for general improvements to East View
Cemetery. A $1.75 per square foot on the size of the grave space sold or 15 percent of the proceeds from the
sale price of any grave space, whichever is greater, shall be allocated to the perpetual care fund. All monies
received as designated in this section, shall be so deposited in said perpetual care fund. (1969 Code, sec. 7-17;
Ordinance 653, sec. 2, adopted 5/10/60; Ordinance 1391, sec. 2, adopted 6/25/02; Ordinance 1416, sec. 1,
adopted 9/9/03)
Sec. 12-28. Use of money advanced.
The city is invested with the power and authority and it shall be its duty to invest and reinvest all funds
advanced to it for the purposes herein set forth in interest bearing bonds or securities of a municipality, state, or
federal government or its agencies. Any normal operating maintenance expense of the cemetery shall be
eligible for use by these funds. However, only the use of the accrued interest shall be utilized and not any
principal of the said trust fund. (1969 Code, sec. 7-19; Ordinance 653, sec. 4, adopted 5/10/60; Ordinance
1391, sec. 4, adopted 6/25/02)
Sec. 12-29. Private beautification and care permitted; donations for existing graves.
None of the rights, powers, and duties herein provided for shall deprive any person having any interest in a
grave or burial lot, or kinship within the third degree by affinity or consanguinity to those therein interred, from
beautifying or caring for the same individually or at his own expense under the reasonable rules and regulations
the city may provide; however, watering of any grave space shall not be allowed in any area that has not been
deemed as a special care area; and all persons who now have kinship with or are otherwise interested in
persons interred therein may make donations to the city for the perpetual care fund. (1969 Code, sec. 7-21;
Ordinance 653, sec. 6, adopted 5/10/60; Ordinance 1391, sec. 6, adopted 6/25/02)
Secs. 12-30-12-46. Reserved.

DIVISION 2. RULES AND REGULATIONS
Sec. 12-47. Definitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in
this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:
Deed or certificate of ownership refers to any instrument conveying right of interment in East View Cemetery.
Superintendent includes any employee of the city who may, in the absence of the superintendent, be acting for
him.
(1969 Code, sec. 7-31; Ordinance 1105, secs. 1, 2, adopted 9/23/85)
Sec. 12-48. Applicability.
All interments, disinterments and removals in East View Cemetery shall be subject to these rules and
regulations and all other orders and laws of the properly constituted authorities of the city, county, state, or
federal government. (1969 Code, sec. 7-32; Ordinance 1105, sec. 3, adopted 9/23/85)
Sec. 12-49. Prior notice required; permitted interment.
(a) At least six working hours' notice shall be given to the superintendent prior to any interment and at least
one week's notice prior to any disinterment or removal.
(b) No interment of any body other than that of a human being shall be permitted in the cemetery.
(1969 Code, sec. 7-33; Ordinance 1105, secs. 4, 5, adopted 9/23/85)
Sec. 12-50. Time of payment for cemetery services.
All fees or proceeds from sale of grave spaces shall be paid in advance before any services or interments are
allowed. The only exceptions are for cemetery services rendered to any funeral home that is located in the city
or to the county for indigents. (1969 Code, sec. 7-34; Ordinance 1105, sec. 6, adopted 9/23/85; Ordinance
1391, sec. 7, adopted 6/25/02)
Sec. 12-51. Validity of grave space transfers, assignments.
No transfer or assignment of any grave space or interest therein shall be valid until recorded in the cemetery
records in the office of the city secretary. (1969 Code, sec. 7-35; Ordinance 1105, sec. 7, adopted 9/23/85)
Sec. 12-52. Setting of memorials and markers.
Memorials or markers must be set on suitable foundations and the setting thereof supervised by the
superintendent. (1969 Code, sec. 7-36; Ordinance 1105, sec. 8, adopted 9/23/85)
Sec. 12-53. Hours of operation.
East View Cemetery shall be open to visitors during the hours between sunrise and sunset during the entire
year. (1969 Code, sec. 7-37; Ordinance 1105, sec. 9, adopted 9/23/85)
Sec. 12-54. Removal of flowers, etc., and debris.
(a) After a period of deterioration municipal employees shall remove all flowers, ornaments and decorations.
(b) Grave space owners or their agents or employees when caring for cemetery property, must not leave any
weeds, refuse, or debris of any kind on their property, streets, or alleyways. All debris must be disposed of in a
proper container at the cemetery or removed from the cemetery grounds.
(1969 Code, sec. 7-38; Ordinance 1105, secs. 10, 11, adopted 9/23/85; Ordinance 1391, sec. 8, adopted
6/25/02)
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 40/283
Sec. 12-55. Special and nonspecial care areas designation.
(a) Property in East View Cemetery that is designated as special care areas shall be maintained with a
certain level of maintenance that includes routine irrigation watering, as local law may allow; routine mowing of
grasses; and other routine maintenance items that are determined prudent and necessary by city
administration. The following property shall be developed exclusively as special care areas: the entire blocks of
21, 22 and 23.
(b) All other property in East View Cemetery shall be designated as nonspecial care areas. The nonspecial
care areas shall be maintained with a lesser level of care that does not include in the providing of water for
landscape irrigation purposes, except for burial lots that have been converted to perpetual care as prescribed
by previous policies and as local law may allow. A burial lot owner or family member shall make the request for
landscape irrigation water and when the superintendent receives such a request he shall respond in a timely
fashion to provide such water service. All irrigation water shall be used in a conservative-like fashion; and if
abuses occur, then the superintendent may terminate the usage of irrigation water to the burial lot where the
abuse is occurring. Other maintenance items include routine mowing of grasses and various maintenance items
that are deemed prudent and necessary by city administration shall be performed.
(c) The regulations listed in subsections (a) and (b) of this section supersedes all other rules or regulations
that have been adopted by previous city commissions in defining the level of care to be provided at East View
Cemetery.
(1969 Code, sec. 7-39; Ordinance 1105, sec. 12, adopted 9/23/85; Ordinance 1391, sec. 9, adopted 6/25/02;
Ordinance 1401, sec. 1, adopted 10/22/02)
Sec. 12-56. Construction of memorials and head markers.
All family memorials and head markers in blocks 21 and 22 shall be constructed only of bronze, granite, or
marble; and no more than one family memorial shall be permitted on any lot. Each and every memorial or
marker shall be set on a foundation installed at the owner's expense and under the supervision of the
superintendent and shall be set flush with the lawn and follow the contour of the particular section in which the
same is located. Families buying six spaces or more, in a row, that have by prior pattern been established with
laydown markers, may erect one family upright memorial not to exceed 24 inches in height above ground level.
The family memorial shall be set in a straight line with the rest of the markers. Upright memorials are permitted
in blocks 21, 22 and 23 only on designated rows which have by prior history had upright memorials. (1969
Code, sec. 7-40; Ordinance 1105, sec. 13, adopted 9/23/85; Ordinance 1131 adopted 10/14/86)
Sec. 12-57. Grave space prices; fees.
(a) The prices for lot or grave spaces sold in a special care area are as follows:
(1) Upright monument grave space: $700.00.
(2) Flat monument grave space: $650.00.
(b) The price for lot or grave spaces sold in a nonspecial care area is $450.00. Grave space in a nonspecial
care area for persons classified by the county as an indigent is $50.00.
(c) All interments shall utilize municipal services for opening and closing graves. The following fees shall be
collected for the opening and closing of graves:
(1) Normal workday with closing before 5:00 p.m.: $500.00.
(2) Normal workday with closing after 5:00 p.m.: $600.00.
(3) Saturday or holiday: $700.00.
(4) Persons classified by the county as indigent: $50.00.
(d) All funerals shall utilize municipal services for awning, setup and lowering of the casket. The following
fees shall be collected for this service:

(1) Normal workday with closing before 5:00 p.m.: $200.00.
(2) Normal workday with closing after 5:00 p.m.: $240.00.
(3) Saturday or holiday: $240.00.
(4) Persons classified by the county as indigent: No charge.
(e) Any person requesting a disinterment shall be charged a fee based on actual cost that includes labor and
equipment charges.
(1969 Code, sec. 7-41; Ordinance 1105, sec. 14, adopted 9/23/85; Ordinance 1277 adopted 9/20/95;

The city is hereby authorized to remove items such as trees, shrubbery, curbing or coping if the owner or
relatives of the decedents request such removal. The expense of removal for such items shall be borne entirely
by the requestor. The cost for such service shall be based on current rates for labor and equipment charged by
