CHAPTER 16
ELECTRICAL CODE*
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 42/283
ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL
Sec. 16-1. Definitions.
For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply:
Accessible in an attic means a distance of not less than 30 inches shall exist from the top of the ceiling joists to
the bottom of the roof joists or rafters at the highest point.
Apprentice electrician means one who assists a master or a journeyman electrician in installations and who
works under the constant supervision of a master or a journeyman electrician.
Board means a quorum of the board of electrical examiners.
Building means any building or structure, including a residence.
Commercial means anything other than residential.
Commission means the city commission of the City of Vernon, Texas.
Fixture means a unit which supports a means of illumination.
Holiday means a holiday which is established by the personnel rules of the city.
Homeowner means a person owning and living in (or who will live in, if the building is under construction) a
single-unit dwelling.
Installation means all electrical work of any nature performed on, or in, a consumer's premises.
Journeyman electrician means one skilled and experienced in the physical labor involved in electrical
installations, and who does, or holds himself out as intending to do, electrical installations under the
employment and supervision of a master electrician.
Maintenance electrician means one who is employed by one employer to maintain and to repair existing
electrical installations in a designated building under one ownership and who does not otherwise engage
himself as either a master, journeyman, or apprentice electrician.
Master electrician means a person who, himself being highly skilled in methods and practices of electrical
installations, proposes to do installations and to enter into agreements or contracts for such installations.
National Electrical Code means the current edition of the National Electrical Code, adopted by the city.
Opening means the location where a ceiling light is to be mounted; also a convenience outlet or a switch.
Person means a master electrician, a journeyman electrician, an apprentice electrician, a maintenance
electrician, a firm, a partnership, a corporation, any other type of organization, any individual and the plural of
any or all of these as well as the singular.
Secretary means the secretary of the board of electrical examiners, of the duly appointed electrical inspector, or
of a duly appointed assistant electrical inspector who has been specifically appointed by the electrical inspector
to serve in his absence.
(1969 Code, sec. 10-1; Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Sec. 16-2. Exemptions-City and state departments and electric utility companies.
The provisions of this chapter shall not apply to installations maintained by the electrical department of the city,
by the state highway department or by an electric public utility company. (1969 Code, sec. 10-2; Ordinance
1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Sec. 16-3. Same-Other utility companies as to own property.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 43/283
The provisions of this chapter shall not apply to electric light, heat, and power companies, or telephone and
telegraph companies operating under the franchise of state or federal laws in the installation, maintenance,
removal, or repair of wires or other equipment used in connection with the business or plants. (1969 Code, sec.
10-3; Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Sec. 16-4. Manufacturer's research; limitation.
Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to prohibit manufacturers of electrical apparatus or equipment from
carrying on reasonable electrical experiments with materials and products within the confines of their own
premises and all installations therein; provided, further, that the electrical inspector may require the
manufacture to make whatever changes he believes necessary for the protection of public life, welfare, and
property. (1969 Code, sec. 10-4; Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Sec. 16-5. Penalties; license revocation for two or more violations.
(a) Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall, upon conviction, be fined as provided in
section 1-6. Each day a violation shall continue shall constitute a separate offense.
(b) In addition to any penalty authorized, two or more violations of this chapter by any person holding a
license hereunder shall be grounds for revocation of such license. Upon complaint being made to the city
commission of two or more violations by a license holder, the commission shall set the matter of revocation of
the license down for a hearing and shall give the licensee at least ten days' notice by registered mail of such
hearing. Said hearing will be public and the licensee shall be entitled to be heard in person or by his attorney.
After full hearing the commission shall determine whether such license should be revoked.
(1969 Code, sec. 10-6; Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Sec. 16-6. Work in progress.
Installations contracted for before the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived shall be
governed by the electrical ordinance effective at that time or by the ordinance herein enacted, at the option of
the electrical contractor; provided the electrical contractor advises the electrical inspector in writing within 30
days after the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived of such contract and the
manner in which it conflicts with this chapter but is applicable to prior electrical ordinances and secures written
acknowledgement of the electrical inspector. (1969 Code, sec. 10-7; Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Secs. 16-7—16-34. Reserved.
ARTICLE II. ADMINISTRATIVE
DIVISION 1. GENERALLY
Sec. 16-35. Electrical inspector's office-Created; appointment of personnel.
There is created the office of electrical inspector of the city. The city manager shall appoint the electrical
inspector and such other assistants as he shall deem proper. (1969 Code, sec. 10-17; Ordinance 1248 adopted
11/17/93)
Sec. 16-36. Same-Personnel qualifications; additional duties as prescribed.
The electrical inspector and his assistants shall be persons having adequate knowledge of current and
approved methods and practices relating to the electrical installations. In addition to the duties set forth, the
electrical inspector and his assistants shall perform such other functions and duties as the city manager may,
from time to time, direct. (1969 Code, sec. 10-18; Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Sec. 16-37. Same-Duties and powers.
The electrical inspector shall have the following duties:
(1) Inspect all installations, alterations and repairs of electrical work in consumer installations as
set out in this chapter. He shall make such inspection within 24 hours after application therefor
(Saturdays, Sundays and holidays, recognized by the city, excluded). For an approved installation,
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 44/283
he shall attach a green tag or card; for a disapproved installation, he shall attach a red tag or card.
To remove, deface, damage or mutilate a tag or card which the electrical inspector has attached to
an installation shall constitute an offense against the city.
(2) Upon determining that unsafe, improper or unlawful consumer installations exist, immediately
notify the owner of said premises, or his agent and the electrician performing the work on said
premises, in writing, specifying the exact deficiency existing, and shall allow said parties a
reasonable time, as determined by the electrical inspector, to correct said deficiency. If corrective
action is not begun immediately or the deficiency is not corrected within a prescribed time, and if he
believes public welfare endangered, the electrical inspector shall order the electrical supply to the
premises discontinued. A written record of such orders shall be kept in the office of the electrical
inspector.
(3) As far as may be necessary for the performance of his duties, have the right to enter any
consumer's premises at all reasonable hours for the purpose of making any test or inspections of the
electrical wiring, appliances, or equipment contained therein. When on duty the electrical inspector
shall wear a badge clearly identifying his official capacity.
(4) Keep, or cause to be kept, a written record of all permits, licenses and inspections which are
required under this chapter. He shall also keep a written record of all condemnations and
disconnects of electrical installations resulting from condemnations.
(5) The electrical inspector shall stop the installation, alteration, operation or repair of any
electrical work on or in any consumer's premises when, in the inspector's opinion, the work is being
done in a reckless, careless or unsafe manner or in a manner which violates the provisions of this
chapter.
(6) Upon determining that particular work should stop, post notices to that effect on the
consumer's premises and thereafter no person shall proceed with the installation until the electrical
inspector has canceled the stop work notice. The posting of a red tag or card on the premises shall
constitute a stop work notice. It shall be a violation of this chapter to remove, deface or damage or
mutilate the stop work notice.
(1969 Code, sec. 10-19; Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Sec. 16-38. Same-Not eligible for examination during term.
No person serving as electrical inspector shall be permitted to take the examination for a master electrician's
license during his term of office. (1969 Code, sec. 10-20; Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Sec. 16-39. Same-Conflict of interest.
No electrical inspector may have any interest in any electrical company nor shall he do any electrical work for
any private party or any company while he is in the employment of the city. (1969 Code, sec. 10-21; Ordinance
1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Secs. 16-40—16-66. Reserved.
DIVISION 2. RESERVED*
Secs. 16-67-16-100. Reserved.
DIVISION 3. LICENSES AND RESTRICTIONS†
Sec. 16-101. Licensing requirements.
Every person desiring to engage in the electrical business in a capacity for which a license is required by this
Code shall be the holder of a valid electrician's license issued by the state. (1969 Code, sec. 10-36; Ordinance
1248 adopted 11/17/93; Ordinance 1615, sec. 2, adopted 7/23/13)
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 45/283
Sec. 16-102. Neon work.
At no time may a neon man do work in the city on any signs, buildings, etc., without holding a master or
journeyman electrical license with bond made to the city. (1969 Code, sec. 10-58; Ordinance 1248 adopted
11/17/93)
Secs. 16-103—16-132. Reserved.
DIVISION 4. PERMITS AND INSPECTIONS
Sec. 16-133. Permit required; exceptions; fees.
(a) Before commencing work on any electrical installation, the fees hereinafter provided shall be paid to and
a permit therefor must be secured from the office of the electrical inspector; provided, however, no permit shall
be required for minor work, such as repairing flush switches, replacing fuses, and changing lamp sockets and
receptacles. Permits shall be issued only to master electricians and to homeowners who qualify as hereinafter
set forth.
(b) Failure to obtain a permit shall constitute a violation of this chapter and each day work is done without a
permit shall constitute a separate offense.
(c) Where work for which a permit is required by this Code is started or proceeded with prior to obtaining said
permit, the fees herein specified shall be doubled. However, the payment of such double fee shall not relieve
any person from fully complying with the requirements of this Code in the execution of the work, nor from any
other penalties prescribed herein.
(1969 Code, sec. 10-65; Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Sec. 16-134. Contractor's responsibility to obtain permit.
All electrical contractors shall take out all permits and make payments for same at the office of the city
secretary in the city hall. (1969 Code, sec. 10-66; Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Sec. 16-135. Expiration of permit.
All permits shall expire and become null and void if the work authorized by such permit is not commenced
within 90 days from the date of issue, or if after commencement of work, the work is suspended for a period of
60 days. (1969 Code, sec. 10-67; Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Sec. 16-136. Homeowner's affidavit; scope of permit.
A homeowner shall be entitled to secure a permit for electrical installation only upon executing an affidavit
attesting to the following:
(1) Ownership of the property upon which the electrical installation is to be installed.
(2) Applicants bona fide intention to live therein.
(3) That applicant has not secured a homeowner's permit for other property within the last two
years.
(4) That applicant will perform all of the electrical installation without any physical assistance from
anyone other than members of his immediate family living in the household.
Nothing herein contained shall entitle anyone not a master electrician to secure a permit to install wiring in any
structure other than a single unit residence.
(1969 Code, sec. 10-68; Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Sec. 16-137. Permit fees.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 46/283
(a) Electrical permit fees are set out in section 10-63. On new construction, ranges and dryers are included
as a regular opening. All dryers, ranges and refrigerated coolers and hot water heaters wired in as separate
units will have a minimum fee of $1.50 for each permit.
(b) Signs with:
(1) Lights:
(A) Less than five, $0.25;
(B) Five to ten, $0.50;
(C) Ten to 20, $0.75;
(D) 20 to 50, $1.00;
(E) All signs containing more than 50 lights, $2.00.
(2) Motors:
(A) Less than one horsepower, $0.25;
(B) Over one and less than three horsepower, $0.50;
(C) Three to five horsepower, inclusive, $1.00;
(D) All motors above five horsepower, $1.50.
When an extension is made to old work or when new work is finished complete with fixtures or droplights or
switches, necessitating but one inspection, charge for outlet only.
(c) The state and federal governments and all instrumentalities thereof shall be exempt from the payment of
any fee for any electrical permit.
(1969 Code, sec. 10-69; Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Sec. 16-138. Inspections-Notice; making.
The holder of a permit shall notify the electrical inspector's office in writing as to when the installation is ready
for the rough-in inspection and shall also notify the electrical inspector's office as to when the electrical
installation is ready for the final inspection; and the electrical inspector shall cause such inspection to be made
within 24 hours of the time of receipt of such notice, exclusive of Saturdays and Sundays, and holidays
recognized by the city. (1969 Code, sec. 10-70; Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Sec. 16-139. Same-Reinspection fees.
If the installation shall fail to pass the rough-in or final inspection and a reinspection is therefore required, a fee
of $5.00 for the second reinspection, and $10.00 for each subsequent reinspection, shall be required. (1969
Code, sec. 10-71; Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93)
Secs. 16-140—16-161. Reserved.
ARTICLE III. CONSTRUCTION
Sec. 16-162. National Electrical Code-Adoption.
All electrical installations hereafter installed within the corporate limits of the city shall be done in a first class,
workmanlike manner, and in accordance with the National Electric Code, most current edition adopted after two
years from publication to allow for proper local review, at least one copy of which is on file in the office of the
building inspector; and the same is hereby adopted and made a part of this chapter, as fully as if set out at
length herein, subject to all amendments and deletions hereinafter contained. (1969 Code, sec. 10-78;
Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93; Ordinance 1615, sec. 3, adopted 7/23/13)
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 47/283
Sec. 16-163. Same-Amendments.
The National Electrical Code shall be amended as follows:
(1) All Romex installed shall be of the ground type, such as, 12-2WG, 12-3WG, etc.
(2) All receptacles shall be of the grounding type.
(3) The use of flexible conduit (except MC cable) will not be permitted for use as general wiring
system, but may be used for special types of connections, such as connecting motors, appliances,
recessed fixtures or where space limits the use of larger raceway for short runs or extensions, with
the approval of the electrical inspector.
(4) All lights in bathrooms, kitchens, or laundry rooms shall be controlled by wall switches, located
where lights cannot be readily reached from bathtub, sink, lavatory, or shower. In bathrooms and
kitchens all metal fixtures, receptacles and switches shall be grounded. Lights shall not be grounded
to their neutral wires.
(5) When additions or expansions are made that enclose the meter installations which exist on the
outside of buildings prior to the expansion, then it shall be the responsibility of the owner to have the
meter installation removed to a point that will be outside the expanded buildings and readily
accessible to public utility personnel for purposes of reading or repair.
(6) All newly installed panels and load centers must be large enough to accommodate the present
load requirements and have at least two spare circuits for future use. A one-inch empty conduit shall
be installed from the panel to the attic and from the panel to below the first floor of every new or
completely remodeled installation.
(7) Not more than four current-consuming outlets shall be connected to a 20-ampere appliance
circuit. Not more than eight current-consuming outlets shall be connected to a 15-ampere general
use branch circuit. Not more than ten current-consuming outlets shall be connected to a 20-ampere
general use branch circuit.
(8) Should any residence or building be moved from one location to another and should the wiring
be nonconforming to the new use, the residence or building shall be rewired.
(9) Should the occupancy of a residence be changed to a public building, such as, but not limited
to, a child-care facility caring for more than six children, a private school with more than six students
in attendance at one time or a nursing home facility caring for more than three patients, the wiring of
the entire building shall be made to comply with the requirements of the public building standards of
this chapter. When less than 25 percent of a residence is converted to public building use, such as,
but not limited to, a beauty shop, ceramic shop, service or retail shop, medical office, dental office or
clinic, then, and in that event only, the portion of the building in which the occupancy has changed
shall be rewired to comply with the public building standards. Where there has been a partial and
minor change of occupancy in a residence which displays no sign visible from the street such as, but
not limited to, an office not generally open to the public or a music studio at which not more than six
students congregate at one and the same time, then, and in that event only, residence-type wiring
will comply with this chapter.
(10) An all metal service entrance or service entrance cable complete with raintight entrance
equipment, shall be used from the point of contact with the power company to the distribution panel
and to all subpanels.
(11) Where service entrance equipment is installed outside a building, a minimum clearance of
41/2 feet must be maintained from the ground or any floor or platform to the bottom of such
equipment.
(12) Service entrance conductors shall not be run more than 20 feet within the hollow spaces of
combustible frame buildings, unless provided with automatic overcurrent protection at the outer
ends. On buildings where the electricity supply agency sets a transformer and extends from their
transformer, a number of connection boxes for customer convenience or where the electricity supply
agency designates a location for the meters, from these locations, the service conductors to each
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 48/283
individual occupancy shall be run either: under the slab; outside of building; on the roof, and when
conductors emerge into occupancy shall extend no more than 20 feet to service equipment, unless
they have overcurrent protection at the outer end, but in no case can unfused service conductors
feed through one single occupancy to another.
(13) Grounding electrode conductors shall be copper. The following will be acceptable as
grounding electrodes:
a. Rigid metal or copper water lines when there are 20 or more feet of them buried in the
earth.
b. Eight-foot driven ground rod of either one-half-inch copper, or five-eighths-inch copper
weld.
c. 20 feet of No. 4 solid copper buried in the bottom of the footing.
(14) Electrical metallic tubing shall not be installed in the ground or in concrete slabs poured on
the ground.
(15) All buildings open to the public and/or buildings in the fire zone shall be considered as places
of assembly and the fixed wiring methods shall be metal raceways or MC cable.
(16) Fire damage. Where, in the opinion of the electrical inspector, a fire originated due to faulty
electrical wiring, overloading of wiring or equipment or any unauthorized electrical installation, it shall
be the duty of the electrical inspector to inspect the premises involved, and where said lines or
electrical services have been cut in the firefighting process, no electrical service shall be reinstated
or reconnected until the said premises conform to the provisions of this chapter. Any where the lines
have not been cut in the firefighting process, and the electrical inspector deems such premises to be
dangerous or hazardous to life and property, he shall order the electrical service to be disconnected
immediately and remain disconnected until such defects have been corrected.
(17) Concealed wiring. Installations, where there is wiring to be concealed, shall be inspected
before concealment. The person installing such wiring shall notify the electrical inspector thereof and
the work shall not be covered until the inspector has approved same. Any person covering or
concealing wires before having same inspected shall be deemed guilty of violation of this chapter
and subject to the penalties provided for in section 16-5.
(18) Service connection. No person engaged in the business of transmission and sale of electric
current to users thereof shall make any connections of any kind to their transmission lines with the
electric wiring or apparatus in any building or place without first having received the electrical
inspector's certificate of compliance for said building or place.
(1969 Code, sec. 10-79; Ordinance 1248 adopted 11/17/93; Ordinance 1265 adopted 12/14/94)
CHAPTER 18
EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT*
Sec. 18-1. Organization established and named.
There exists the office of emergency management director of the city, which shall be held by the mayor in
accordance with state law.
(1) An emergency management coordinator shall be appointed by the city manager and serve at
his pleasure.
(2) The director shall be responsible for a program of comprehensive emergency management
within the city and for carrying out the duties and responsibilities set forth in this chapter. The
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 49/283
director may delegate authority for execution but the responsibility shall remain with the director.
(3) The operational emergency management organization of the city shall consist of the officers
and employees of the city so designated by the director in the emergency management plan, as well
as organized volunteer groups. The functions and duties of this organization shall be distributed
among such officers and employees in accordance with the terms of the emergency management
plan.
(1969 Code, sec. 8-1; Ordinance 1418, sec. 1, adopted 9/23/03)
Sec. 18-2. Director-Powers and duties.
The duties and responsibilities of the emergency management director shall include the following:
(1) Surveying actual or potential hazards that threaten life and property within the city and
identifying and requiring or recommending the implementation of measures that would tend to
prevent the occurrence or reduce the impact of such hazards if a disaster did occur.
(2) Supervision of the development and approval of an emergency management plan for the city,
and shall recommend for adoption by the city commission all mutual aid arrangements deemed
necessary for the implementation of such plan.
(3) Authority to declare a local state of disaster. The declaration may not be continued or renewed
for a period in excess of seven days except by or with the consent of the city commission. Any order
or proclamation declaring, continuing, or terminating a local state of disaster shall be given prompt
and general publicity and shall be filed promptly with the city secretary.
(4) Issuance of necessary proclamations, regulations, or directives, which are necessary for
carrying out the purposes of this chapter. Such proclamations, regulations or directives shall be
disseminated promptly by means calculated to bring its contents to the attention of the general
public and, unless circumstances attendant on the disaster prevent or impede, promptly filed with
the city secretary.
(5) Direction and control of the operations of the city emergency management organization as well
as the training of emergency management personnel.
(6) Determination of all questions of authority and responsibility that may arise within the
emergency management organization of the city.
(7) Maintenance of liaison with other municipal, county, district, state, regional, or federal
emergency management organizations.
(8) Marshalling of all necessary personnel, equipment, or supplies from any department of the city
to aid in the carrying out of the provisions of the emergency management plan.
(9) Supervision of the drafting and execution of mutual aid agreements, in cooperation with the
representatives of the state and of other local political subdivisions of the state, and the drafting and
execution, if deemed desirable, of an agreement with the county in which said city is located and
with other municipalities within the county, for the county-wide coordination of emergency
management efforts.
(10) Supervision of, and final authorization for, the procurement of all necessary supplies and
equipment, including acceptance of private contributions that may be offered for improving
emergency management within the city.
(11) Authorizing of agreements, after approval by the city attorney, for the use of private property
for public shelter and other purposes.
(12) Surveying the availability of existing personnel, equipment, supplies, and services that could
be used during a disaster, as provided for herein.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 50/283
(13) Other requirements as specified in the Texas Disaster Act, V.T.C.A., Government Code ch.
418.
(1969 Code, sec. 8-2; Ordinance 1418, sec. 2, adopted 9/23/03)
Sec. 18-3. Emergency management plan, regional mitigation action plan, and National Incident
Management System (NIMS).
(a) A comprehensive emergency management plan shall be developed and maintained in a current state.
The plan shall set forth the form of the organization; establish and designate divisions and functions; assign
responsibilities, tasks, duties and powers; and designate officers and employees to carry out the provisions of
this section. As provided by state law, the plan shall follow the standards and criteria established by the state
division of emergency management. Insofar as possible, the form of organization, titles, and terminology shall
conform to the recommendations of the state division of emergency management. When approved, it shall be
the duty of all departments and agencies to perform the functions assigned by the plan and to maintain their
portion of the plan in a current state of readiness at all times. The emergency management plan shall be
considered supplementary to this section and have the effect of law during the time of a disaster.
(b) A regional mitigation action plan shall be developed for the Nortex Region and maintained in a current
state. The objective of the Nortex Regional Mitigation Action Plan is to fulfill the requirements of the Hazard
Mitigation Grant, Pre-Disaster Mitigation Program (DMA 2000 Plan Criteria) and Flood Mitigation Assistance
Program.
(c) The National Incident Management System (NIMS) is hereby established as the standard command and
control system in the management of all incidents occurring within the city and incidents involving any public
safety division organized through the city.
(1969 Code, sec. 8-3; Ordinance 1418, sec. 3, adopted 9/23/03; Ordinance 1462, sec. 1, adopted 5/23/06)
Sec. 18-4. Interjurisdictional program.
The mayor is hereby authorized to join with the county judge in the formation of an interjurisdictional emergency
management program for the county, and shall have the authority to cooperate in the preparation of an
interjurisdictional emergency management plan and in the appointment of a joint emergency management
coordinator, as well as all powers necessary to participate in a countywide program of emergency management
insofar as said program may affect the city. (1969 Code, sec. 8-4; Ordinance 1418, sec. 4, adopted 9/23/03)
Sec. 18-5. Override conflicting orders, rules and regulations.
At all times when the orders, rules, and regulations made and promulgated pursuant to this chapter shall be in
effect, they shall supersede and override all existing ordinances, orders, rules and regulations insofar as the
latter may be inconsistent therewith. (1969 Code, sec. 8-5; Ordinance 1418, sec. 5, adopted 9/23/03)
Sec. 18-6. Liability.
This chapter is an exercise by the city of its governmental functions for the protection of the public peace,
health, and safety and neither the city, the agents and representatives of said city, nor any individual, receiver,
firm, partnership, corporation, association, or trustee, nor any of the agents thereof, in good faith carrying out,
complying with or attempting to comply with, any order, rule, or regulation promulgated pursuant to the
provisions of this chapter shall be liable for any damage sustained to persons as the result of said activity. Any
person owning or controlling real estate or other premises who voluntarily and without compensation grants to
the city a license or privilege, or otherwise permits the city to inspect, designate, and use the whole or any part
of such real estate or premises for the purpose of sheltering persons during an actual, impending or practice
enemy attack or natural or manmade disaster shall, together with his successors in interest, if any, not be civilly
liable for the death of, or injury to, any person on or about such real estate or premises under such license,
privilege or other permission or for loss of, or damage to, the property of such person. (1969 Code, sec. 8-6;
Ordinance 1418, sec. 6, adopted 9/23/03)
Sec. 18-7. Commitment of funds.
No person shall have the right to expend any public funds of the city in carrying out any emergency
management activity authorized by this chapter without prior approval by the city commission, nor shall any
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 51/283
person have any right to bind the city by contract, agreement, or otherwise without prior and specific approval of
the city commission unless during a declared disaster. During a declared disaster, the mayor may expend
and/or commit public funds of the city when deemed prudent and necessary for the protection of health, life, or
property. (1969 Code, sec. 8-7; Ordinance 1418, sec. 7, adopted 9/23/03)
Sec. 18-8. Offenses and penalties.
(a) It shall be unlawful for any person willfully to obstruct, hinder, or delay any member of the emergency
management organization in the enforcement of any rule or regulation issued pursuant to this chapter. It shall
likewise be unlawful for any person to wear, carry, or display any emblem, insignia, or any other means of
identification as a member of the emergency management organization of the city, unless the proper officials so
have granted such authority.
(b) Convictions for violations of the provisions of this chapter shall be punishable by fine as provided in
section 1-6.
(1969 Code, sec. 8-8; Ordinance 1418, sec. 8, adopted 9/23/03)
CHAPTER 20
FEES
ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL
Sec. 20-1. Fee to defray costs of collection.
In accordance with Vernon's Ann. C.C.P. art. 103.0031, there shall be imposed an additional fee of 30 percent
on all debts and accounts receivable (i.e., fines, fees, restitution, other debts, and costs) that are more than 60
days past due and have been referred to an attorney for collection. (1969 Code, sec. 10 ½-1; Ordinance 1483,
sec. 1, adopted 7/26/07)
Secs. 20-2—20-20. Reserved.
ARTICLE II. COURT FUNDS
Sec. 20-21. Municipal court technology fund.
(a) Established.
(1) There is hereby created and established a municipal court technology fund, here-in-now
known as the fund, pursuant to Vernon's Ann. C.C.P. art. 1102.0172.
(2) The fund may be maintained in an interest bearing account and may be maintained in the
general revenue account.
(b) Establishment of amount of the fee and assessment and collection.
(1) The fee shall be in the amount of $4.00.
(2) The fee shall be assessed and collected from the defendant, upon conviction for a
misdemeanor offense in the municipal court, as a cost of court. A defendant is considered convicted
if:
a. Judgment, sentence, or both are imposed on the person;
b. The person is placed on deferred disposition; or
c. The court defers final disposition or imposition of the judgment and sentence.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 52/283
(3) The fee shall be collected on conviction for an offense committed on or after February 26,
2008.
(4) The clerk of the court shall collect the fee and pay the fee to the finance director, who shall
deposit the fee into the municipal court technology fund.
(c) Designated use of the fund and administration.
(1) The fund shall be used only for the purpose of financing the purchase of or to maintain
technology enhancements for the municipal court. The term “technology enhancements” shall
include any and all items described in Vernon's Ann. C.C.P. art. 102.0172.
(2) The fund shall be administered by or under the direction of the city commission.
(1969 Code, sec. 10 ½-11; Ordinance 1495, secs. 1—3, adopted 2/26/08)
Sec. 20-22. Municipal court building security fund.
(a) There is hereby created and established a municipal court building security fund (the fund) pursuant to
Vernon's Ann. C.C.P. art. 102.017.
(b) The municipal court is hereby authorized and required to assess a municipal court building security fee
(the fee) in the amount of $3.00 against all defendants convicted of a misdemeanor offense by the municipal
court. Each misdemeanor conviction shall be subject to a separate assessment of the fee.
(c) A person is considered to have been convicted in a case, if:
(1) Judgment, sentence, or both are imposed on the person;
(2) The person receives deferred disposition; or
(3) The court defers final disposition or imposition of the judgment and sentence.
(d) The municipal court clerk is hereby authorized and required to collect the fee and to pay same to the city
treasury. All fees so collected and paid over to the city treasury shall be segregated in the fund.
(e) The fund shall be used only for the purpose of financing the purchase of security devices and/or services
for the building housing the municipal court. Security devices and/or services shall include any and all items
described in Vernon's Ann. C.C.P. art. 102.017(d).
(f) The fund shall be administered by or under the direction of the city commission.
(1969 Code, sec. 10 ½-12; Ordinance 1496, sec. 1, adopted 2/26/08)
CHAPTER 22
FIRE PROTECTION AND PREVENTION*
ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL
Sec. 22-1. Arson reward.
The city hereby offers a reward of $250.00 for the arrest and conviction of any person found guilty of committing
the crime of arson within the city. This reward is a standing offer, and shall be paid out of the general fund of the
city. (1969 Code, sec. 11-1; Ordinance 677 adopted 10/23/62)
Sec. 22-2. Fire site to remain clear of unauthorized persons.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 53/283
On a fire alarm being sounded for fire purposes, it shall be unlawful for any person, other than those owning an
interest in the property involved in the fire and (except the members of the fire department) persons authorized
by the fire chief and peace officers to go within 500 feet of the site of the fire while the fire department is in
action fighting the fire; provided, the fire chief may prescribe the limits of the field of operation of the fire
department in fighting a fire and designate same by ropes or stationing men along its lines, and when so
designated it shall be unlawful for any person, other than those mentioned in this section, to enter said limits.
(1969 Code, sec. 11-2; Ordinance 394, sec. 2, adopted 9/15/22)
Sec. 22-3. Spark and dust arresters for gin plants.
Before any gin plant shall be run or operated by any person in the city, it shall be equipped with and have within
and upon its smokestack a spark arrester sufficient to arrest and prevent the escape of fire sparks. The gin
plant shall also be equipped with and have a dust room sufficient to take care of and prevent the escape of dust
and fine lint cotton from the exhaust fans of said gin. (1969 Code, sec. 11-3; Ordinance 350, sec. 2, adopted
8/29/1916)
Sec. 22-4. Dumping ashes, etc.; fires in streets.
It shall be unlawful for any person to empty, dump, pour or place any ashes, live coals, trash or refuse in, or
burn any paper, trash or other matter or create any bonfire upon or in any street, alley or other public place in
the city. (1969 Code, sec. 11-4; Ordinance 310, sec. 1, adopted 1/14/1914)
Sec. 22-5. Pyrotechnics regulated.
(a) The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to
them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:
Pyrotechnics means and includes any combustible or explosive composition, or any substance or combination
of substances, or article prepared for the purpose of producing a visible or an audible effect by combustion,
explosion, deflagration or detonation, and includes Roman candles; sky rockets; helicopter type rockets;
cylindrical fountains; cone fountains; wheels; illuminating torches and colored fire in any form; sparklers and dip
sticks; mines; shells; firecrackers; salutes; whistles without report; squibs; a fire balloon; a hydrogen filled
balloon; signal lights; blank cartridges; toy pistols, toy cannons, toy canes or toy guns in which explosive or
flammable compound, or any tablets or other devices containing any explosive substance. The term
“pyrotechnics” shall not include auto flares, paper caps containing not in excess of an average of 0.25 of a grain
of explosive content per paper cap, manufactured in accordance with the interstate commerce commission
regulations for packing and shipping as provided therein and toy pistols, toy canes, toy guns, or other devices
for use of such caps the sale and use of which shall be permitted.
(b) No person shall hereafter fire or explode or keep, store, manufacture, or sell any pyrotechnics in the
corporate limits of the city to be used, fired or exploded in said city.
(c) No person shall hereafter have in his possession in the corporate limits of the city any pyrotechnics for the
purpose of using, firing, or exploding same in the corporate limits of said city; any pyrotechnics so found in the
possession of any person shall be condemned, seized, and confiscated by the police department except all
persons transporting any pyrotechnics within the city limits and extending for a distance outside of the city limits
for a total of 5,000 feet must secure a permit from the fire marshal's office of the department of public safety.
Any person transporting pyrotechnics under the provisions of this section shall at their own expense and at all
times during the term of the permit must obtain and secure for its and the city's protection public bodily injury
liability insurance in the amount of $100,000.00/$300,000.00 and property damage insurance in the amount of
$50,000.00. A certificate of the required insurance evidencing the carrying out of such insurance issued by an
insurance carrier authorized to transact business in the state for the benefit of the person named therein as
insured, as evidence of ability to respond in damages in at least such amount must be filed with and approved
by the city fire marshal. Any notice of cancellation of such insurance shall be immediately furnished to the city
fire marshal.
(d) This section shall not apply to the possession or use of signaling devices for current daily consumption by
railroads, police department, and fire department and other required to use them by law; to the possession, sale
or use of normal stock of flashlight compositions by photographers or dealers in photographic supplies; for
signal or ceremonial purposes; athletic or sports events; nor for the use by military organizations.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 54/283
(e) The state fire marshal may issue a written permit to a properly qualified person for giving a pyrotechnic
display in accordance with state law. It shall be the duty of the city fire marshal to make an investigation as to
whether such a display as proposed shall be of such a character and so located that it may be hazardous to
property or dangerous to any person, and he shall so advise the state fire marshal of his findings. All
pyrotechnic displays must be supervised by the city fire marshal or one of his fire prevention assistants. A copy
of all permits received from the state fire marshal must be filed with the city fire marshal within 24 hours before
such display is held.
(f) No person shall have, keep, store, manufacture or sell any pyrotechnics within the area immediately
adjacent and contiguous to the city limits, and extending for a distance outside of the city limits for a total of 50
feet, and it shall be unlawful to do or perform any act in violation of this section within such area of 50 feet
outside the city limits; provided this section shall not apply within any portion of such 50-foot area which is
contained within the territory of any other municipal corporation.
(g) No person shall use, fire or explode, or cause to be used, fired or exploded, any pyrotechnics within the
area immediately adjacent and contiguous to the city limits and extending for a distance outside of the city limits
for a total of 50 feet. It shall be unlawful to do or perform any act in violation of this section within such area of
50 feet outside the city limits; provided that this section shall not apply within any portion of such 50-foot area
which is contained within the territory of any other municipal corporation.
(h) No person shall have, keep, store, manufacture or sell any pyrotechnics within an area extending for a
distance outside of the city limits from a distance of 50 feet to a distance of 5,000 feet from the city limits;
unless such person shall have obtained a permit from the city fire marshal's office of the department of public
safety. The application for such permit shall contain the specific location of the building used to keep, store,
manufacture or sell the pyrotechnics and must also contain a blueprint or diagram showing the construction of
said building. The construction of the building must comply with the rules and regulations of the city fire
marshal's office.
(i) All persons manufacturing or selling pyrotechnics within an area extending for a distance outside of the
city limits from a distance of 50 feet to a distance of 5,000 feet from the city limits shall close their doors and
places of business each night from 11:55 p.m. until 6:00 a.m. the following morning and shall not sell or
manufacture any pyrotechnics during this time period.
(j) Should any section, paragraph, clause or phrase hereof be declared to be void or unconstitutional, such
holdings shall not affect the other valid provisions of this section, and same shall remain in full force and effect.
(k) Any person violating any provisions of this section shall upon conviction be punished as provided in
section 1-6.
(1969 Code, sec. 11-5; Ordinance 878 adopted 10/9/73)
Sec. 22-6. Fire prevention code adopted; penalty.
(a) There is hereby adopted a fire prevention code known as the International Fire Code, with the most
current published edition. Such code is published in book form and is to be maintained in the fire chief's office
and is referred to, incorporated herein, and made a part hereof for all purposes. Provided, however, that in the
event any conflict may arise between the provisions of the code adopted by the provisions of this article and
any other applicable provisions of this Code, state law, or city ordinance, rule or regulation, the provisions of
this Code, state law or city ordinance, rule or regulation shall prevail and be controlling.
(b) Any person violating the provisions of said fire prevention code shall be punished as provided in section
1-6.
(1969 Code, sec. 11-6; Ordinance 1145, sec. 1, adopted 3/10/87; Ordinance 1231, sec. 1, adopted 4/8/92;
Ordinance 1255, sec. 1, adopted 7/13/94; Ordinance 1364, sec. 3, adopted 3/6/01)
Sec. 22-7. Outdoor burning-Permit required.
The fire chief or his designated representatives is hereby authorized to issue permits for outdoor burning within
the city limit in compliance with the Texas Clean Air Act, located in V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code sec.
382.001 et seq., and the rules and regulations of the state commission on environmental quality regulating
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 55/283
outdoor burning, located in 30 Tex. Admin. Code ch. 111. (1969 Code, sec. 11-7; Ordinance 1411, sec. 1,
adopted 6/24/03)
Sec. 22-8. Same-Guidelines adopted.
The Texas Clean Air Act relating to outdoor burning and 30 Tex. Admin. Code ch. 111 that contains the rules
and regulations of the state commission on environmental quality for outdoor burning is hereby adopted as
guidelines for the regulation of outdoor burning. (1969 Code, sec. 11-8; Ordinance 1411, sec. 2, adopted
6/24/03)
Sec. 22-9. Same-Permit application.
The fire chief is hereby authorized to promulgate an application for a permit for outdoor burning within the city
limits, which said application will contain the name of the applicant, the time of the scheduled outdoor burn, the
amount and description of the items to be burned, the location of said outdoor burn, safety precautions to be
taken, and any other information relating to the decision of whether the outdoor burn should take place. The
application shall also state the times such burning is allowed, the minimum safety precautions, which applicants
must take, and any limitation regarding weather conditions. The fire chief or his designated representatives may
stop any burn which does not comply with all these requirements set out herein, or if it becomes necessary to
prevent a dangerous situation, or if it is a nuisance to any person or property. (1969 Code, sec. 11-9; Ordinance

Sec. 22-10. Penalty for failure to obtain an outdoor burning permit.
Any person failing to obtain an outdoor burning permit and performs an act in outdoor burning shall be punished
as provided in section 1-6. (1969 Code, sec. 11-10; Ordinance 1411, sec. 4, adopted 6/24/03)
Sec. 22-11. Fire limits construction.
Any construction within the fire limits must comply with chapter 10, pertaining to buildings.
Sec. 22-12. Combustible storage permit required.
In order to store combustible material according to Section 315 of the International Fire Code in a building
located in the fire limits as set out in section 10-1 of this Code, a permit must be acquired from the office of the
fire marshal. The fee for said permit shall be $100.00 per calendar year and must be renewed by January 31st
of any year. Application shall be made on a form developed by the fire marshal, a copy of which shall be kept
on file in the office of the city secretary. Periodical inspections, financial assurance, and signage will be required
as well as other requirements according to the fire marshal. (Ordinance 1575, sec. 1, adopted 12/20/11)
Sec. 22-13. Penalty for failure to obtain a combustible storage permit.
Failure to obtain a combustible storage permit and/or storage of combustible materials in a building located in
the fire limits without a permit shall be punished as provided in section 1-6. (Ordinance 1575, sec. 1, adopted
12/20/11)
Secs. 22-14—22-38. Reserved.
ARTICLE II. FIRE MARSHAL
Sec. 22-39. Appointment and qualifications.
The fire marshal shall be appointed by and report directly to the fire chief. (1969 Code, sec. 11-16; Ordinance
296, sec. 1, adopted 4/8/1913; Ordinance 1664, sec. 1, adopted 5/26/15)
Sec. 22-40. Investigation of fires-Required; records.
The fire marshal shall investigate the cause, origin and circumstances of every fire occurring within the city, by
which property has been destroyed or damaged, and shall especially make investigation as to whether such fire
was the result of carelessness or design. Such investigation shall be begun within 24 hours, not including
Sunday, of the occurrence of such fire. The fire marshal shall keep in his office a record of all fires occurring
within the city, together with all facts, statistics, and circumstances, including the origin of the fires and the
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 56/283
amount of the loss, which may be determined by the investigation required by this section. Such record shall at
all times be open to public inspection. (1969 Code, sec. 11-17; Ordinance 296, sec. 2, adopted 4/8/1913)
Sec. 22-41. Same-Gathering evidence; charging crimes.
The fire marshal, when in his opinion further investigation is necessary, shall take or cause to be taken the
testimony on oath, of all persons supposed to be cognizant of any facts or to have means of knowledge in
relation to the matter to which an examination as herein required is being made, and shall cause the same to
be reduced to writing; and if he shall be of the opinion that there is evidence sufficient to charge any person
with the crime of arson, or with the attempt to commit the crime of arson, or of conspiracy to defraud, or criminal
conduct in connection with such fire, he shall cause such person to be lawfully arrested and charged with such
offense, and shall furnish to the proper prosecuting attorney all such evidence, together with the name of
witnesses and all of the information obtained by him, including a copy of all pertinent and material testimony
taken in the case. (1969 Code, sec. 11-18; Ordinance 296, sec. 3, adopted 4/8/1913)
Sec. 22-42. Same-Power to take testimony.
The fire marshal shall have the power to summon witnesses before him to testify in relation to any matter which
is, by the provisions of this article, a subject of inquiry and investigation, and may require the production of any
book, paper, or document deemed pertinent thereto. The fire marshal is authorized and empowered to
administer oaths and affirmations to any persons appearing as witnesses before him. (1969 Code, sec. 11-19;
Ordinance 296, sec. 4, adopted 4/8/1913)
Sec. 22-43. Same-Contemptuous conduct of witnesses.
Any witness who:
(1) Refuses to be sworn;
(2) Refuses to appear or testify;
(3) Disobeys any lawful order of the fire marshal;
(4) Fails or refuses to produce any book, paper, or document touching any matter under
examination; or
(5) Is guilty of any contemptuous conduct;
during any of the proceedings of the fire marshal in the matter of said investigation or inquiry, after being
summoned to give testimony in relation to any matter under investigation as aforesaid, shall be deemed guilty
of a misdemeanor. It shall be the duty of the fire marshal to cause all such offenders to be prosecuted.
(1969 Code, sec. 11-20; Ordinance 296, sec. 5, adopted 4/8/1913)
Sec. 22-44. Private hearings; invoking the rule as to witnesses.
All investigations held by or under the direction of the fire marshal may, in his discretion, be private. Persons
other than those required to be present may be excluded from the place where such investigation is held.
Witnesses may be kept separate and apart from each other and not allowed to communicate with each other
until they have been examined. (1969 Code, sec. 11-21; Ordinance 296, sec. 6, adopted 4/8/1913)
Sec. 22-45. Right-of-entry-Investigation of fires.
The fire marshal shall have the authority at all times of day or night, when necessary in the performance of the
duties imposed upon him by the provisions of this article, to enter on and examine any building or premises
where any fire has occurred, and other buildings and premises adjoining or near the same, which authority shall
be exercised only with reason and good discretion. (1969 Code, sec. 11-22; Ordinance 296, sec. 7, adopted
4/8/1913)
State Law reference- See V.A.T.S. Insurance Code, art. 543 for similar provisions as to state fire marshal.
Sec. 22-46. Same-Investigation of condition of premises.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 57/283
The fire marshal, upon complaint of any persons having an interest in any building or property adjacent or
without any complaint, shall have the right at all reasonable hours, for the purposes of examination, to enter into
and upon all buildings and premises within the city. It shall be his duty, annually or more often, to enter upon
and make, or cause to be entered upon and made, a thorough examination of all mercantile, manufacturing,
and public buildings, together with the premises belonging thereto. (1969 Code, sec. 11-23; Ordinance 296,
sec. 8, adopted 4/8/1913)
Sec. 22-47. Maintaining unsafe condition-Dilapidated buildings; faulty appliances, etc.; dangerous
accumulations; order to eliminate.
Whenever the fire marshal shall find any building or other structure which, for want of repair or by reason of age
or dilapidated condition or for any cause, is especially liable to fire; which is so situated as to endanger other
buildings or property, or so occupied that fire would endanger persons or property therein; and shall find an
improper or dangerous arrangement of stoves, ranges, furnaces, or other heating appliances of any kind
whatsoever, including chimneys, flues, and pipes with which the same may be connected; a dangerous
arrangement of lighting devices or systems; or a dangerous or unlawful storage of explosives, compounds,
petroleum, gasoline, kerosene, dangerous chemicals, vegetable products, ashes, combustibles, inflammable
materials, refuse, or other conditions which may be dangerous in character or liable to cause or promote fire or
create conditions dangerous to the firemen or occupants; he shall order the same to be removed or the
condition to be remedied. Such order shall be forthwith complied with by the owners or occupants of said
buildings or premises; provided, however, if any such owner or occupant deems himself aggrieved by such
order, he may within five days appeal to the city manager who shall investigate the cause of the complaint; and
unless by his authority the order is revoked, such order shall remain in force and be forthwith complied with by
said owner or occupant. (1969 Code, sec. 11-24; Ordinance 296, sec. 8, adopted 4/8/1913)
Sec. 22-48. Same-Dilapidated buildings, etc., constitutes misdemeanor.
Any owner or occupant of a building or other structure or premises who shall keep or maintain the same when,
for want of repair, or by reason of age or dilapidated condition, or for any cause it is especially liable to fire and
which is so situated as to endanger buildings or property of others, or it is especially liable to fire and which is
so occupied that fire would endanger other persons or their property therein, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor
and punished as provided in section 1-6. (1969 Code, sec. 11-25; Ordinance 296, sec. 9, adopted 4/8/1913)
Sec. 22-49. Same-Improper appliances, etc., or dangerous accumulations, constitutes misdemeanor.
Any owner or occupant of any building or other structure or premises, who shall keep or maintain the same with
an improper arrangement of any stove, range, furnace, or other heating appliance of any kind whatever,
including chimneys, fines and pipes with which the same may be connected, so as to be dangerous in the
matter of fire or health of safety of persons or property of others; or who shall keep or maintain any building, or
other structure or premises with any improper arrangement of any lighting device or system, or with storage of
explosives, petroleum, gasoline, kerosene, chemicals, vegetable products, ashes, combustibles, inflammable
materials, refuse or with any other condition which shall be dangerous in character to the persons, health or
property of others; or which shall be dangerous in the matter of promoting, augmenting or causing fires; or
which shall create conditions dangerous to firemen or occupants of such building, structure or premises other
than the maintainer thereof, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and punished as provided in section 1-6. (1969
Code, sec. 11-26; Ordinance 296, sec. 10, adopted 4/8/1913)
Sec. 22-50. Same-Order prerequisite to prosecution.
No prosecution shall be brought under sections 22-48 and 22-49 until the order provided for in section 22-47 is
given, and the party notified shall fail or refuse to comply with the same. (1969 Code, sec. 11-27; Ordinance
296, sec. 11, adopted 4/8/1913)
Secs. 22-51—22-73. Reserved.
ARTICLE III. EMERGENCY RESPONSE AND RESCUE SERVICES*
Sec. 22-74. Definitions.
The following words, terms and phrases shall have the meaning ascribed to them in this section, unless the
context of their usage clearly indicates another meaning:
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 58/283
Business entity or person means any corporation, sole proprietorship, partnership, limited partnership, firm or
other similar entity, or any individual person, engaged in any commercial, business or industrial transactions of
any nature.
Hazardous material means any substance defined under section 101(14) of CERCLA; any biological agent or
other disease-causing agent which, after release into the environment and upon exposure, ingestion, inhalation,
or assimilation, by ingestion through food chains, will or may reasonably be anticipated to cause death,
disease, behavioral abnormalities, cancer, genetic mutation, physiological malfunctions (including malfunctions
in reproduction), or physical deformations in such persons or their offspring; any substance listed by the U.S.
Department of Transportation as hazardous materials under 49 CFR 172.101 and appendices; or any
hazardous waste as defined under 29 CFR 1910.120.
Responsible party means all persons involved in the possession, ownership or transportation of any hazardous
material that is released or abandoned, or who have legal liability for the causation of an incident resulting in
the release or abandonment of any hazardous materials.
Service means a response by one or more fire/EMS department units to an incident involving a leakage, spill
and/or other release and/or abandonment of any hazardous material.
Service call means the period of time from the dispatch of fire/EMS department units at the site where the
service is to be performed, to the return of all department units to an available status.
(1969 Code, sec. 11-76; Ordinance 1451, sec. 1, adopted 9/27/05)
Sec. 22-75. Defraying of costs authorized.
In order to partially defray the costs incurred by the city for providing hazardous materials service by the
fire/EMS department, charges are hereby established and shall be paid and collected from the responsible
party.
(1) For service calls of one hour or less, the responsible party shall pay for expendable supplies,
plus an additional 30 percent of the cost of the expendable supplies.
(2) For service calls of more than one hour, the responsible party shall pay the actual per hour
labor cost and a 50 percent markup for fringe benefits for the firefighters involved in the response
and $185.00 per hour for any vehicle involved in the response except for the fire chief's vehicle. The
charge shall be based on per quarter hour for every quarter hour, or portion thereof, over the first
hour. The responsible party shall also pay for expendable supplies, plus an additional 30 percent of
the cost of the expendable supplies.
(1969 Code, sec. 11-77; Ordinance 1451, sec. 1, adopted 9/27/05)
Sec. 22-76. Identification of responsible party.
If the responsible party cannot be identified or refuses to remedy all hazardous conditions created by leakage,
spill and/or other release and/or abandonment of a hazardous material, the fire/EMS department may contract
with a third party to complete the necessary remedial measures. The responsible party shall pay for all third
party costs, plus an additional 20 percent of third party cost, associated with the hazardous materials
remediation. (1969 Code, sec. 11-78; Ordinance 1451, sec. 1, adopted 9/27/05)
Sec. 22-77. Duty to report incidents.
It shall be the duty of each responsible party to report any incident involving any leakage, release, spill, or
abandonment of any hazardous materials to the fire/EMS department immediately upon the discovery of the
same, or as soon thereafter as possible. (1969 Code, sec. 11-79; Ordinance 1451, sec. 1, adopted 9/27/05)
Sec. 22-78. Exceptions to payment of charges.
Notwithstanding any other provision of this article, any individual who constitutes a responsible party shall not
be required to pay charges authorized under this article if all of the following conditions are met:
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 59/283
(1) The responsible party does not illegally dispose of nor abandon substances deemed as
hazardous materials;
(2) The individual otherwise responsible or liable for the release of a hazardous material is not
involved in the possession, ownership or transportation of the hazardous material as the employee,
agent, or servant of any business entity or person;
(3) The individual involved in the possession, ownership or transportation of the hazardous
material released is so involved solely for private, noncommercial purposes related to the
individual's own residential property, real property or private personal property, and the individual
receives or is to receive no compensation for any services involving the hazardous materials; and
(4) The hazardous material possessed, owned or being transported by the individual are in forms,
quantities and containers ordinarily and lawfully available for sale as consumer products to members
of the general public.
(1969 Code, sec. 11-80; Ordinance 1451, sec. 1, adopted 9/27/05)
Sec. 22-79. Exempt entities.
This article shall not apply to any hazardous materials possessed, owned or transported by the city, the state
(including its political subdivisions) or the federal government. (1969 Code, sec. 11-81; Ordinance 1451, sec. 1,
adopted 9/27/05)
Sec. 22-80. Offenses and penalties.
(a) It shall be unlawful for any person willfully to obstruct, hinder, or delay any member of the fire/EMS
department in the enforcement of any rule or regulation issued pursuant to this article.
(b) Convictions for violations of the provisions of this article shall be punishable by fine as provided in section
1-6.
(1969 Code, sec. 11-82; Ordinance 1451, sec. 1, adopted 9/27/05)
Sec. 22-81. Fees.
(a) The city commission authorizes the city manager to authorize collection of fees to be billed against the
insurance coverage or parties involved in motor vehicle accidents, vehicle fires, hazardous waste or chemical
spills, and/or other non-fire suppression activities to which the city responds with fire department equipment
and/or personnel.
(b) Those charges will be assessed as a debt to the party causing the event, the landowner, the party
controlling the premises in the event of a spill or dumping and/or the party transporting said hazardous,
dangerous and/or injurious product.
Fire suppression activities resulting from third party negligence may be billed against that third party. Fire
suppression activities resulting from arson may be billed against the arsonist.
(c) Fees for services assessed and collected in this section shall be as follows:
(1) The response cost shall be $425.00 per hour, for each fire response apparatus.
(2) When an ambulance is used as a safety stand-by vehicle the cost of $300.00 per hour for
each ambulance shall apply.
(3) The cost for a command vehicle or manpower vehicle shall be $200.00 per hour for each
vehicle.
(4) If any protective equipment or firefighting equipment is damaged or contaminated, the current
replacement cost shall be charged.
