(8) Information provided by the applicant will be subject to verification by the police department.
(9) A permit will not be issued if there is affirmative statement as to whether the applicant has ever
been:
(A) Convicted of or pleaded nolo contendere to a misdemeanor involving fraud, theft,
embezzlement, burglary, fraudulent conversion, or misappropriation of property within the
preceding ten years, or convicted of or pleaded nolo contendere to any felony.
(B) Found liable in a civil or administrative action in which the complaint or petition alleged
fraud, theft, embezzlement, fraudulent conversion, misappropriation of property, or the use of
untrue or misleading representations in an attempt to sell or dispose of property or to obtain
money or a thing of value from another.
(C) Found liable under law regarding the use of unfair, unlawful, or deceptive business
practices.
(D) Subject to an injunction or restrictive court order relating to business activity as the result
of an action brought by a federal, state, or local public agency, including action affecting a
vocational license.
(E) Found to be soliciting before a permit is approved.
(10) If a permit is denied, the person whose application was denied cannot go within one city
block of other valid permit holders.
(b) Itinerant merchants, transient merchants and peddlers.
(1) Any driver or person desiring a permit to conduct sales activity in the city as a mobile ice
cream truck, mobile frozen dairy vendor, or other itinerant or transient vendor shall make a written
application to the city.
(2) Fee for an itinerant merchants permit shall be $115.00. A non-refundable deposit of $15.00 will
be paid upon application for a permit, with the balance due when permit is issued.
(3) After review of the permit application and after a minimum of 24 hours of the receipt of the
application, the city secretary or his designee shall either issue a permit, as provided in this
ordinance, or notify the person applying that the application does not comply with the requirements
of this chapter, specifying why the application is incomplete or otherwise does not comply.
(4) A permit granted under this article will be valid only until the termination of the solicitation
period specified in the permit with a maximum of three days. No permit will be issued to the same
applicant more than four times per year. Regardless of when issued, all permits expire December 31
of each calendar year.

(B) The applicant had no active suspension on his or her driving privileges in any state.
(C) No permit shall be issued if the applicant has been convicted of or pleaded nolo
contendere to any felony.
(D) Permit is obtained prior to beginning of operations.

Sec. 42-4. Investigation, issuance, denial and revocation.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 123/283
(a) It shall be the duty of the city secretary or her designee to investigate each applicant for a permit under
this chapter before issuance of such a permit based on a review of the applicant's background.
(b) The city secretary or her designee shall issue the applicant a home solicitation or itinerant vendor permit if
the city secretary determines that the application has been fully and accurately completed, the permit
application fee has been paid, and that the applicant satisfied each requirement of this ordinance. If not, the city
secretary can deny the permit.
(c) A home solicitation or itinerant vendor permit may be revoked if the chief of police so determines that
reasonable cause exists to believe that:
(1) A statement of fact contained in the application was false or materially misleading.
(2) The permit holder has failed to comply with any of the provisions off this ordinance.
(3) Any of the conditions of this ordinance is, or has become applicable to the permit holder.
(4) The permit holder has engaged in a home solicitation that involves the use of false,
misleading, fraudulent or deceptive acts.
(5) If, at the discretion of the chief of police, the permit is not in the best interest of the citizen's of
Vernon.
(Ordinance 1562, sec. 2(Exh. A(IV)), adopted 6/28/11)
Sec. 42-5. Penalties.
(a) Any person violating any provision of this ordinance or failing to observe any provision of this chapter
shall have their permit revoked immediately and will not be entitled to reapply for a period of one year from the
date of the revocation. In the event of such forfeiture of permit, no part of such permit fee as may have been
paid shall be refunded to such person.
(b) Any person, firm, or corporation violating any of the terms or provisions of this chapter shall be guilty of a
Class C misdemeanor and upon conviction, shall be fined in a sum not to exceed the maximum amount allowed
by state law and city charter for each offense, and a separate offense shall be deemed committed upon each
day during or on which a violation occurs or continues.
(c) In case of any willful violation of any of the terms and provisions of this chapter, the city, in addition to
imposing the penalties above provided, may institute any appropriate action or proceeding in any court having
proper jurisdiction, to restrain, correct or abate such violations; and the definition of any violation of the terms of
this ordinance as a misdemeanor, shall not preclude the city from invoking the civil remedies given it by the
laws of the state, but same shall be cumulative and subject to prosecution as hereinabove prescribed for such
violations.
(Ordinance 1562, sec. 2(Exh. A(V)), adopted 6/28/11)

Sec. 44-19. Social Security Act provisions-Responsibility for entering agreements.

Sec. 44-20. Same-Mayor to execute agreements.
The mayor is appointed as agent of the city commission and of the city to execute all necessary agreements
and instruments for and in behalf of the commission and city. (1969 Code, sec. 21-32; Ordinance 622, sec. 2,
adopted 6/12/56)
Sec. 44-21. Same-Responsibility for assessments, collections, payments and reports.
The city finance manager is directed to be responsible for making assessments, collections, payments and
reports as required by the state department of public welfare. (1969 Code, sec. 21-33; Ordinance 622, sec. 3,
adopted 6/12/56; Ordinance 1084 adopted 3/12/85)
Sec. 44-22. Same-Funds allocation.
A sufficient sum of money shall be allocated and set aside from available funds for the purpose of carrying out
the provisions of the Acts mentioned in section 44-19, such money so allocated and set aside to be known as
the city social security fund, which fund shall be set aside and maintained in the regular city depository. (1969
Code, sec. 21-34; Ordinance 622, sec. 4, adopted 6/12/56)
Sec. 44-23. TMRS service credits for probationary period of employment.
(a) Any employee of the city who is a member of the Texas Municipal Retirement System (TMRS) and who
performed service as a probationary employee for the city prior to September 1, 1989, for which the employee
did not receive credited service in the system because the person, as a probationary employee was not
enrolled as a member of the system during the period of probationary employment, is hereby allowed to obtain
prior service credit for the period of such probationary service (not in excess of six months), pursuant to the
provisions of V.T.C.A., Government Code sec. 853.303.
(b) To obtain prior service credit allowable under subsection (a) of this section, any employee entitled thereto
shall file a detailed written statement of the service claimed with the city secretary within one year from the
effective date of the ordinance from which this section is derived.
(c) As soon as practicable after the employee has filed a claim for the prior service credit under V.T.C.A.,
Government Code sec. 853.303, the city secretary shall, if said officer determines that such service was
performed as claimed, verify the prior service allowable (not exceeding six months) and the average monthly
compensation paid the member during the period of probationary employment, and shall certify to the board of
trustees of the system the creditable prior service approved, and the average monthly compensation paid to the
person by the city during the period of probationary employment.
(1969 Code, sec. 21-35; Ordinance 1924, secs. I-III, adopted 11/19/96)
Sec. 44-24. Authorization of restricted prior service credit.
(a) On the terms and conditions set out in V.T.C.A., Government Code sec. 853.305, as amended
(hereinafter referred to as the “TMRS Act”), each member of the Texas Municipal Retirement System
(hereinafter referred to as the “system”) who is now or who hereafter becomes an employee of the city shall
receive restricted prior service credit for service previously performed as an employee of any of the entities
described in said V.T.C.A., Government Code sec. 853.305; provided that:
(1) The person does not otherwise have credited service in the system for that service; and
(2) The service meets the requirements of said V.T.C.A., Government Code sec. 853.305.
(b) The service credit hereby granted may be used only to satisfy length-of-service requirements for
retirement eligibility, has no monetary value in computing the annuity payments allowable to the member, and
may not be used in other computations, including computation of updated service credits.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 125/283
(c) A member seeking to establish restricted prior service credit under this section must take the action
required under said V.T.C.A., Government Code sec. 853.305 while still an employee of the city.
(1969 Code, sec. 21-36; Ordinance 1295, sec. I, adopted 11/19/96)
Sec. 44-25. Authorization of updated service credits.
(a) On the terms and conditions set out in V.T.C.A., Government Code secs. 853.401-853.404, as amended
(hereinafter referred to as the “TMRS Act”), each member of the Texas Municipal Retirement System
(hereinafter referred to as the “system”) who has current service credit or prior service credit in the system in
force and effect January 1 of the calendar year preceding such allowance, by reason of service in the
employment of the city, and on such date had at least 36 months of credited service with the system, shall be
and is hereby allowed updated service credit, as that term is defined in V.T.C.A., Government Code sec.
853.402(d).
(b) On the terms and conditions set out in V.T.C.A., Government Code sec. 853.601, any member of the
system:
(1) Who is eligible for updated service credits on the basis of service with this city;
(2) Who has unforfeited credit for prior service and/or current service with another participating
municipality by reason of previous service; and
(3) Was a contributing member on January 1 of the calendar year preceding such allowance;
shall be credited with updated service credits pursuant to, calculated in accordance with, and subject to
adjustment as set forth in V.T.C.A., Government Code sec. 853.601, both as to the initial grant hereunder and
all future grants under this section.
(c) The updated service credit hereby allowed and provided for shall be 100 percent of the base updated
service credit of the member, calculated as provided in V.T.C.A., Government Code sec. 853.402(c).
(d) Each updated service credit allowed hereunder shall replace any updated service credit, prior service
credit, special prior service credit, or antecedent service credit previously authorized for part of the same
service.
(e) In accordance with the provisions of subsection (d) of section 853.401 of the TMRS Act (V.T.C.A.,
Government Code sec. 853.303(d)), the deposits required to be made to the system by employees of the
several participating departments on account of current service shall be calculated from and after the effective
date of this section on the full amount of such person's compensation as an employee of the city.
(1969 Code, sec. 21-37; Ordinance 1311, sec. I, adopted 11/25/97; Ordinance 1381, sec. I, adopted 12/11/01)
Sec. 44-26. Increase in retirement annuities.
(a) On terms and conditions set out in V.T.C.A., Government Code sec. 853.203, the city hereby elects to
allow and to provide for payment of the increases below stated in monthly benefits payable by the system to
retired employees and to beneficiaries of deceased employees of the city under current service annuities and
prior service annuities arising from service by such employees to the city. An annuity increased under this
section replaces any annuity or increased annuity previously granted to the same person.
(b) The amount of the annuity increase under this section is computed as the sum of prior service and
current service annuities on the effective date of retirement of the person on whose service the annuities are
based, multiplied by 70 percent of the percentage change in Consumer Price Index for all urban consumers,
from December of the year immediately preceding the effective date of the person's retirement to the December
that is 13 months before the effective date of the ordinance from which this section is derived.
(c) An increase in an annuity that was reduced because of an option selection is reducible in the same
proportion and in the same manner that the original annuity was reduced.
(d) If a computation hereunder does not result in an increase in the amount of an annuity, the amount of the
annuity will not be changed hereunder.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 126/283
(e) The amount by which an increase under this section exceeds all previously granted increases to an
annuitant is an obligation of the city and of its account in the municipality accumulation fund of the system.
(1969 Code, sec. 21-31; Ordinance 1311, sec. II, adopted 11/25/97; Ordinance 1381, sec. II, adopted 12/11/01)
Sec. 44-27. Dates of allowances and increases.
The initial allowance of updated service credit and increase in retirement annuities hereunder shall be effective
on January 1, 2002, subject to approval by the board of trustees of the system. An allowance of updated
service credits and an increase in retirement annuities shall be made hereunder on January of each
subsequent year until this article ceases to be in effect under V.T.C.A., Government Code sec. 853.404(e),
provided that, as to such subsequent year, the actuary for the system has made the determination set forth in
V.T.C.A., Government Code sec. 853.404(d) of the TMRS Act. (1969 Code, sec. 21-39; Ordinance 1311, sec.
III, adopted 11/25/97; Ordinance 1381, sec. III, adopted 12/11/01)
Sec. 44-28. Increased deposit rate.
All employees of the city, who are members of the Texas Municipal Retirement System, shall make deposits to
the system at the rate of seven percent of their individual earnings. (1969 Code, sec. 21-40; Ordinance 1311,
sec. IV, adopted 11/25/97; Ordinance 1381, sec. IV, adopted 12/11/01)
Sec. 44-29. Rate of contributions by the city.
Pursuant to V.T.C.A., Government Code sec. 853.407(g) of the TMRS Act, the city hereby elects to make future
normal and prior service contributions to its account in the municipal accumulation fund of the system at such
combined rate of the total compensation paid by the city to employees who are members of the system, as the
system's actuary shall annually determine as the rate necessary to fund, within the amortization period
determined as applicable to the city under the TMRS Act, the costs of all benefits which are or may become
chargeable to or are to be paid out of the city's account in said accumulation fund, regardless of other
provisions of the TMRS Act limiting the combined rate of city contributions. (1969 Code, sec. 21-41; Ordinance
1402, sec. 1, adopted 12/17/02)
CHAPTER 46
PLUMBING
Sec. 46-1. Plumbing code adopted; penalty.
(a) There is hereby adopted a plumbing code known as the International Plumbing Code, with the most
current published edition. Such code is published in book form and is to be maintained in the community
development division director's office and is referred to, incorporated herein, and made a part hereof for all
purposes. Provided, however, that in the event any conflict may arise between the provisions of the code
adopted by the provisions of this article and any other applicable provisions of this Code, state law, or city
ordinance, rule or regulation, the provisions of this Code, state law or city ordinance, rule or regulation shall
prevail and be controlling.
(b) Any person violating the provisions of said plumbing code shall be punished, as provided in section 1-6.
(1969 Code, sec. 22-1; Ordinance 1256, sec. 1, adopted 8/10/94; Ordinance 1364, sec. 5, adopted 3/6/01)
Sec. 46-2. Fuel gas code adopted; penalty.

published edition. Such code is published in book form and is to be maintained in the community development
division director's office and is referred to, incorporated herein, and made a part hereof for all purposes.
Provided, however, that in the event any conflict may arise between the provisions of the code adopted by the
provisions of this article and any other applicable provisions of this Code, state law, or city ordinance, rule or
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0

regulation, the provisions of this Code, state law or city ordinance, rule or regulation shall prevail and be
controlling.
(b) Any person violating the provisions of said fuel gas code shall be punished, as provided in section 1-6.

CHAPTER 48
STREETS AND SIDEWALKS*
ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL
Sec. 48-1. Damage to pavement-By vehicles.
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate or propel any traction engine or other kind of engine, vehicle,
implement or machinery of any kind, the surface of the wheels of which have cogs or lugs on them or are
otherwise rough or uneven, or which have no wheels on, along or across any paved street within the city. (1969
Code, sec. 23-1; Ordinance 354, sec. 1, adopted 6/12/1917)
Sec. 48-2. Same-Cutting, digging in or breaking pavement; permit and fee required.
(a) It shall be unlawful for any person or utility company to enter upon any paved street, alley, or sidewalk
within the city and cut, dig, or break any hole or trench in the pavement without first making application therefor
to the city. Said application shall set forth in designating the street, alley or sidewalk to be thus disturbed, and
the extent of the pavement cut to be made. The city shall issue a permit for such pavement cut. Said permit
shall set forth the regulations to restore the pavement from the cut.
(b) A fee of $250.00 plus $1.58 per square foot shall be charged and collected by the city to repair the
pavement. The measurement for charging the fee is to be determined by the street department's inspector.
(1969 Code, sec. 23-2; Ordinance 468, sec. 1, adopted 7/15/30; Ordinance 1365, sec. 1, adopted 3/27/01;
Ordinance 1611, sec. 1, adopted 3/26/13)
Sec. 48-3. Use for utility purposes; consent required.
It shall be unlawful for any person operating or intending to operate a telegraph, telephone, electric power or
light, street railway, interurban railway, steam railway, sewer or sewage disposal or gas company, or any other
character of public utility, to use for any such purpose any street, alley, highway or grounds of the city without
first obtaining the consent of the city commission expressed by ordinance and upon paying such compensation
as may be prescribed and upon such conditions as may be provided by such ordinance. (1969 Code, sec. 23-3;
Ordinance 449, sec. 1, adopted 10/28/27)
Sec. 48-4. Hanging signs, etc., prohibited.
It shall be unlawful for any person to hang or suspend, or permit to remain hanging or suspended, any sign,
board, plank or other thing over, above or across any public sidewalk in this city. (1969 Code, sec. 23-4;
Ordinance 228, sec. 1, adopted 6/9/1908)
Sec. 48-5. Sale of vehicle prohibited.
It shall be unlawful for any person to park or place any vehicle on any public street or alley in the city for the
purpose of exhibiting, advertising, or offering the same for sale. (1969 Code, sec. 23-5; Ordinance 395B, sec. 1,
adopted 4/10/23)
Secs. 48-6—48-28. Reserved.
ARTICLE II. STREET CLOSING PROCEDURE
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 128/283
Sec. 48-29. Petition-Authorized.
All of the fee owners of real property abutting on any street, alley, or other public thoroughfare in the city may
petition the city commission to vacate and abandon and close any such street, alley, or public thoroughfare, or
any portion thereof. (1969 Code, sec. 23-27; Ordinance 707, sec. 1, adopted 1/12/65)
Sec. 48-30. Same-Execution; acknowledgment.
Such petition shall be duly executed and acknowledged by all of the fee owners of real property abutting on
such street, alley, or thoroughfare, or portion thereof, sought to be closed, in the same manner as required by
the laws of the state for the execution of deeds of conveyances to real property. If such property is a homestead
property, as that term is defined under the laws of this state, such instrument shall be executed and
acknowledged by the husband and wife. (1969 Code, sec. 23-28; Ordinance 707, sec. 2, adopted 1/12/65)
Sec. 48-31. Same-Filing.
Such petition, duly executed, shall be considered filed when it is left with the community development director
at his normal place of conducting business. (1969 Code, sec. 23-29; Ordinance 707, sec. 4, adopted 1/12/65;
Ordinance 1417, sec. 1, adopted 9/23/03)
Sec. 48-32. Proof of ownership.
For the purposes of establishing the identity of the actual fee owners of such abutting property, the community
development director may require the petitioners to submit proof of their title acceptable to the city attorney. All
expenses in connection with such proof of ownership shall be borne by petitioners. (1969 Code, sec. 23-30;
Ordinance 707, sec. 3, adopted 1/12/65; Ordinance 1417, sec. 2, adopted 9/23/03)
Sec. 48-33. Hearing-Setting.
The community development director shall bring such petition to the attention first to the planning and zoning
commission after the notice of public hearing for such street closure has been published. The planning and
zoning commission public hearing shall be at a time of not more than 30 days before the city commission may
consider the petition in a second public hearing. (1969 Code, sec. 23-31; Ordinance 707, sec. 5, adopted
1/12/65; Ordinance 1417, sec. 3, adopted 9/23/03)
Sec. 48-34. Same-Publishing notice.
The community development director shall cause a notice of such hearing to be published one time in a
newspaper published in the city at least seven days before the date of such hearing before the planning and
zoning commission and the date of a possible public hearing before the city commission. Such notice shall
describe the street, alley or public right-of-way, or portion thereof, sought to be closed, as described in the
petition, and shall state the date, hour and place of hearing before the planning and zoning commission and city
commission. The cost of the publication for the public hearing shall be borne by the petitioners. Payment for the
cost of publication shall be paid before the public hearings and certified as being paid by the community
development director to the city manager. (1969 Code, sec. 23-32; Ordinance 707, sec. 6, adopted 1/12/65;
Ordinance 1417, sec. 4, adopted 9/23/03)
Sec. 48-35. Same-Receiving evidence.
At the hearings described in this article, the commissioners of the planning and zoning commission and city
commission may hear evidence as to whether or not it would be for the benefit of the public to close such
street, alley or public right-of-way, or any portion thereof, described in such petition, or any part thereof. At such
hearing any citizen of the city may present evidence for or against such petition. The planning and zoning
commission shall recommend to the city commission for the petition either to be approved or denied. If
recommended for approval the city commission shall hear the petition. If recommended for denial the petitioner
may request a hearing by the city commission. (1969 Code, sec. 23-33; Ordinance 707, sec. 7, adopted
1/12/65; Ordinance 1417, sec. 5, adopted 9/23/03)
Sec. 48-36. Ordinance closing street.
After such hearings described in this article, if the city commission is of the opinion that it would be to the public
benefit to close such street, alley, or public right-of-way, or any portion thereof, described in such petition, or
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 129/283
any part thereof, the city commission, after two readings, pass an ordinance to that effect and take such further
action as might be necessary to effect such closing and abandonment. After passage of the ordinance by the
city commission, the city secretary shall cause the ordinance to be filed for record with the county clerk's office.
(1969 Code, sec. 23-34; Ordinance 707, sec. 8, adopted 1/12/65; Ordinance 1417, sec. 6, adopted 9/23/03)
Sec. 48-37. Procedure not exclusive.
The procedures outlined in this article shall not be exclusive of any other procedures for closing public streets,
alleys or public thoroughfares in the city that are otherwise permitted under the laws of the state. (1969 Code,
sec. 23-35; Ordinance 707, sec. 9, adopted 1/12/65)
Secs. 48-38—48-62. Reserved.
ARTICLE III. OBSTRUCTIONS*
Sec. 48-63. Obstructions; permit required.
It shall be unlawful for any person to place or erect any obstruction on any street or sidewalk within the city
without first having obtained a permit therefor from the city commission, except for periodic sidewalk sales in
front of a business. (1969 Code, sec. 23-47; Ordinance 388, sec. 1, adopted 4/13/22)
Sec. 48-64. Fencing or placing articles therein.
It shall be unlawful for any person to obstruct any sidewalk, street, or alley, or any part thereof, in any manner,
either by fencing or by placing or leaving any kind of obstruction thereon or therein; provided that nothing in this
section shall prevent persons from placing packages, articles and goods which they may be receiving or
sending out, on any sidewalk directly in front or in any alley directly to the rear, of the building such person may
then be occupying, provided the same shall not be placed more than four feet from the outer edge of such
sidewalk and provided same shall not remain thereon or therein for more than two hours. (1969 Code, sec. 23-
48; Ordinance 222, adopted 6/13/1905; Ordinance 289, sec. 2, adopted 11/12/1912)
Sec. 48-65. Stands, structures, etc., in streets-Declared a nuisance.
All hamburger stands, popcorn stands, restaurants, fruit stands, and other stands, obstructions, and structures
erected, used, maintained, and located in the streets of the city within the fire limits are declared to be
nuisances. (1969 Code, sec. 23-49; Ordinance 290 adopted 2/4/1913)
Sec. 48-66. Same-Unlawful to permit.
It shall be unlawful for any person to erect, place or allow to remain within any street or any part thereof within
the fire limits any obstruction, stand or structure described in section 48-65. (1969 Code, sec. 23-50; Ordinance
291 adopted 2/4/1913)
Sec. 48-67. Obstructions; streets, sidewalks and alleys.
The occupant or owner of any property is responsible for keeping the street, alley, sidewalk and public grounds
clear of obstructions that are caused by overgrowth of trees, shrubs or vines that originate on the owner's
property. This includes the trimming of trees, shrubbery and vines which may obstruct any vehicle traveling
through an alley, or which may obstruct a sidewalk or street or other public grounds. Additionally, sidewalks
must have a height clearance of eight feet; streets and alleys must have 15 feet of overhead clearance.
(Ordinance 1674, sec. I, adopted 11/24/15)
Secs. 48-68—48-90. Reserved.
ARTICLE IV. SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION AND REPAIR
Sec. 48-91. Resolution ordering construction.
The city commission whenever in its opinion the interests of the public demand the construction of sidewalks
along and upon any street and whenever in its opinion the construction of such sidewalks will enhance the
value of the lot, block, or tract along and in front of which it is constructed, in a sum at least equal to the cost
and expense of constructing such sidewalk, may, by resolution, order the construction of sidewalks along any
street or any part of a street under the provisions of this article, and such resolution shall particularly describe
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 130/283
the streets, or parts of streets, along and upon which said sidewalk shall be constructed, and shall designate
the lots, blocks, or tracts, along or in front of which such sidewalk shall be constructed. (1969 Code, sec. 23-62;
Ordinance 224, sec. 7, adopted 8/13/1907)
Sec. 48-92. Notice to owner to construct-Publication.
(a) Upon the passage of such resolution as is provided for in section 48-91, the city secretary may cause
notice thereof to be published in one issue of the official newspaper of the city, which notice in addition to the
facts set out in the resolution shall state that if the sidewalk is not constructed by the owners of said lots or
blocks, within 90 days after publication of such notice, such sidewalk will be constructed by the city and the cost
and expense thereof charged against and collected from the owners of said lots, and shall also be a lien on the
lots.
(b) The publisher of the official newspaper shall make an affidavit of the publication of said notice and attach
a printed copy thereof to the same and file the same among the papers with the city secretary, and such
affidavit shall be prima facie evidence of the publication of said notice.
(1969 Code, sec. 23-63; Ordinance 224, sec. 8, adopted 8/13/1907)
Sec. 48-93. Same-Personal service requirement; form.
The city secretary shall likewise issue and cause to be served on the owner of any lot or property described in
the resolution, if known, and if his residence can be ascertained, a written notice. (1969 Code, sec. 23-64;
Ordinance 224, sec. 9, adopted 8/13/1907)
Sec. 48-94. Same-Effecting service; return.
The notice required by section 48-93 may be served by any police officer by delivering a true copy thereof to
such owner in person, if a resident or is to be found in the city, or by leaving such copy with any agent of such
owner, who may control the lots referred to for him. The person serving the notice shall make his return
thereon, in writing, showing how and when he served the same, which shall be filed with the city secretary. If
the owner cannot be served in the manner as set out in this section, the city secretary, if such owner's address
is known, shall mail to him at said address a copy of the notice and shall make and file his affidavit to the fact
that he has so mailed him said notice. However, if for any reason any owner cannot be served with the notice in
any of the ways provided in this section, the publication of said notice provided for in section 48-92 in the official
paper shall be deemed as full legal notice to him. (1969 Code, sec. 23-65; Ordinance 224, sec. 10, adopted
8/13/1907)
Sec. 48-95. Construction by city on failure of owner.
Should the owner of any lot or block fail to construct the sidewalk as ordered by the resolution of the city
commission and within the time required, at the expiration of said time the city may by order of the commission
construct such sidewalks, either by buying material and employing labor to do the work or by letting the same
out by contract, as the commission may deem will be the more economical method of doing the work. (1969
Code, sec. 23-66; Ordinance 224, sec. 11, adopted 8/13/1907)
Sec. 48-96. Performing construction and reporting costs.
The city shall as speedily as practical construct or cause the sidewalk to be constructed in accordance with the
provisions of this article, the officer in charge to report the cost and expense thereof to the commission in
writing, stating separately the cost of the sidewalk abutting each lot and the amount assessed against each
owner. (1969 Code, sec. 23-67; Ordinance 224, sec. 12, adopted 8/13/1907)
Sec. 48-97. Construction to comply with article.
All sidewalks hereafter constructed along and upon any street within the city shall be constructed in accordance
with, and conform to, the requirements and conditions as set forth in this article. (1969 Code, sec. 23-68;
Ordinance 224, sec. 1, adopted 8/13/1907)
Sec. 48-98. Supervision; conformity to grade; establishing grade upon application.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 131/283
All sidewalks which may hereafter be constructed along and upon any street within the city shall be constructed
under the supervision, superintendence, and to the satisfaction of the city commission or designated city officer;
and all such sidewalks shall be constructed in strict conformity to the grade of the street upon which it is being
constructed as then established by the city commission, or under its direction; provided any person desiring to
construct a sidewalk upon and along any street the grade of which street has not then been established shall
apply to the city commission to have the grade of such street established, and the commission shall forthwith
cause the grade of such street to be regularly established at the cost and expense of the city. When such grade
is so established, such sidewalk shall be constructed in strict conformity therewith. (1969 Code, sec. 23-69;
Ordinance 224, sec. 2, adopted 8/13/1907)
Sec. 48-99. Slope.
All sidewalks hereafter constructed along and upon any street within the city shall have a uniform slope of one
inch in every six feet sloping towards the center of the street from the lot, block or tract line along which it is
constructed to the outside edge thereof. (1969 Code, sec. 23-70; Ordinance 224, sec. 3, adopted 8/13/1907)
Sec. 48-100. Minimum widths.
Unless a different width is specified in the resolution ordering sidewalk construction as hereinafter provided, all
sidewalks hereafter constructed shall be the width prescribed by the city commission. (1969 Code, sec. 23-71;
Ordinance 224, sec. 4, adopted 8/13/1907; Ordinance 272 adopted 2/15/1911)
Sec. 48-101. Construction at owner's expense; charge on land and debt of owner.
All sidewalks constructed along and upon any street shall be constructed by the owner of the lots, blocks, or
tracts along or in front of which such sidewalk is constructed and required as herein provided; and at the cost
and expense of such owners, and, if constructed by the city under and in accordance with the provisions of this
article, the reasonable cost and expense of constructing such sidewalk:
(1) Shall be a valid and subsisting charge and debt against such owners of such lots, blocks, or
tracts along or in front of which such sidewalk is constructed;
(2) Shall be personal debts against such owners; and
(3) Shall, in all cases where permitted by law to secure its payment, be a valid lien and charge
against and upon such lots, blocks, or tracts along or in front of which such sidewalk is constructed
to the extent of the amount of increased value of such lots, blocks, or tracts by reason of the
construction of such sidewalk.
(1969 Code, sec. 23-72; Ordinance 224, sec. 5, adopted 8/13/1907)
Sec. 48-102. Specifications.
All sidewalks hereafter constructed along and upon any street within the city shall be constructed of concrete or
as otherwise ordered by resolution of the commission in such manner as to furnish a reasonably smooth and
hard surface, and where constructed of concrete shall be constructed substantially in accordance with the
specifications prescribed by the city commission. (1969 Code, sec. 23-73; Ordinance 224, sec. 6, adopted
8/13/1907)
Sec. 48-103. Resolution assessing cost.
Upon receipt of the report the city commission shall by a resolution passed by a two-thirds vote of all its
members, the vote to be entered on the minutes, assess against each owner of said lots the cost of
constructing the sidewalks along and in front of the lots, and shall declare the same a lien on said lots. (1969
Code, sec. 23-74; Ordinance 224, sec. 13, adopted 8/13/1907)
Sec. 48-104. Collecting assessments.
If the amount assessed against any such person is not paid within 20 days after the passing of said resolution,
it is the duty of the city attorney, or any other attorney employed by the commission for the purpose, and they
are hereby authorized:

https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 132/283
(1) To bring suit in the name of the city in any court having jurisdiction thereof against each of said
persons so failing to pay the amount assessed against them in said 20 days;
(2) To recover against each of them the amount so assessed against each of them; and
if in the opinion of such attorney there is a valid lien against any lot to secure the same, then to foreclose the
same and to prosecute the suits to final judgment, and to collect and receive any sums so recovered and pay
the same into the city treasury, taking the treasurer's receipt therefor, and such sums shall be credited to the
street fund.
(1969 Code, sec. 23-75; Ordinance 224, sec. 14, adopted 8/13/1907)
Sec. 48-105. Repair-Order to owner.
Whenever any sidewalk shall become broken or otherwise out of repair, the city shall cause a written or printed
notice to be served on the owner or the agent of the owner or the person in possession of the premises
adjacent to said broken sidewalk, requiring the same to be repaired within a reasonable time to be mentioned
therein. (1969 Code, sec. 23-76; Ordinance 224, sec. 17, adopted 8/13/1907)
Sec. 48-106. Same-Performance by city; assessment of cost.
In any case where any owner, agent, or occupant cannot be found or refuses or fails to repair any sidewalk
pursuant to the notice within a reasonable time, the city shall repair the same, and the cost to be assessed and
collected in the same manner as provided in sections 48-101 through 48-104, in case new sidewalks are built
by the city. (1969 Code, sec. 23-77; Ordinance 224, sec. 18, adopted 8/13/1907)
Secs. 48-107—48-125. Reserved.
ARTICLE V. STREET PAVING ASSESSMENT
Sec. 48-126. Assessment policy.
(a) When the public works director receives a request for a street paving assessment from a property owner,
then a petition shall be prepared in accordance to an engineer's estimate. The cost of preparing the engineer's
estimate shall not cost the city.
(b) The petition must be signed by at least 60 percent of the abutting property owners.
(c) Costs of the paving project shall include:
(1) All street construction costs including street intersections, alley ways, curb and gutter and
drainage structures;
(2) Engineering fees associated with the paving project, and legal fees associated with the paving
assessments.
(d) Commission-approved bids or expenses of the paving project shall be shared with 75 percent by the
abutting property owners and 25 percent by the city.
(e) The actual costs shall be assessed against the abutting properties.
(f) Payment of the actual construction and other related costs are to be paid at the completion of the paving
project or the property owner may elect to sign a promissory note for 36 months at eight percent interest rate
with annual payments.
(1969 Code, sec. 23-91; Ordinance 1331, sec. 1, adopted 12/22/98)
Sec. 48-127. Street paving.
Nothing in this article will limit the city from paving any street at any time when approved by a majority vote of
the city commission.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 133/283
CHAPTER 50
TAXATION AND LICENSES*
ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL
Sec. 50-1. Additional penalty on delinquent taxes.
The city hereby adopts the provisions of V.T.C.A., Tax Code sec. 33.07 so that hereafter an additional penalty of
15 percent of the delinquent tax, penalty, and interest on delinquent taxes shall be imposed on taxes becoming
delinquent after January 31, 1983. (1969 Code, sec. 24-2; Ordinance 1020 adopted 3/8/83)
Sec. 50-2. Tax abatement policy, guidelines and criteria.
(a) Objective. The objective of this tax abatement program is to create new jobs, new capital investment, and
a broadened tax base for our community by:
(1) Providing an incentive for already established businesses to expand and/or modernize; and/or
(2) Providing an incentive to attract businesses that might not locate in our community otherwise.
The city may make exceptions to these guidelines at any time in order to fulfill the original purpose or intent.
(b) Candidate qualifications.
(1) Compliments existing businesses and/or increases the diversity of our community's economy
(2) Creates new jobs and capital investment as outlined in the following abatement schedule
(c) Abatement schedule. The amount and term of abatement will depend on the number of additional full-time
(or equivalent) jobs and/or the amount of capital investment according to schedule A.
Schedule A. Property Tax Abatement-City of Vernon

7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 135/283
Only the increase in fair market value of real property directly resulting from the development, redevelopment
and/or improvement specified in the abatement contract will be eligible for abatement. Tax abatement must
benefit the party making the investment; by ownership or by contract.
The construction period may not exceed two (2) years.
The number of additional full-time (or equivalent) jobs specified in the abatement contract should be maintained
for the entire term of the abatement and pay no less than federal minimum wages.
(d) Abatement committee. Upon receipt of an application for tax abatement, the mayor will create a tax
abatement advisory committee consisting of the mayor, city manager and a representative from each of all
other affected taxing jurisdictions.
Said committee shall sit as to inform each taxing unit as to the particulars of each application and to concur in
the advisory committee's recommendation to each taxing unit.
(e) Guidelines.
(1) Tax abatements may be provided for both new facilities and structures and for the expansion
or modernization of existing facilities and structures. Each project proposed for tax abatement shall
be considered individually on its own merits, benefit to the public, and in context of any other
economic incentives for the project or existing in the reinvestment zone.
(2) The developer, project owner, or other recipient of a tax abatement must annually certify in
writing to the city commission of each participating taxing unit that the developer, owner or recipient
is in compliance with each applicable term of the agreement.
(3) The taxable value of improvements to a site and the inventory, furniture, fixtures, and
equipment will qualify for tax abatement. The taxable value and any reevaluation of the land prior to
improvement will be subject to taxation at the applicable rates.
(4) A tax abatement agreement must ensure that the periods of abatement are directly
proportional to the capital expenditures for improvements and/or the number of permanent fulltime
jobs created.
(5) Expansion or modernization of existing facilities qualifies for tax abatement if the expansion
meets the qualifications for capital expenditures and/or nets new jobs. The number of jobs created
must be new jobs and not replacement of jobs, which were in the payroll within the year immediately
prior to application for tax abatement. A tax abatement shall not be granted if the facility has been
the subject of or included in a prior tax abatement agreement.
(6) If a new facility is constructed to replace an existing facility, and the existing facility is
abandoned by the developer, only the difference in taxable value of the new facility over the existing
facility will qualify for tax abatement.
(7) An agreement will be executed by the developer which incorporates the terms of this section
and includes any other site and development specific terms, which might be found applicable at the
time.
(8) The tax abatement agreement will require, among other things, that the city will have the right
of access to the site and books and records of the applicant for tax abatement to determine
compliance with statutory requirements and the agreement. Failure to fulfill any of the requirements
of the agreement will result in cancellation of the agreement and retroactive loss of tax abatement.
(Ordinance 1560, secs. 1—4, adopted 5/24/11; Ordinance 1572, secs. 1-6, adopted 10/25/11; Ordinance 1603,
sec. 2, adopted 12/18/12)
Editor's note- Ordinance 1560, adopted May 25, 2011, repealed sec. 50-2, in its entirety. Sections 1-4 of said
ordinance, adopted new provisions to read as herein set out. Prior to this amendment, sec. 50-2 pertained to
criteria for tax abatement within reinvestment zones. See Code Comparative Table for derivation.
Sec. 50-3. Commercial filming.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 136/283
Persons seeking commercial use of city-owned property (streets, rights-of-way, parks, public buildings),
commercial use of private property which may affect adjacent public or private property, and the use of city
equipment and personnel in the filming of movies, TV shows, commercials, and related activities, must obtain
authorization of the city manager and obtain permits and pay fees according to the terms of the commercial
filming application. (Ordinance 1517 adopted 6/23/09)
Sec. 50-4. Chapter 380 incentive policy.
(a) Under these guidelines, to be eligible for consideration by the city for chapter 380 economic development
incentives, a company or project must meet and/or exceed all of the criteria, as described below:
(1) Minimum amounts of real and personal property investments must be achieved as outlined in
section 50-6.
(2) Minimum levels of full-time job creation or retention must be achieved as determined by the
city commission.
(b) The amount and term of the chapter 380 economic development incentive will also be impacted by:
(1) The location of the facility;
(2) Other incentives used for the same project; and
(3) Overall benefit to the community
(Ordinance 1640, sec. 1, adopted 6/2/14)
Sec. 50-5. Chapter 380 requirements.
(a) Either the project:
(1) Results in a minimum increased taxable value for the city of $5,000.00 in real and business
personal property; or
(2) Will result in a minimum increased taxable value for the city of $5,000.00 in real and business
personal property; or
(3) Is specifically determined by the city commission to bring extraordinary benefit to the city.
(b) A project shall not be eligible for incentives under this article if building permit has been issued for the
project prior to making application in accordance with this article.
(c) Incentives established under this program will be provided only to the extent that the revenues realized by
the city and attributable to a project exceeds a minimum amount established by agreement. The public benefit
or amount of revenue realized by the city and attributable to the project must be commensurate with value of
any incentives granted under this program.
(Ordinance 1640, sec. 1, adopted 6/2/14)
Sec. 50-6. Chapter 380 exceptional investment projects.
(a) A project will be considered an “exceptional investment” if the project has a total capital investment (real
property improvements and new personal property investments) of at least $5,000,000.00 in the property of
interest; and/or
(b) Creation and maintenance of at least 50 new, full-time, permanent jobs at the property of interest.
(Ordinance 1640, sec. 1, adopted 6/2/14)
Sec. 50-7. Chapter 380 agreement terms.
An agreement established for a program must include:
