https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 187/283
CHAPTER 54
UTILITIES*
ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL
Secs. 54-1—54-18. Reserved.
ARTICLE II. LIQUID WASTE DISPOSAL
Sec. 54-19. Penalties.
(a) Any violation of the provisions of this article shall constitute an offense and shall be punishable by a fine
of more than $2,000.00. Each instance of violation shall constitute a separate offense.
(b) Disposal of any liquid or semisolid wastes as described in this article at any location without authorization
from the wastewater treatment department shall be a violation of this article and shall be punishable by a fine of
not more than $2,000.00. Each instance of violation shall constitute a separate offense.
(c) Any person who disposes of wastes at the city wastewater treatment plant which causes harm to the
plant, creates a hazard to humans or animals, causes a violation of Texas Pollutant Discharge Elimination
System (TPDES) or state discharge permits, or interferes with the use and disposal of sludge, shall be subject
to being banned from disposal of wastes at the city wastewater treatment plant.
(d) A director, officer, employee or other person authorized to act in behalf of a corporation or association
having primary responsibility for the discharge of a duty to act imposed by law on a corporation or association is
criminally responsible for a violation under this article to the same extent as if such person were criminally
responsible under this article.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-52; Ordinance 1354, sec. 6, adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-20. Permit required.
No person shall engage in the business of collection, transportation, and disposal, or any of them, of liquid or
semisolid wastes from septic tanks, cesspools, chemical toilets, grease traps, sand and mud traps, or other
similar activity within the city or its extraterritorial jurisdiction without a permit from the state natural resource
conservation commission for each vehicle used in such activity. No person may dispose of such wastes in the
city's sanitary wastewater system without such a permit. (1969 Code, sec. 26-47; Ordinance 1354, sec. 1,
adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-21. Operation requirements.
A permit holder under this article shall take all reasonable measures to prevent hazards to health, which can
arise from operations within the scope of this article and shall be subject to the following requirements:
(1) No material taken from a septic tank, cesspool, chemical toilet, sewage seepage pit, privy,
grease trap, sand and mud trap or other liquid or semisolid waste container shall be disposed of
other than in a manner and place approved by the wastewater treatment department.
(2) Tanks on such vehicles shall have the capacity of the tank indicated with two-inch numerals on
the side of the tank.
(3) No vehicle or auxiliary equipment used for carrying, transporting, or handling the wastes as
described herein shall be allowed to stand or remain overnight within 100 feet of an occupied
premises; nor shall the loading and unloading of such vehicles and the transportation thereof
through any street, place, or premises consume an unreasonable period of time.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-48; Ordinance 1354, sec. 2, adopted 10/24/00)
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 188/283
Sec. 54-22. Acceptable wastes.
(a) Only domestic septic wastes or other specifically permitted wastes may be disposed of at the city
wastewater treatment plants.
(b) All other wastes as described herein shall be disposed of in a state and federal approved site.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-49; Ordinance 1354, sec. 3, adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-23. Waste control records.
Any person who collects, transports, and disposes of waste as described in this article shall maintain a record
of each collection and each deposit on a manifest trip ticket form approved by the state. The manifest shall
include:
(1) Name, address, telephone, and commission registration number of transporter;
(2) Name, signature, address, and phone number of person who generated the waste and the
date collected;
(3) Type and amount of waste collected or transported;
(4) Name and signature of responsible person collecting, transporting, and depositing the waste;
(5) Date and place where the waste was deposited;
(6) Identification (permit or site registration number, location, and operator) of the facility where
the waste was deposited;
(7) Name and signature of facility on-site representative acknowledging receipt of the waste and
the amount of waste received; and
(8) The volume of the grease and grit trap or the septic tank deposited.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-50; Ordinance 1354, sec. 4, adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-24. Disposal charge for liquid waste disposal.
(a) A disposal charge will be assessed each time that wastes as described in this article are deposited.
(1) For septic loads originating in Wilbarger County the minimum fee per 500 gallons or less will
be $35.00 per load.
Loads over 500 gallons will be charged $35.00 for the first 500 gallons plus $7.00 per 100 gallons
in excess of 500 gallons.
(2) For septic loads originating in Archer, Baylor, Foard, Hardeman or Wichita County the
minimum fee per 500 gallons or less will be $70.00 per load.
Loads over 500 gallons will be charged $70.00 for the first 500 gallons plus $14.00 per 100
gallons in excess of 500 gallons.
(3) For septic loads originating from Childress, Clay, Cottle, Haskell, Jack, King, Knox,
Throckmorton or Young County the minimum fee per 500 gallons or less will be $140.00 per load.
Loads over 500 gallons will be charged $140.00 for the first 500 gallons plus $28.00 per 100
gallons in excess of 500 gallons.
(4) Septic loads originating from counties other than those listed above may be accepted only by
approval from the public works director at a negotiated rate.
(b) Disposal may be made after normal operating hours at the city wastewater treatment plant for an
additional charge of $100.00 per load.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 189/283
(c) The charges shall be payable to the city within ten days after such charge is rendered.
(d) If any charge for disposal services is not paid within ten days after such charge is rendered, the city shall
charge and collect an additional service charge in the amount of ten percent of the net amount of such charge.
(e) Any person who shall fail or refuse to pay the charge herein specified within 15 days from the date it shall
have become due and payable shall have his disposal privileges suspended.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-51; Ordinance 1354, sec. 5, adopted 10/24/00; Ordinance 1610, sec. 1, adopted 3/26/13)
Secs. 54-25—54-51. Reserved.
ARTICLE III. SEWERS
Sec. 54-52. Definitions.
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in
this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:
Commercial class means those users which have three or more living units served by a single water meter, or
which have one or more businesses served by a single water meter.
Industrial class means those users whose wastewater results from a product manufactured, processed or
fabricated by the customer.
Living unit means a residential unit providing dwelling facilities for one family, including permanent provisions
for living, sleeping, cooking, eating, and sanitation.
Normal sewage has the same meaning as normal strength wastewater, as defined in article IV of this chapter.
Residential class means those users who have no more than two living units served by a single meter.
User has the meaning provided in article IV of this chapter.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-77; Ordinance 1356, sec. 1, adopted 9/26/00)
Sec. 54-53. Sewer cleaning services.
(a) City personnel are hereby authorized to perform sewer cleaning services on privately owned sewer piping
of industrial and public institutions that are utility customers of the city. The charge for such sewer cleaning
services is as follows: minimum $100.00 per hour or fraction thereof after the first four hours. The private
industries or public institutions that receive these municipal performed sewer cleaning services shall agree to
indemnify and hold harmless the city against all claims, demands, suits, judgments, costs, or expenses arising
from such loss or injury.
(b) City personnel are not authorized to perform sewer cleaning services on residential or nonindustrial
privately owned sewer piping.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-68; Ordinance 437, sec. 60, adopted 12/17/26; Ordinance 1319, secs. 1, 2, adopted
6/23/98)
Sec. 54-54. Sewer system use required for adjacent property.
It shall be unlawful for any person when living on property abutting or adjoining any street or alley upon which
sanitary sewer pipes have been laid, to throw or allow to be thrown or deposited on the surface of the ground,
or in any hole, cesspool or vault in or under the surface of the ground, or in any place other than the sanitary
sewer system, after authorized connection, except the proper fertilizing of the soil, any water which has been
used for domestic purposes or any liquids or solid filth, feces, or urine. (1969 Code, sec. 26-69; Ordinance 245,
sec. 1, adopted 10/15/09)
Sec. 54-55. Connections-Applications.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 190/283
Applications for connection with the city sewer system, must be made in writing by the owner of the property to
be connected, or by his authorized agent. Such application shall give the precise location of the property, the
type of service desired and the name of the owner, and shall be made on blanks furnished for the purpose.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-70; Ordinance 437, sec. 5, adopted 12/17/26)
Sec. 54-56. Same-Tapping fee.
The tapping fee for connection with the sewer system shall be $2.00. (1969 Code, sec. 26-71; Ordinance
adopted 12/9/52, sec. 4)
Sec. 54-57. Same-Compliance before issuance of permit.
Permits to make connections with the sewer system will be issued only when the plumbing in the house or
building to be connected is in accordance with the plumbing code. (1969 Code, sec. 26-72; Ordinance 437, sec.
5, adopted 12/17/26)
Sec. 54-58. Same-Designating “Y” branch position; connection under city supervision.
The city will designate the position of the “Y” branch in the street, as shown by the records in the city hall. All
connections made with the sanitary sewers or drains shall be made under the direction of the city. (1969 Code,
sec. 26-73; Ordinance 437, sec. 5, adopted 12/17/26; Ordinance adopted 12/9/52, sec. 5)
Sec. 54-59. Same-Old plumbing.
Before any old private or other drain shall be connected with the sewer system, the owner of any such drain or
sewer shall prove to the satisfaction of the city that it is clean and conforms in every respect with the city rules
and regulations. (1969 Code, sec. 26-74; Ordinance 437, sec. 13, adopted 12/17/26)
Sec. 54-60. Damaging system.
(a) No person willfully or negligently break, damage, uncover, deface, or tamper with any of the city's
wastewater system facilities or equipment which is a part of the city's wastewater system.
(b) No person, without the expressed authorization of the city, shall discharge wastes into any part of the
wastewater system. Any violation of this section shall constitute an offense punishable as provided in section 1-
6 for each violation.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-75; Ordinance 437, sec. 10, adopted 12/17/26; Ordinance 1354, sec. 7, adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-61. Private system discharges.
The city shall have power to stop and prevent from discharging into the sewer system any private sewer or
drain. (1969 Code, sec. 26-76; Ordinance 437, sec. 12, adopted 12/17/26)
Sec. 54-62. Rate schedules.
Every user whose premises are served by a connection with the wastewater system of the city, whereby the
wastewater is disposed of by the city, shall pay a service charge as follows:
(1) All users located inside the corporate boundary limits shall pay a monthly service charge of
$35.45.
(2) All residential class users with two living units shall pay an additional monthly service charge of
$26.60 for a total of $62.05.
(3) A monthly service charge shall also be charged to all users in the amount of $2.45 per 1,000
gallons of water used after the first 1,000 gallons, or $2.45 per 1,000 gallons of wastewater
produced, as more specifically set forth hereinafter.
(A) The monthly volume charges for residential class users will be based on the individual
user's average monthly water use during the preceding winter quarter months of December,
January, and February. The volumes used to compute these charges are based on the amount
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 191/283
of water used by the residential class user as measured by a water meter. Where no preceding
winter quarter average is available from records, the finance director shall estimate a volume to
be used for this monthly volume charge, such estimate to be the current system-wide
residential average.
(B) The monthly volume charge to all other users will be based on the total water use as
measured by appropriate meters except as by subsection d. below.
(C) Users, other than residential class users, connected to the wastewater system who have
a source of water supply that is in addition to, or in lieu of, the city supply, must have a meter
approved and tested by the city for that source of supply and the volume charge as set forth
herein above shall be based on the sum of the volumes delivered by all sources of water
supply except as by subsection e. below.
(D) Users, other than residential class users, may install an approved meter on the
wastewater discharge, or use other approved methods to determine actual wastewater flows,
and be charged per 1,000 gallons of wastewater produced as set forth herein above.
(E) Residential class users connected to the wastewater system who have a water source in

equal to the current system-wide residential average.
(F) The monthly volume charge for industrial class users will be based on an approved
meter of $2.45 per 1,000 gallons of wastewater produced.
(G) The monthly charges for industrial class users who discharge other than normal strength
wastewater shall be charged, in addition to volume charge of $2.45, a surcharge for BOD and
TSS, as defined in article V of this chapter. The surcharges for BOD and TSS are $0.17 per
pound and $0.17 per pound respectively that are above the limits, as set in article IV of this
chapter.

Sec. 54-63. Monthly billing.
(a) The wastewater service charge shall be billed monthly in conjunction with the billing of water and
sanitation service charges.
(b) Any user, who shall fail to pay any authorized wastewater service charge within the time limit prescribed
for the payment of water, sewer and sanitation bills shall have his water line disconnected from the city's water
system. Water service shall not be restored until the user has paid all amounts due and in arrears and the water
reconnecting charge provided for in section 54-154.
(c) Any user, who shall fail to pay any authorized wastewater service charge within the time limit prescribed
for the payment of water, sewer and sanitation bills shall be subject to having his wastewater service line
disconnected from the city wastewater system. Wastewater service shall not be restored until the user shall
have paid all amounts due and in arrears and the actual cost of the disconnection and reconnection. The
estimated cost of the disconnection and reconnection shall be deposited with the city before the reconnection is
made.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-79; Ordinance 1354, sec. 8, adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-64. Determining bill in special cases; measuring actual discharge.
Water usage by commercial or industrial customers in excess of 50,000 gallons per month may be reviewed by
the director of utilities for in-plant consumption. (1969 Code, sec. 26-80; Ordinance 1354, sec. 9, adopted
10/24/00)
