Sec. 54-65. Powers, authority of enforcing agents.
The duly authorized employees of the city presenting proper identification may enter upon all properties with the
consent of the owner or occupant or upon compliance with law if permission is refused, for the purposes of
inspection, observations measurement, sampling, and testing, in accordance with any provisions of this
chapter. Only in the event of an emergency affecting life, public health or property may private property be
entered without consent or without a search warrant. (1969 Code, sec. 26-81; Code 1969, sec. 26-81;
Ordinance 1354, sec. 10, adopted 10/24/00)
Secs. 54-66—54-88. Reserved.
ARTICLE IV. DISCHARGE OF INDUSTRIAL WASTES
Sec. 54-89. Definitions.
Unless the context specially indicates otherwise, the following terms and phrases, as used in this article, shall
have the meanings designated in this section:
Abnormal sewage means any industrial wastewater having a pollutant content in excess of that found in the
definition of “normal waste.”
Approval authority means the executive director of the Texas Natural Resource Conservation Commission, or
his duly designated representative.
Authorized representative of industrial user means an authorized representative of an industrial user may be a
principal executive officer of at least the level of vice-president, if the industrial user is a corporation; a general
partner or proprietor if the industrial user is a partnership or proprietorship, respectively; a duly authorized
representative of the individual designated in this definition if such representative is responsible for the overall
operation of the facilities from which the indirect discharge originates.
Biochemical oxygen demand (BOD) means the quantity of oxygen utilized in the biochemical oxidation of
organic matter under laboratory procedures in five days at 20 degrees Celsius, expressed in milligrams per liter
by weight. The methodology shall follow EPA approved methods.
Building drain means that part of the lowest horizontal piping of a drainage system which receives the
discharge from soil waste, and other drainage pipes inside the walls of the building and conveys it to the
building sewer, beginning three feet outside the inner face of the building wall.
Building sewer means the extension from the building drain to the public sewer or other place of disposal.
Categorical pretreatment standard or pretreatment standard means any regulation containing pollutant
discharge limits promulgated by the EPA in accordance with section 307(b) and (c) of the Act (33 USC 1317(b),
(c)) which applies to a specific category of industrial user.
Categorical standards means national categorical pretreatment standards or pretreatment standard, as
referenced by 40 CFR 403.
Chief operator means the chief operator of wastewater treatment of the city or his authorized deputy, agent or
representative.
City manager means the city manager of the City of Vernon, Texas, or his authorized agent or representative.
Composite sample means a mixture of grab samples collected at the same sample point at different times. A
flow-composite sample takes into account the variation in flow of the sample stream at the different times of
collection.
Control authority means the person employed as utilities director for the city or his authorized representative.
Direct discharge means the discharge of treated or untreated wastewater directly to the waters of the state.
Director means the person employed as utilities director for the city or his authorized representative.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 193/283
Environmental Protection Agency or EPA means the United States Environmental Protection Agency or, where
appropriate, the term may also be used as a designation for the administrator or other duly authorized official of
such agency.
Fats, oils and greases (FOG) means any material including biological and mineral hydrocarbons measured in
any EPA approved FOG method. Any FOG sample must be a grab sample.
Garbage means solid wastes from the preparation, cooking, and dispensing of food, and from the handling,
storage or sale of produce.
Grab sample means a sample that is taken from a waste stream on a one-time basis with no regard to the flow
in the waste stream and without consideration of time.
Holding tank waste means any waste from holding tanks such as vessels, chemical toilets, campers, trailers,
septic tanks, and vacuum-pump tank trucks.
Indirect discharge means the discharge or the introduction of nondomestic pollutants from any source regulated
under section 307(b) and (c) of the Act (33 USC 1317(b), (c)), into the POTW, including holding tank waste
discharged into the system.
Industrial user means a source of indirect discharge.
Industrial waste means the water-borne solids, liquid or gaseous wastes from industrial manufacturing
processes, trade or business as distinguished from sanitary sewage.
Interference means the inhibition or disruption of the POTW treatment processes or operations, may contribute
to a violation of any requirement of the city's TPDES permit. The term “interference” includes prevention of
sewage sludge use or disposal by the POTW in accordance with section 405 of the Act (33 USC 1345) or any
criteria, guidelines or regulations developed pursuant to the Solid Waste Disposal Act (SWDA), the Clean Air
Act, the Toxic Substances Control Act, or more stringent state criteria (including those contained in any state
sludge management plan prepared pursuant to title IV of SWDA) applicable to the method of disposal or use
employed by the POTW.
Milligrams per liter (mg/l) means the concentration by weight per unit volume of liquid, also parts per million.
National prohibitive discharge standard or prohibitive discharge standard means any regulation developed
under the authority of section 307(b) of the Act and 40 CFR 403.5.
Natural outlet means any outlet into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake, or other body of surface water or
groundwater.
New source means any source, the construction of which is commenced after the publication of proposed
regulations prescribing a section 307(c) (33 USC 1317(c)) categorical pretreatment standard which will be
applicable to such source, if such standard is thereafter promulgated. The term “new source” includes the
conditions of 40 CFR 403.3(k), as amended.
Normal strength wastewater means wastewater having a maximum BOD of 300 mg/l, a maximum TSS of 300
mg/l, a maximum TOC of 200 mg/l, a maximum FOG of 100 mg/l, and a maximum TPH of 20 mg/l. The quantity
of other pollutants shall be those values determined in the latest domestic waste survey,
Pass through means a discharge which exits the POTW into waters of the United States in quantities or
concentrations which, alone or in conjunction with a discharge from other sources, is a cause of a violation of
any requirement of the POTW's TPDES permit (including an increase in the magnitude or duration of a
violation).
pH means the logarithm (base 10) of the reciprocal of the concentration of hydrogen ions measured in grams
per liter of solution. Any pH sample must be a grab sample.
Pollutant means any dredged spoil, solid waste, incinerator residue, sewage, garbage, sewage sludge,
munitions, chemical wastes, biological materials, radioactive materials, heat, wrecked or discharged equipment,
rock, sand, cellar dirt, and industrial, municipal and agricultural waste discharged into water.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 194/283
Pollution means the manmade or man-induced alteration of the chemical, physical, biological, and radiological
integrity of water.
Pretreatment or treatment means the reduction of the amount of pollutants, the elimination of pollutants, or the
alteration of the nature of pollutant properties in wastewater to a less harmful state prior to or in lieu of
discharging or otherwise introducing such pollutants into a POTW. The reduction or alteration can be obtained
by physical, chemical or biological processes, or by process changes and other means, except as prohibited by
40 CFR 4036(d).
Pretreatment requirements means any substantive or procedural requirement related to pretreatment, other
than a national pretreatment standard imposed on an industrial user.
Properly shredded garbage means the waste from the preparation, cooking or dispensing of food that have
been shredded to such degree that all particles will be carried freely under the flow conditions normally
prevailing in public sewers, with no particle greater than one-half-inch in any dimension.
Publicly owned treatment works (POTW) means the city's wastewater treatment works designed to provide
treatment to wastewater.
Sanitary sewer means a sewer that carries wastewater and to which stormwaters, surface waters and
groundwaters are not intentionally admitted.
Sewer means a pipe or conduit for carrying wastewater.
Shall, when used in the context of this article, connotes a mandatory requirement; the term “may,” in contrast, is
permissive.
Significant industrial user (SIU) means:
(1) All industrial users subject to categorical pretreatment standards under 40 CFR 403.6 or 40
CFR 405-471; and
(2) Any other industrial user that discharges an average of 25,000 gallons per day or more of
process wastewater to the POTW (excluding sanitary, noncontact cooling up five percent or more of
the average dry weather hydraulic or organic capacity of the POTW treatment plant; or is designated
as such by the control authority as defined in 40 CFR 403.12(a) on the basis that the industrial user
has a reasonable potential for adversely affecting the POTW's operation or for violating any
pretreatment standard or requirement (in accordance with 40 CFR 403.8(f)(6)).
Slug load means any discharge of a nonroutine episodic nature, including but not limited to an accidental spill
or a noncustomary batch discharge.
Standard industrial classification (SIC) means a classification pursuant to the Standard Industrial Classification
Manual issued by the Executive Office of the President, Office of Management and Budget, Latest Edition.
State means the State of Texas.
Storm water means any flow occurring during or following any form of natural precipitation and resulting
therefrom.
Texas Natural Resource Conservation Commission means the state agency delegated the responsibility of
TPDES permitting system and enforcing the Clean Water Act or other acts and regulations promulgated by the
Environmental Protection Agency.
Texas Pollution Discharge Elimination System or TPDES permit means a permit issued pursuant to section 402
of the Act (33 USC 1342).
Total suspended solids (TSS) means the total suspended matter that floats on the surface of (or is suspended
in) water, wastewater or other liquids, and which is removable by laboratory filtering per EPA approved method.
Toxic pollutant means any pollutant or combination of pollutants listed as toxic in regulations promulgated by
the Environmental Protection Agency under the provisions of the Clean Water Act 307(a) or other acts.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 195/283
User means any person who contributes, causes or permits the contribution of wastewater into the city's
POTW.
Waste means anything left over, not needed or superfluous as an excess material or byproduct.
Wastewater means the liquid and water-carried industrial or domestic wastes from dwellings, commercial
buildings, industrial facilities, and institutions, together with any groundwater, surface water, and stormwater
that may be present, whether treated or untreated, which is contributed into or permitted to enter the POTW.
Watercourse means a channel in which a flow of water occurs, either continuously or intermittently.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-89; Ordinance 1354, sec. 11, adopted 10/24/00; Ordinance 1638, sec. 1, adopted 6/24/14)
Sec. 54-90. Penalties.
(a) All industrial users discharging wastewater to the city's POTW are required to be in compliance with the
applicable provisions of the EPA's Pretreatment Rule before discharging into the city's POTW. A copy of the
Pretreatment Rule, in its entirety, can be obtained from the EPA's website.
Those industries and/or businesses not meeting compliance, or not possessing an industrial wastewater
discharge permit issued by the city will be denied access to the city's wastewater collection system, nor will they
be conditionally allowed to discharge to the POTW, in addition a penalty will be assessed for not meeting these
requirements.
Industry users discharging or desiring to discharge into the city's wastewater collection/wastewater treatment
plant will be permitted to do so, but under specific permit conditions only. The industrial wastewater discharge
permit must be developed by a registered professional engineer retained by the city.
(b) Penalties for exceeding permitted effluent limits will result when specific permitted effluent limits are not
met, and/or the occurrence results in an interference or pass through at the POTW, and such violation is likely
to recur, then the following corrective actions will be taken against the industrial user:
(1) First offense: The industrial user is required to submit a corrective action plan addressing the
cause for each permitted effluent limit failure. The corrective action plan must directly address the
cause of the failure, and provide a schedule for completing the action(s) necessary for correcting the
failure, and the corrective action plan must meet the approval of the POTW chief operator and the
city public works director.
(2) Second offense: The industrial user will be issued a notice of violation (NOV), and will be
expected to immediately take corrective action(s) to eliminate the cause of the failure. The NOV will
be issued by the public works director direct to the manager of the facility that is in violation. In the
event the manager does not accept the NOV, then the facility will be placed into enforcement with
penalties not to exceed $1,000.00 per day per offense. The facility manager may appeal to the city
commission, at their next regular meeting, who may consider the circumstances and validity of the
facility being fined. The city commission's ruling will be final.
(3) Third offense. The industrial user will be fined up to $500.00 per day per violation.
(4) Fourth offense. The industrial user's wastewater discharge permit will be revoked (per section
54-106).
(c) Criminal penalties. Any user who is found to have violated an order of the public works director or who
has willfully, knowingly or with criminal negligence failed to comply with any provision of this article or the
orders, rules, regulations and permits issued hereunder, shall be fined in an amount not to exceed $2,000.00
for each offense. Each day on which a violation shall occur or continue shall be deemed a separate and distinct
offense.
(d) Falsifying information. Any person who knowingly makes any false statement, representation or
certification in any application, record, report, plan or other document filed or required to be maintained
pursuant to this article, or industrial waste permit, or who falsifies, tampers with or knowingly renders inaccurate
any monitoring device or method required under this article shall, upon conviction, be punished by a fine as
provided in subsection (a) of this section.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 196/283
(e) Corporate responsibility. A director, officer, employee or other person authorized to act on behalf of a
corporation or association having responsibility for the discharge of a duty to act imposed by law on a
corporation or association is criminally responsible for a violation under this chapter to the same extent as if
such person were criminally responsible under this chapter.
(f) Public participation will be solicited before an industrial wastewater discharge permit is issued, or a permit
waiver is approved, to any part or whole thereof, to the permit. Public participation is required during the
development, and/or revision, of any regulation standard, effluent limitation, plan, or program established by the
administrator (EPA) or the Texas Commission on Environmental Quality (TCEQ) under the Clean Water Act,
Sec. 101(e). The director of public works will post such notices at City Hall for a period of at least one week,
and will advertise twice in a week, in the local newspaper, the notice will provide the name of the industrial user
making the request, his address and contact information, and also that of the director of public works, will be
provided on the notice so that anyone wishing to make comments, suggestions, or that may have questions,
may contact both, or either one, of these individuals and provide their input.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-99.7; Ordinance 1354, sec. 28, adopted 10/24/00; Ordinance 1638, sec. 1, adopted
6/24/14)
Sec. 54-91. Purpose and policy.
(a) This article sets forth uniform requirements for direct and indirect contributors into the wastewater
collection and treatment system for the city and enables the city to comply with all applicable state and federal
laws required by the Clean Water Act of 1977 and the general pretreatment regulations (40 CFR 403). The
objectives of this article are to:
(1) Prevent the introduction of pollutants into the city's wastewater system, which will interfere with
the operation of the system or contaminate the resulting sludge or final effluent, or both;
(2) Prevent the introduction of pollutants into the city's wastewater system which will pass through
the system, inadequately treated into receiving waters or the atmosphere or otherwise be
incompatible with the system; and
(3) Improve the opportunity to recycle and reclaim wastewater and sludge from the system.
(b) This article shall apply to all users of the city's sewer system. Except as otherwise provided herein, the
utilities director of the city shall administer, implement and enforce, or cause to be enforced, the provisions of
this article.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-90; Ordinance 1354, sec. 12 adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-92. Use of public sewers generally.
(a) No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any stormwater, surface water, groundwater, roof
runoff, or subsurface drainage to any sanitary sewer.
(b) Stormwater and all other unpolluted drainage shall be discharged to such sewers as are specifically
designated as storm sewers, or to a natural outlet approved by the director. Unpolluted industrial process
waters may be discharged, upon approval of the director, to a storm sewer, or natural outlet, or into the sanitary
sewer system upon prior written approval of the director. It shall be the responsibility of the city to monitor and
control the quality of all discharges to the storm sewer system.
(c) In cases where, and in the opinion of the director, the character of the wastewater from any manufacturer
or industrial plant, building or other premises is such that it will damage the system or cannot be treated
satisfactorily in the system, the director shall have the authority to require such user to dispose of such
wastewater otherwise, and prevent it from entering the system.
(d) The director shall have the authority to deny or condition any new or increased contributions.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-91; Ordinance 1354, sec. 13, adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-93. General discharge prohibitions.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 197/283
No user shall contribute or cause to be contributed, directly or indirectly, any pollutant or wastewater which will
interfere with the operation or performance of the POTW. A user shall not contribute the following substances to
any POTW:
(1) Pollutants which create a risk of fire or explosion in the POTW, including but not limited to
wastestreams with a closed cup flashpoint of less than 140 degrees Fahrenheit or 60 degrees
centigrade using the test methods specified in 40 CFR 261.21;
(2) Petroleum oil, nonbiodegradable cutting oil or products of mineral oil origin in amounts that will
cause interference or pass through;
(3) Any solid or viscous substances in amounts which may cause obstruction to the flow in a
sewer or other interference with the operation of the wastewater treatment facilities such as, but not
limited to, grease, garbage with particles greater than one-half inch in any dimension, animal guts or
tissues, paunch manure, bones, hair, hides or fleshings, entrails, whole blood, feathers, ashes,
cinders, spent lime, stone or marble dust, metal, glass, straw, shavings, grass clippings, rags, spent
grains, spent hops, waste paper, wood, plastics, gas, tar, asphalt residues from refining, or
processing of fuel or lubricating oil, mud or glass grinding or polishing wastes;
(4) Any wastewater having a pH less than 5.5 or more than ten, or wastewater having any other
corrosive property capable of causing damage or hazard to structures, equipment and/or personnel
of the POTW;
(5) Any wastewater containing toxic pollutants in sufficient quantity, either singly or by interaction
with other pollutants, to injure or interfere with any wastewater treatment process, constitute a
hazard to human beings or animals, create a toxic effect in the receiving waters of the POTW, or to
exceed the limitation set forth in a categorical pretreatment standard; a toxic pollutant shall include
but not be limited to any pollutant identified pursuant to section 307(a) of the Act;
(6) Any noxious or malodorous liquids, gases or solids which either singly or by interaction with
other wastes are sufficient to create a public nuisance or hazard to life or are sufficient to prevent
entry into a sewer for maintenance and repair;
(7) Any substance which may cause the POTW's effluent or any other product of the POTW such
as residues, sludges or scums, to be unsuitable for reclamation and reuse or to interfere with the
reclamation process. In no case shall a substance discharged to the POTW cause the POTW to be
in noncompliance with sludge use or disposal criteria, guidelines or regulations developed under
section 405 of the Act; any criteria, guidelines or regulations affecting sludge use or disposal
developed pursuant to the Solid Waste Disposal Act, the Clean Air Act, the Toxic Substances
Control Act or State criteria applicable to the sludge management method being used;
(8) Any substance which will cause the POTW to violate either its TPDES or state disposal system
permit, or both, or the receiving water quality standards;
(9) Any wastewater with objectionable color not removed in the treatment process, such as, but
not limited to, dye wastes and vegetable tanning solutions;
(10) Any wastewater having a temperature which will inhibit biological activity in the POTW
treatment plant resulting in interference, but in no case wastewater with a temperature at the
introduction into the sewer system which exceeds 180 degrees Fahrenheit, or which, singularly or in
combination with other users, will cause the POTW plant influent to exceed 95 degrees Fahrenheit;
(11) Any pollutants, including oxygen-demanding pollutants (BOD, etc.) released at a flow rate or
pollutant concentration which a user knows or has reason to know will cause interference to the
POTW;
(12) Any wastewater containing any radioactive wastes or isotopes of such half-life or
concentration as may exceed limits established by the director in compliance with applicable state or
federal regulations;
(13) Any wastewater which is known to cause a hazard to human life or which constitutes a public
nuisance; or
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 198/283
(14) Any trucked or hauled-in pollutants, except at discharge points designated by the POTW.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-92; Ordinance 1354, sec. 14, adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-94. Specific pollutant limitations and wastewater characteristics.
No user shall discharge the following pollutants in amounts greater than allowed by an industrial waste permit.
Pollutants not specifically regulated by permit shall be considered background pollutants. Permit limits shall be
set and allocated according to the pretreatment program. Limits for the following parameters and any other
parameters, the city may want to regulate shall be placed in the permit.
Arsenic
Cadmium
Chromium
Copper
Cyanide
Lead
Mercury
Molybdenum
Nickel
Selenium
Silver
Zinc
Phenols
Specific permitted limits are established as following:
(1) BOD 300 mg/l
(2) TSS 300 mg/l
(3) TOC 200 mg/l
(4) FOG 100 mg/l
(5) TPH 20 mg/l
Notice: If an industrial user exceeds the 300 mg/l limits for BOD and/or 300 mg/l limit TSS 66 percent of the
time over a six-month period, the industrial user will receive a $500.00 fine per day, per violation, until the
condition has been brought under control, as determined by the chief operator of the POTW. If an industrial
user exceeds 600 mg/l for BOD and/or TSS the industrial user will be fined up to $500.00 per day, per violation,
until the condition has been brought under control, as determined by the chief operator of the POTW.
The permit limits apply at the point where the wastewater is discharged to the POTW. All concentrations for
metallic substances are for total metal, unless indicated otherwise. The director may impose mass limitations in
addition to, or in place of, the concentration based on limitations listed in this section.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-93; Ordinance 1354, sec. 15, adopted 10/24/00; Ordinance 1638, sec. 1, adopted 6/24/14)
Sec. 54-95. Federal categorical pretreatment standards.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 199/283
Upon the promulgation of the federal categorical pretreatment standards for a particular industrial subcategory,
the federal standard, if more stringent than limitations imposed upon this article for sources in that subcategory,
shall immediately supersede the limitations imposed under this article. The director shall notify all affected
users of the applicable reporting requirements under 40 CFR 403.12. (1969 Code, sec. 26-94; Ordinance 1354,
sec. 16, adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-96. State requirements.
State requirements and limitations on discharges shall apply in any case where they are more stringent than
federal requirements and limitations or those in this article. (1969 Code, sec. 26-95; Ordinance 1354, sec. 17,
adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-97. Excessive discharge.
No user shall increase the use of water or in any way attempt to dilute a discharge as a partial or complete
substitute for adequate treatment to achieve compliance with the limitations contained in the federal categorical
pretreatment standards, or in any other pollutant-specific limitation developed by the city or state, except as
specified in section 54-101(c)(2). (1969 Code, sec. 26-96; Ordinance 1354, sec. 18, adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-98. Accidental discharges.
(a) Policy. Each significant industrial user shall provide protection from accidental discharge of prohibited
materials or other substances regulated by this article. Facilities to prevent accidental discharge of prohibited
materials shall be provided and maintained at the owner's or user's own cost and expense. Detailed plans
showing facilities and operating procedures to provide this protection shall be submitted to the city for review,
and shall be approved by the city before construction of the facility. All existing significant industrial users shall
complete such a plan and implementation schedule by December 1, 2000. Such plan and implementation
schedule shall specify a definite completion date for the construction of facilities to prevent accidental discharge
of prohibited materials. No user who commences contribution to the POTW after the effective date of the
ordinance from which this article is derived shall be permitted to introduce pollutants into the sewer system until
the city has approved accidental discharge procedures. Review and approval of such plans and operating
procedures shall not relieve the industrial user from the responsibility to modify such user's facility as necessary
to meet the requirements of this article. Such plans shall be reviewed every two years and modified as
necessary to meet changing conditions. In the case of an accidental discharge, the user shall immediately
notify by telephone the POTW of the incident. The notification shall include location of discharge, type of
discharge, its concentration and volume, and type of corrective actions taken by the user.
(b) Written notice to city. Within five days following an accidental discharge, the user shall submit to the
director a detailed written report describing the cause of the discharge and the measures to be taken by the
user to prevent similar future occurrences, such notification shall not relieve the user of any expense, loss,
damage or other liability which may be incurred as a result of damage to the POTW, fish kills or any other
damage to person or property; nor shall such notification relieve the user of any fines, civil penalties or other
liability which may be imposed by this article or other applicable law.
(c) Emergency notification procedure. An emergency notification procedure shall be made available to
employees on whom to call in the event of an accidental discharge. Employers shall ensure that all employees
who may cause or suffer such an accidental discharge to occur are advised of the emergency notification
procedure.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-97; Ordinance 1354, sec. 19, adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-99. Excessive strength surcharge.
Wastewater containing BOD or TSS in excess of that provided for in a prohibited discharge standard or normal
strength wastewater may be discharged into the sanitary sewer provided:
(1) The waste will not cause damage to the collection system;
(2) The waste will not impair the treatment process;
(3) The person discharging such wastewater pays a monthly surcharge to the city utilities division
in addition to the usual monthly sewer service charges. Computation of such surcharge shall be
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 200/283
based on the following formulas:
DBOD in pounds = (ABOD mg/L × V million gal × 8.34)/D days in month
DBOD = (ABOD × V × 8.34)/D
S1 surcharge is for all BOD over 300 mg/L for the month
S1 = a × 8.34 × V × (ABOD - 300)
If ABOD is less than or equal to 300 mg/L, S1 = 0
If DBOD is greater than 1,560 lbs calculate S2
S2 = (b - a) × (DBOD - 1,560) × D
If DBOD is less than or equal to 1,560, S2 = 0
If DBOD is greater than 1,944 lbs calculate S3
S3 = (c - b) × (DBOD - 1,944) × D
If DBOD is less than or equal to 1,944 lbs, S3 = 0
S4 is surcharge for TSS over 300 mg/L
S4 = d × (TSS - 300) × 8.34 × V
If TSS is less than or equal to 300 mg/L, S4 = 0
S5 is surcharge for FOG over 100 mg/L
S5 = e × (FOG - 100) × 8.34 × V
If FOG is less than or equal to 100 mg/L, S5 = 0
Total surcharge = S1 + S2 + S3 + S4 + S5
Where:
S = Surcharge for extra strength wastewater per day.
V = Monthly wastewater flow in million gallons.
D = Days of the month.
a = Unit cost for removing one pound of BOD for DBOD amounts up to 1,560 (section 54-
62(g)).
b = Unit cost for removing one pound of BOD for DBOD amounts between 1,560 and 1,944
(section 54-62(g)).
c = Unit cost for removing one pound of BOD when daily BOD is 1,944 or more (section 54-
62(g)).
d = Unit cost for removing one pound of TSS (section 54-62(g)).
e = Unit cost for removing one pound of FOG (section 54-62(g)).
BOD = Actual BOD measured at point of discharge mg/l.
TSS = Actual average TSS measured at point of discharge mg/l.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 201/283
FOG = Actual average FOG measured at point of discharge mg/l.
DBOD = Daily average BOD (in pounds).
ABOD = Actual average BOD in mg/l.
300 = Normal BOD in mg/l.
300 = Normal TSS in mg/l.
100 = Normal FOG.
8.34 = Conversion factor (to convert mg/l to lbs/1,000,000 gal.)
Unit cost for removing BOD, FOG and TSS shall be set in article III of this chapter.
Methods and frequency of testing shall be established by permit.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-98; Ordinance 1354, sec. 20, adopted 10/24/00; Ordinance 1555, sec. 2, adopted 2/22/11;
Ordinance 1638, sec. 1, adopted 6/24/14; Ordinance 1658 adopted 3/24/15)
Sec. 54-100. User permit.
(a) Required. All potential significant and categorical industrial users must apply for and obtain an industrial
waste permit prior to discharging, unless such user is an existing user. Existing users, reclassified as significant
or categorical, must apply for and obtain an industrial waste permit or waiver within 90 days of notice of
reclassification.
(b) Policy. Where the user is a significant user, or a categorical user, a written statement on a standard form
provided by the chief operator, setting forth the nature of operation contemplated or presently carried on, shall
be filed with the director of utilities. The statement shall contain the amount of water which will be used and its
source, the proposed point of discharge of such wastes into the public sewers, the estimated amount to be so
discharged, and a fair statement setting forth the known or expected physical, chemical and other
characteristics of the wastes. The director shall approve such applications and grant an industrial waste permit
only when the evidence submitted by the applicant demonstrates that the wastes or wastewater to be deposited
by the applicant in the sanitary sewer will comply with all the regulations of this chapter. Any violations of the
conditions of this industrial waste permit shall make the permittee subject to the penalties provided in section
54-90.
(c) Permit modifications. Within nine months of the promulgation of a national categorical pretreatment
standard, the industrial waste permit of users subject to such standard shall be revised to require compliance
with such standard within the time prescribed by such standard. Where a user which is subject to a national
categorical pretreatment standard has not previously submitted an application for an industrial waste permit as
required, the user shall apply for an industrial waste permit within 180 days after the promulgation of the
applicable pretreatment standard.
(d) Permit fee. Permit fee is $3,300.00. The fee is payable upon issuance of the permit and is for the duration
of the permit.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-99; Ordinance 1354, sec. 21, adopted 10/24/00; Ordinance 1638, sec. 1, adopted 6/24/14)
Sec. 54-101. Reporting requirements for permittee.
(a) Baseline monitoring report required. All new or reclassified categorical users must submit a baseline
monitoring report, which meets or exceeds the requirements of 40 CFR 403.12(b).
(b) Compliance date report. Within 90 days following the date of final compliance with applicable
pretreatment standards or, in the case of a new source, following commencement of the introduction of
wastewater into the POTW, any user subject to pretreatment standards and requirements shall submit to the
director a report indicating the nature and concentration of all pollutants in the discharge from the regulated
process which are limited by pretreatment standards and requirements and the average and maximum daily
flow for these process units in the user facility which are limited by such pretreatment standards or
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 202/283
requirements. The report shall state whether the applicable pretreatment standards or requirements are being
met on a consistent basis and, if not, what additional pretreatment is necessary to bring the user into
compliance with the applicable pretreatment standards or requirements. This statement shall be signed by an
authorized representative of the industrial user, and certified by a professional person qualified by training to
render such certification.
(c) Periodic compliance reports.
(1) All categorical or significant users shall submit to the chief operator during the months of June
and December, unless required more frequently in the pretreatment standard or by the director, a
report indicating the nature and concentration of pollutants in the effluent which are limited by the
industrial waste permit. At the discretion of the director and in consideration of such factors as local
high or low flow rates, holidays, budget cycles, etc., the director may agree to alter the months
during which the above reports are to be submitted.
(2) The director may impose mass limitations on users which are using dilution to meet applicable
standards or requirements, or in other cases where the imposition of mass limitations are
appropriate. In such cases, the report required by subsection (c)(1) of this section shall include the
mass of pollutants regulated in the effluent of the user. These reports shall contain the results of
sampling and analysis of the discharge, including the flow and the nature and concentration, or
production and mass where requested by the director, of pollutants contained therein which are
limited by the applicable standards. The frequency of monitoring shall be prescribed in the
applicable standard. All analyses shall be performed in accordance with procedures established by
the EPA pursuant to section 304(g) of the Act and contained in 40 CFR part 136 and amendments
thereto or with any other test procedures approved by the EPA. Sampling shall be performed in
accordance with the techniques approved by the EPA. The director may waive the semi-annual
reporting requirement in subsection (c)(1) of this section when the chief operator collects all the
information required in the semiannual report.
(3) The user shall report any significant changes in operations, or wastewater constituents and
characteristics.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-99.1; Ordinance 1354, sec. 22, adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-102. Monitoring facilities.
(a) Every user shall provide and operate at the user's own expense, monitoring facilities to allow inspection,
sampling, and flow measurement of the building sewer and/or internal drainage systems. The monitoring facility
shall normally be situated on the user's premises, but the city may, when such a location would be impractical
or cause undue hardship on the user, allow the facility to be constructed in a public street or sidewalk area and
located so that it will not be obstructed by landscaping or parked vehicles.
(b) There shall be ample room in or near such sampling manhole or facility to allow accurate sampling for
analysis. The facility and flow measuring equipment shall be maintained at all times in a safe and proper
operating condition at the expense of the user.
(c) Whether constructed on public or private property, the sampling and monitoring facilities shall be provided
in accordance with the city's requirements and all applicable local construction standards and specifications.
Construction shall be completed within 120 days following written notification by the city to begin construction.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-99.2; Ordinance 1354, sec. 23, adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-103. Inspection and sampling.
(a) Policy. The city may inspect the facilities of any user to ascertain whether the purpose of this article is
being met and all requirements are being complied with. Occupants of premises where wastewater is created
or discharged shall allow the city or its representative ready access at all reasonable times to all parts of the
premises for the purposes of inspection, sampling and records examination or in the performance of their
duties. The city, the state natural resource conservation commission and the EPA shall have the right to set up
on the user's property such devices as are necessary to conduct sampling inspection, compliance monitoring or
metering operations or all of these operations. Where a user has security measures in force which would
require proper identification and clearance before entry into their premises, the user shall make necessary
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 203/283
arrangements with its security so that upon presentation of suitable identification, personnel from the city, the
state natural resource conservation commission and the EPA will be permitted to enter the user's premises,
without delay, for the purposes of performing their specific responsibilities.
(b) Determining character, volume, and concentration of waste.
(1) The industrial waste discharged or deposited into the sanitary sewers shall be subject to
periodic inspection and sampling as often as may be deemed necessary by the director. Samples
shall be collected in such a manner as to be representative of the character and concentration of the
wastewater under operational conditions. The determination of the character and concentration of
industrial waste shall be made by the director at such times and on such schedules as may be
established by the director. Should a user discharging industrial waste into the sanitary sewers
desire that a determination of the quality of such industrial waste be made at some time other than
that scheduled by the director, such special determination may be made by the director at the
expense of the user discharging such industrial waste.
(2) Grease, oil and sand interceptors shall be provided for the proper handling of liquid wastes
containing greases in excessive amounts, or any flammable wastes, sand and other prohibited
ingredients; except that such interceptors shall not be required for private living quarters or dwelling
units. All interceptors shall be of a type and capacity approved by the chief operator and shall be
located so as to be readily and easily accessible for cleaning and inspection. Grease and oil
interceptors shall be constructed of impervious materials capable of withstanding abrupt and
extreme changes in temperature. They shall be of substantial construction, watertight and equipped
with easily removable covers which when bolted in place shall be gastight and watertight. Sizing of
such grease and oil interceptors shall be in accordance with the provisions of the city's plumbing
code. Where installed, all grease, oil, and sand interceptors shall be maintained by the user at his
expense in proper operating condition at all times.
(c) Measurement of flow.
(1) The volume of flow used in computing abnormal sewage surcharges shall be based upon
metered water consumption as shown in the records of meter readings maintained by the water
department. If a user discharging waste into the city's sanitary sewer system produces evidence to
the director demonstrating that a substantial portion of the total amount of metered water does not
reach the city's sewer system, an estimated percentage of total water consumption to be used in
computing charges may be established by the director.
(2) Any user who procures any part or all of his water supply from sources other than the city
water department, all or part of which is discharged into the sanitary sewer, shall install and maintain
at his expense water meters of the type approved by the director for the purpose of determining the
proper volume of flow to be used in computing sewer service charges. Such meters shall be read
monthly and tested for accuracy when deemed necessary by the director. Where it can be shown to
the satisfaction of the director that a substantial portion of the water as measured by the aforesaid
meter does not enter the sanitary sewer system of the city, then the director may require or permit
the installation of additional meters at the user's expense in such manner as to measure the quantity
of water actually entering the sanitary sewer system from the lot, parcel of land, building or premises
of such user, and the quantity of water used to determine the sewer service charge may be the
quantity of water actually entering the sewer system as so determined, if the director so elects.
If the director finds that it is not practicable to measure the quantity or quality of waste by the aforesaid meters
or monitoring devices, he shall determine the quantity or quality, or both, of the waste in any manner or method
he may find practicable in order to arrive at the percentage of water entering the sanitary sewer system of the
city and the quality of the sewage to be used to determine the sewer service charge.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-99.3; Ordinance 1354, sec. 24, adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-104. Pretreatment.
Users shall provide necessary wastewater treatment as required to comply with this article and shall achieve
compliance with all industrial waste permit limits within the time limitations as specified by the industrial waste
permit. Any facilities required to pretreat wastewater to a level acceptable to the city shall be provided, operated
and maintained at the user's expense. Detailed plans showing the pretreatment facilities and operating
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 204/283
procedures shall be submitted to the city for review, and shall be acceptable to the city before construction of
the facility. The review of such plans and operating procedures will in no way relieve the user from the
responsibility of modifying the facility as necessary to produce an effluent acceptable to the city under the
provisions of the article. Any subsequent changes in the pretreatment facilities or method of operation shall be
reported to and be acceptable to the city prior to the user's initiation of the changes. (1969 Code, sec. 26-99.4;
Ordinance 1354, sec. 25, adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-105. Confidential information; trade secrets.
(a) Information and data on a user obtained from reports, questionnaires, permit applications, permits and
monitoring programs and from inspections shall be available to the public or other governmental agency without
restriction, unless the user specifically requests and is able to demonstrate to the satisfaction of the city that the
release of such information would divulge information, processes or methods or production entitled to protection
as trade secrets of the user.
(b) When requested by the person furnishing a report, the portions of a report which might disclose trade
secrets or secret processes shall not be made available for inspection by the public, unless ordered to be
disclosed by the attorney general of the state but shall be made available upon written request to governmental
agencies for uses related to this article, the Texas Pollutant Discharge Elimination System (TPDES) permit,
state disposal system permit or the pretreatment programs; provided, however, that such portions of a report
shall be available for use by the state or any state agency in judicial review or enforcement proceedings
involving the person furnishing the report. Wastewater constituents and characteristics will not be recognized as
confidential information.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-99.5; Ordinance 1354, sec. 26, adopted 10/24/00)
Sec. 54-106. Enforcement procedures; revocation of permit.
Enforcement procedures for violations of this article shall be as stated in the approved pretreatment program,
including but not limited to the following:
(1) Immediate danger. When in the opinion of the director of utilities a continuing or proposed
discharge presents an immediate danger to the health or welfare of citizens or the environment, or
an immediate danger to the wastewater collection and treatment system or any of its components,
he shall immediately terminate the discharging person's sewer and water service. The discharging
person shall be notified as soon as possible of the termination of service and of the reason for the
termination. After notice, the discharging person may appeal the decision of the director of utilities to
the city manager who may uphold, amend or overrule the director of utilities' decision. Any person
dissatisfied with the city manager's decision may appeal to the city commission by filing a written
notice of appeal within five days of the city manager's decision with the city secretary. The city
commission may uphold, amend or overrule the city manager's decision after a hearing into that
decision has been held. In any hearing before the city commission under this section the substantial
evidence rule shall govern its determination of the matter.
(2) Substantial danger.
(A) The city may suspend the wastewater treatment service or an industrial waste permit or
both when such suspension is necessary, in the opinion of the director of utilities, in order to
stop an actual or threatened discharge which endangers or might endanger the health or
welfare of persons or the environment, or causes, or could cause, interference with the POTW,
or causes, or could cause, the city to violate any condition of its state or TPDES permits.
(B) Any person notified of a suspension of the wastewater treatment service, or the industrial
waste permit, or both shall immediately stop or eliminate the contribution. In the event of a
failure of the person to comply voluntarily with the suspension order, the city shall take such
steps as it deems necessary, including immediate severance of the sewer connection and
termination of the violator's water service, to prevent or minimize damage to the POTW
system, danger to any individuals, or violation of the city's state or TPDES permits. The city
shall, if possible, conduct an administrative hearing prior to the severance of a user's sewer
service. Such administrative hearing shall be conducted in the same manner as is prescribed
for a show cause hearing in the case of revocation of a permit; provided, however, three days'
notice shall be deemed sufficient notice to the violator of the administrative hearing if such
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 205/283
notice is personally served by the city. The city shall reinstate the industrial waste permit or the
wastewater treatment service or both upon proof of the permanent elimination of the
noncomplying discharge. A detailed written statement submitted by the user describing the
causes of the harmful contribution and the measures taken to prevent any future occurrence
shall be submitted to the city within 15 days of the date of occurrence.
(3) Revocation of permit.
(A) Policy. Any user who violates the conditions of this article, or applicable state and federal
regulations, is subject to having his permit revoked in accordance with the procedures of this
section. The following are specific, but not inclusive, violations:
(i) Failure of a user to factually report the wastewater constituents and characteristics
of his discharge;
(ii) Failure of the user to report significant changes in operations, or wastewater
constituents and characteristics;
(iii) Refusal of reasonable access to the user's premises for the purpose of inspection
or monitoring; or
(iv) Violation of conditions of the permit.
(B) Notification of violation. Whenever the city finds that any user has violated or is violating
this article, his industrial waste permit, or any prohibition, limitation of requirements contained
herein, the city shall serve upon such person a written notice stating the nature of the violation
and providing a reasonable time for satisfactory correction thereof.
(C) Show cause hearing.
(i) The city shall order any user who causes or allows an unauthorized discharge to
enter the POTW to show cause before the director of utilities, why the proposed
enforcement action should not be taken. A notice shall be served on the user specifying
the time and place of a hearing to be held by the director of utilities, regarding the
violation, the reasons why the action is to be taken, the proposed enforcement action,
and directing the user to show cause before the director of utilities, why the proposed
enforcement action should not be taken. The notice of the hearing shall be served
personally or by registered or certified mail, return receipt requested, at least ten days
before the hearing. Service may be made on any agent or officer of a corporate user.
(ii) The public works director may conduct the hearing and take the evidence, or may
designate any officer or employee of the city to:
a. Issue in the name of the director of utilities, notices of hearing requesting the
attendance and testimony of witnesses and the production of evidence relevant to
any matter involved in such hearings;
b. Take the evidence;
c. Transmit a report of the evidence and hearing, including transcripts and other
evidence together with recommendations to the director of utilities, for action
thereon.
(iii) After the director of utilities, has reviewed the evidence, he may issue an order to
the user responsible for the discharge directing that, following a specified time period, the
sewer service shall be discontinued, unless adequate treatment facilities, devices or
other related appurtenances shall have been installed on existing treatment facilities.
Further orders and directives as are necessary and appropriate may be issued.
(iv) Failure of a user to attend a show cause hearing or failure of a user to present
evidence required by the person conducting the hearing shall be cause for immediate
termination of sewer service.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 206/283
(4) Civil legal action. If any person discharges wastewater, industrial wastes or other wastes into
the city's wastewater disposal system contrary to the provisions of this article, or federal or state
pretreatment requirements, or any order of the city, the city attorney may commence an action for
appropriate relief in the proper court of the county. In addition to the penalties provided in section 54-
90, the city may recover actual costs, including, but not limited to, repairs, fines and penalties,
reasonable attorney's fees, court costs and other expenses of litigation against the person found to
have violated this article or the orders, rules, regulations and permits issued hereunder.
(5) Other remedies. The director of utilities may employ any other remedies authorized for
enforcement by federal regulations.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-99.6; Ordinance 1354, sec. 27, adopted 10/24/00; Ordinance 1638, sec. 1, adopted
6/24/14)
Secs. 54-107—54-126. Reserved.
ARTICLE V. WATER
DIVISION 1. GENERALLY
Sec. 54-127. Utilities director-Appointment; general duties.
There shall be appointed by the city manager a utilities director, who shall be the administrative officer of the
waterworks system, including all pump and motor houses, pumps and motors, reservoirs, standpipes, ground
and elevated storage tanks, pipelines, hydrants, water meters, valves, automation equipment to operate the
water system, wells, testing equipment, and all other equipment or property used in connection in the operation
of the water system. He shall have general supervision of all employees in the water department, responsibility
to ensure adequate water pressure, and responsibility to plan all work schedules for maintenance and repairs
deemed necessary and consistent with his job description. He shall serve and be compensated in accordance
to the city charter. He shall be subject to all city ordinances, rules and regulations. (1969 Code, sec. 26-100;
Ordinance 646, sec. 1, adopted 9/24/59; Ordinance 1322, sec. 1, adopted 6/23/98)
Sec. 54-128. Same-Reporting offenders.
The utilities director shall cause complaints to be filed on violators of this article with the proper court of
jurisdiction. (1969 Code, sec. 26-101; Ordinance 646, sec. 1, adopted 9/24/59; Ordinance 1322, sec. 2,
adopted 6/23/98)
Sec. 54-129. Same-Attending to control of water supply.
The utilities director shall attend to and control the water supply and at all times see to the sufficiency thereof,
and shall notify the community and customers, unless an emergency requires otherwise, of the necessity of
shutting off any pipeline for the purpose of making repairs, extensions, connections, or any other purpose.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-102; Ordinance 646, sec. 1, adopted 9/24/59; Ordinance 1322, sec. 3, adopted 6/23/98)
Sec. 54-130. Right of entry.
The superintendent and any other authorized city officer shall have access at all reasonable hours to all parts of
the premises to which water is supplied for the purpose of examination. (1969 Code, sec. 26-104; Code 1969,
sec. 26-104; Ordinance 248, sec. 16, adopted 11/9/1909)
Sec. 54-131. Department separate; special fund.
The waterworks department shall be a separate and independent department of the city, and all revenues
arising from this source shall constitute a special fund to be used first for the payment of all expenses of said
waterworks. There shall be kept a separate account of said funds received and disbursed, and the warrants
drawn against this fund shall so state on the face that they are drawn against this fund and for what purpose.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-105; Ordinance 248, sec. 1, adopted 11/9/1909)
Sec. 54-132. Liability of city for breaks or discontinuance or diminution of water.
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 207/283
The city shall not be liable for any damage by reason of the breaking of any pipe or service cock, or the
discontinuance of service for repair or other necessity or for diminution of water supply. (1969 Code, sec. 26-
106; Ordinance 248, sec. 15, adopted 11/9/1909)
Sec. 54-133. Reports of leaks and violations.
It shall be the duty of all employees of the city, including officers and members of the police force, to report to
the superintendent of the waterworks system, any leaks or unnecessary waste of water that may come to their
attention, and also any violations of this article. (1969 Code, sec. 26-107; Ordinance 646, sec. 4, adopted
9/24/59)
Sec. 54-134. Service rate for inadvertent, accidental, and unknown loss of water.
If a water user's monthly bill exceeds $50.00; and the water usage for that bill shows a usage of water three
times in excess of the average monthly water usage on an annualized basis; and a licensed plumber verifies
that the loss of water could not be detected from the exterior of a premises, but in fact the loss was hidden and
concealed and not easily discoverable by the water user, or the loss of water could not reasonably be foreseen
during the customer's absence, then the water rate for the month shall be adjusted to be as follows:
(1) An amount equal to the average water bill paid by the user on an annualized basis in the event
there is no prior history of use for a particular customer seeking benefit from this section, the water
and sewer superintendent shall be responsible for determining an equitable average water bill; and
(2) An amount equal to the cost to the city of water used in excess of the average annualized use.
The cost to the city has been determined to be $0.555 per 1,000 gallons as of January 1, 1984. The
cost to the city shall be calculated not less than annually by the water and sewer superintendent,
and the cost used pursuant to this section shall be the most recent calculated cost.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-107.1; Ordinance 1046 adopted 1/18/84)
Sec. 54-135. Illegal acts in connection with the waterworks system.
It shall be unlawful for any person to do, commit, or assist in committing any of the following things or acts in
the city, or in connection with any part of the waterworks system located outside the city:
(1) Open or close any fireplug, fire hydrant or stopcock connected with the city waterworks
system, or lift or remove the covers of any gate valves or shutoffs thereof, without the permission of
the superintendent of the waterworks, except in case of fire, and then only under the direction of
officers of the fire department;
(2) Interfere with, destroy, deface, impair, injure, or wantonly force open any valve gate, or door, or
in any way whatsoever destroy, injure or deface any part of any engine-house, reservoir, standpipe,
elevated tank, building or appurtenances, fence, tree, shrub, or fixture or property pertaining to the
waterworks system;
(3) Go upon or ascend the stairway or steps, on any elevated water storage tank or standpipe of
the waterworks system, except by permission of the waterworks superintendent;
(4) Place any telegraph, telephone, or electric light pole, or any obstruction whatsoever within
three feet of any fire hydrant;
(5) Resort to any fraudulent device or arrangement for the purpose of procuring water for himself
or others from private connections on privately owned premises contrary to the city regulations or
ordinances;
(6) Interfere with or injure any reservoir, tank, fountain, hydrant, pipecock, valve, or other
apparatus pertaining to the waterworks system, or to turn on or off without authority the water in any
street hydrant, fireplug, fire hydrant, or other water fixture, or to hitch or tie any animal thereto;
(7) Make or permit to be made any connections with a fireplug, or with main or service pipes of
the waterworks system or to turn on or use the water of said system without first obtaining a permit
therefor;
7/15/2019 https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0
https://z2.franklinlegal.net/franklin/PrintViewer.jsp?printCollection=0 208/283
(8) Cover over or conceal from view any water valve box, or service or meter box;
(9) Remove any water meter that has been placed by the city, or to in any manner change,
interfere with or tamper with any water meter; the provisions of this section shall not apply to the
employees of the city when acting in their official capacity; or
(10) Turn on the water supply to any building or to any supply pipe where the supply has been
turned off for the nonpayment of the monthly water charge or for the violation of any rule or
ordinance governing the waterworks system.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-108; Ordinance 646, sec. 2, adopted 9/24/59)
Sec. 54-136. Public water supply wells.
(a) Location. Public water supply wells shall be located so that there will be no danger of pollution from
flooding or from unsanitary surroundings, such as privies, sewage treatment plants, livestock and animal pens,
solid waste disposal sites or underground petroleum and chemical storage tanks and liquid transmission
pipelines, or abandoned and improperly sealed wells.
(b) Prohibited activities within the corporate limit of the city.
(1) Prohibited activities that are within 50 feet of a public water supply wells is a tile or concrete
sanitary sewer, sewerage appurtenance, septic tank, storm sewer, or cemetery; or prohibited
activities that are within 150 feet of a septic tank perforated drainfield, areas irrigated by low dosage,
low angle spray on-site sewage facilities, absorption bed, evapotranspiration bed, improperly
constructed water well, underground petroleum and chemical storage tank or liquid transmission
pipeline. However, sanitary or storm sewers constructed of ductile iron or PVC pipe meeting AWWA
standards, having a minimum working pressure of 150 psi or greater, and equipped with pressuretype
joints may be located at a distance of less than 50 feet from a proposed well site but in no case
shall the distance be less than ten feet. For the purposes of this section, improperly constructed
water wells are those, which do not meet the surface and subsurface construction standards for a
public water supply well.
(2) Prohibited activities located within 500 feet of a public water supply wells include a sewage
treatment plant or within 300 feet of the public water supply well a sewage wet well, sewage
pumping station or a drainage ditch which contains industrial waste discharges or the wastes from
sewage treatment systems.
(3) Prohibited activities from within 500 feet of a public water supply well are animal feed lots,
solid waste disposal sites, lands on which sewage plant or septic tank sludge is applied, or lands
irrigated by sewage plant effluent.
(4) Livestock shall not be permitted within 50 feet of any public water supply well.
(c) Permitted activities.
(1) Nothing in this section shall prohibit the construction of homes or buildings upon properties
within the areas described in subsections (a) and (b) of this section; provided that all restrictions
described in subsections (a) and (b) of this section are recognized and followed.
(2) Nothing in this section shall be construed to prohibit normal farming and ranching operations
allowed elsewhere by this Code.
(1969 Code, sec. 26-111; Ordinance 1366, sec. 1, adopted 3/27/01; Ordinance 1385, sec. 1, adopted 2/26/02)
Sec. 54-137. Water conservation and drought contingency plans.
The city commission hereby approves and adopts the water conservation and drought contingency plans which
are kept on file in the office of the city secretary. (1969 Code, sec. 26-110; Ordinance 1516, sec. 2, adopted
6/23/09; Ordinance 1632, sec. 1, adopted 4/22/14)
Secs. 54-138—54-147. Reserved.

DIVISION 2. SERVICE
Sec. 54-148. Connections-Application; performing; furnishing apparatus.
It shall be unlawful for any person to make any connection to the mains or pipes of the waterworks system
without first making application to the city, stating fully the several and various uses for which water is wanted,
giving the name of the owner of the property, the number of the lot and block, the name of the street and house
number. Upon the payment of the tapping fee, the superintendent shall make, or have made, the necessary
connections and furnish a curb stop box and curb cock, the cost of which is included in the tapping fee, and
every premises connected with any water main, or being supplied with any water from the city waterworks, shall
have a separate service connection, curbstop box and curb cock. All fees and charges shall be paid for at
amounts and rates fixed by ordinance or resolution of the city commission. (1969 Code, sec. 26-120; Ordinance
646, sec. 3, adopted 9/24/59)
Sec. 54-149. Same-Misrepresentations or waste of water; stopping service.
In case of any willful misrepresentation on the part of any applicant, or any unreasonable water or diversion of
the water, the water supply will be stopped. (1969 Code, sec. 26-121; Ordinance 248, sec. 4, adopted
11/9/1909)
Sec. 54-150. Same-Issuance of permit.
When the application mentioned in section 54-148, together with the fee charged by the city for tapping the
mains, has been deposited with the city secretary, he shall issue a permit directed to the superintendent
showing the connection to be made and that the fee has been paid. (1969 Code, sec. 26-122; Ordinance 248,
sec. 3A, adopted 11/9/1909)

boundary of the city and are to be charged and collected by the city as follows:

1 ½-inch tap $1,007.00
2-inch tap, and larger Actual cost

and alleyways, based on the extension of a water service line to the customer's side of the meter.
(b) Except as provided in subsection (c) of this section, tap enlargements which require a new tap will be
charged the tap fee for the size tap as set out in subsection (a) of this section, plus an additional fee of $75.00
for abandoning the existing tap.
(c) Fees for meter enlargements from three-fourths inch to one inch shall be $225.00.
(d) For taps made under a paved surface shall be charged a fee as by the city permit to cut the asphalt or
concrete. See section 48-2(b).
(e) Fees for plugging abandoned water service taps shall be $200.00.

Along with the application for water, sewer, or sanitation service a deposit must be collected as follows:
(1) Before any customer may have water, sewer, or sanitation service from the city as provided by
this Code, a minimum deposit of $100.00 shall be made for residential service, unless the customer
can demonstrate good utility credit, then the deposit is waived; and for a multi-family dwelling,
commercial, and industrial service a sum equal to three times the average monthly billing shall be
deposited, unless the customer can demonstrate good utility credit, then the deposit is waived. Good
utility credit is demonstrated by presentation of a letter or other documentation from a municipal,
gas, or electric utility indicating that the customer has had utility service for the preceding 12 months
and has not missed a payment due date during that period. If there is a disagreement as to whether
the customer has demonstrated good utility credit, the decision of the finance director shall control.
In the event that a customer's service is discontinued by the city for failure to pay for any service, the
customer shall be required to pay a deposit equivalent to 3/12 of the estimated annual billing prior to
restoration of service. The deposit shall be refunded to the depositor when he discontinues the use
of all services. All bills and accounts due the city for water, sewer, or sanitation services must be
paid.
(2) A deposit is required as a guarantee for the payment of water, sewer, and sanitation service
accounts or damages to service connections or meters caused through the neglect, abuses, or
failure of the customer or his agents to use proper care. The deposit or any part thereof may be
applied by the city to the payment of any such accounts when they become past due.
(3) Should a deposit or any part thereof be applied in payment of past due accounts, service may
not be reestablished until the deposit is restored in the appropriate current amount.
(4) During normal working business hours no fee for instituting service shall be charged. However,
if service is requested after normal working business hours or on weekends or on prescribed
holidays of the city, then a connect fee of $50.00 shall be collected.

Sec. 54-154. Late fee; due and delinquency dates; shut off for nonpayment; disconnect fee; courtesy
billing; failure to receive bill and disputed billing.
(a) The monthly water, sewer and sanitation service charges authorized in this Code include consideration of
a ten-percent late fee charge for late payment. To not be charged the late payment fee, the bill will have to pay
in full within 15 days after the billing date.
(b) All charges for water, sewer and sanitation services furnished or rendered by the city shall be due and
payable 15 days after the billing date. If the bill is not paid in full within 55 days after the billing date, then the
customer may be subject to being disconnected for nonpayment of fees as prescribed by this Code and as
determined by the finance director.
(c) Any customer, who is over 55 days in arrears and have experienced an extensive water leak, or sickness
within the immediate household or other extenuating circumstances as in the opinion of the finance director,
may be offered a payout agreement. If the customer misses any payments during the terms of the payout
agreement, then the agreement shall be null and void. In the event a customer's payout agreement is rendered
null and void, the customer shall be required to pay a deposit equivalent to 3/12 of the estimated annual billing.
(d) If disconnected, no connection shall thereafter be made with the city system until such party shall have
paid all amounts due and all costs of disconnecting and reconnecting with such system.
(e) A reconnect fee of $25.00 for non-payment of the balance due of the customer's bill after 55 days of the
billing date, shall be collected during normal working business hours and week days. If service is restored after
normal working business hours or on weekends or on prescribed holidays of the city, then a reconnect fee of
$50.00 shall be collected.
(f) A courtesy past due reminder bill with the disconnect date shall be mailed to each customer that have not
paid their current bill at least 15 days after the billing date.

accurate in accordance to industry standards, then the customer shall be charged a testing fee as follows:
3/4-inch tap $20.00
1-inch tap $30.00
11/2-inch tap $50.00
2-inch tap $60.00
Larger than 2-inch tap Actual cost, including labor
